meeting	sequence	date	type	speaker	statement	code2	code
201410	0	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	I’d like to call this meeting to order.	5	5
201410	1	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Before turning to our agenda, I’d like to say a few words about our communications with the public.	97	9
201410	2	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Many of you will recall that in June 2011, the FOMC adopted a policy pertaining to the external communications of FOMC participants, and we have reaffirmed that policy every year thereafter.	97	9
201410	3	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Principle number one is that every single Committee participant, and not just the Chair, has an obligation to enhance the public’s understanding of monetary policy, including its rationale.	97	9
201410	4	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	I would urge you to keep this principle in mind, especially during these highly sensitive times when there is heightened market volatility and tremendous focus on our ongoing discussions about how and when renormalization might proceed.	97	9
201410	5	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	If we aren’t careful about what we say in speeches and other forums, such as media interviews, we can easily confuse markets and the general public, adding to volatility and ultimately diminishing the effectiveness and credibility of our policy.	97	9
201410	6	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, our guidelines affirm that participants are always free to present their own views.	97	9
201410	7	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	I personally feel that communicating the diversity of views on the Committee, as we also do with the SEP, is valuable, but I consider it important to do that in a way that clearly distinguishes one’s individual view from the Committee’s agreed-upon policy stance.	97	9
201410	8	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	We have also traditionally emphasized in our communications the collegial, consensus-driven nature of the FOMC policy process, the fact that participants come to meetings with open minds and, after discussing the issues, come to a collective decision.	97	9
201410	9	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	I see this tradition as a critical aspect of our decision process, and it could be threatened by what strikes me as an increasing tendency for participants to take strong stands in public on ongoing debates about appropriate policy.	97	9
201410	10	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	If we stake out positions in advance of meetings and we have already decided that it doesn’t matter what our colleagues have to say, there is no real reason for us to meet at all.	97	9
201410	11	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	We could save travel expenses by phoning in our votes.	97	9
201410	12	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	But in reality, I suspect that everyone around the table does support the tradition of arriving at the meeting prepared to listen and to reach a collective decision in which most of us don’t get precisely our first choice on policy.	97	9
201410	13	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	If so, I think the clarity of our communications would be enhanced if discussions about individual views were softened a bit, perhaps by adding a reminder that the ultimate decision will be a collective one and that you look forward to discussing the issues further with your colleagues.	97	9
201410	14	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Such qualifiers might also help the public understand that the thinking on the Committee is less fractured than what a range of speeches might suggest.	97	9
201410	15	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Another concern I have is that the flow of comments on the outlook and policy sometimes takes on the appearance of a public debate in which one participant provides an assessment of the policy implications of some bit of economic news, then another provides a contrasting interpretation, followed by yet other participants weighing in with their views on the correct meaning.	97	9
201410	16	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	And it is easy to see how such sequences can arise, especially with reporters trying to spur them on.	97	9
201410	17	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	While we want to be transparent, I don’t think our communications are necessarily clarified by airing a set of conflicting assessments of the policy implications of the latest news.	97	9
201410	18	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Rather, it may just confuse the markets by introducing noise, and for this reason, I would encourage you to avoid publicly drawing firm policy conclusions about the meaning of the latest data before we’ve had a chance to talk about them here.	97	9
201410	19	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	I’d also like to make a few remarks pertaining to our comments on the dollar.	97	9
201410	20	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	By long- standing agreement, the Treasury speaks for the US government on international economic policy and the dollar, while the Federal Reserve speaks for the US government on monetary policy.	97	9
201410	21	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	It is important to respect this division of labor by carefully limiting our remarks about exchange rates.	97	9
201410	22	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	We need to be careful not to ever inadvertently create the impression that we are somehow trying to jawbone down the value of the dollar, especially because that would violate the agreement of the G-7 countries not to seek competitive advantage by targeting the value of their currencies.	97	9
201410	23	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Such comments could prompt counterproductive policy responses abroad.	97	9
201410	24	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, the exchange rate is an important factor for both the economic outlook and monetary policy transmission, so it is hard to avoid all mention of it.	97	9
201410	25	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	But if we follow a few guidelines, I think we can stay out of trouble.	97	9
201410	26	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	First, we should avoid commenting on whether the dollar is appropriately valued.	97	9
201410	27	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Second, we should not discuss current or prospective exchange market interventions by US authorities.	97	9
201410	28	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	And, third, I would urge you to limit references to the economic effects of changes in the dollar to situations in which those effects are important and the public would benefit from some discussion of them.	97	9
201410	29	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Even in these cases, it might be preferable to point to something more encompassing than exchange rates, such as foreign developments.	97	9
201410	30	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Fourth, we want to be clear that the purpose of changes in policies is to achieve the dual mandate, and that any accompanying movements in the dollar, like shifts in bond yields, are a byproduct.	97	9
201410	31	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Finally, if asked to comment on the dollar in a situation in which you had no plan to discuss it, I would recommend saying something like, “I don’t have anything for you on that.	97	9
201410	32	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	As you know, the Treasury speaks for the US government on international economic policy and the dollar.”	97	9
201410	33	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thanks for indulging me in listening to these comments.	97	9
201410	34	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	I’ll stop there, but I do want to end by noting that a guiding principle of our policy on external communications is that we share a responsibility to enhance the public’s understanding of the Committee’s policy actions and the rationale for our decisions, and I’d encourage all of you to bear in mind the broader purpose of our communications.	97	9
201410	35	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Let’s turn to our agenda.	2	2
201410	36	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	The next part of this meeting is going to be a joint meeting of the FOMC and the Board.	2	2
201410	37	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	I need a motion to close the Board meeting.	2	2

201410	41	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Let me call now on Lorie Logan for the Desk report.	2	2
201410	42	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	2	2
201410	43	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	I’ll begin by discussing financial markets and Desk operations over the intermeeting period.	61	6
201410	44	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Simon will briefly review three staff memos that you received prior to the meeting, including proposed changes to the RRP counterparty list, a strategy to address concerns with the federal funds effective rate, and a discussion of segregated balance accounts.	61	6
201410	45	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	After we take Q&A, Fabio will review the staff’s recommendations regarding an additional set of reverse repo tests.	61	6
201410	46	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-left panel of your first exhibit, longer-term sovereign yields in the United States and abroad declined over the intermeeting period, continuing a trend in place since the start of the year.	61	6
201410	47	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Declines in growth-sensitive risk asset prices were also notable as domestic high-yield credit spreads widened and equities fell.	61	6
201410	48	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Market participants primarily attributed these asset price moves to increased concerns over the global growth outlook and to questions regarding the adequacy of future monetary policy accommodation, particularly from the ECB.	61	6
201410	49	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Consistent with this, European equity price indexes underperformed in relation to US equity prices over the period, and the US dollar appreciated modestly, also shown in the top-left panel.	61	6
201410	50	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	As I’ll discuss in more detail in a moment, the unwind of crowded trades predicated on higher US interest rates along with a sharp increase in volatility across markets may have also contributed to the moves, particularly in US interest rates.	61	6
201410	51	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-right panel, the implied federal funds rate path flattened over the period.	61	6
201410	52	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Despite the substantial improvement in the outlook for the labor market over recent months that has led nearly all market participants to expect the conclusion of asset purchases at this meeting, the market-implied funds rate path is now much lower than in December, when the initial reduction in the pace of asset purchases was announced.	61	6
201410	53	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Over this intermeeting period, market rates for 2015 and 2016 reached the furthest below corresponding median SEP values on record.	61	6
201410	54	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	In contrast to the large decline in the market-implied path, the Desk’s October surveys showed that respondents’ target rate expectations were little changed.	61	6
201410	55	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Expectations for the most likely timing of liftoff remained clustered near the second quarter of 2015, and the median expectation for the most likely level of the target rate over the next several years barely moved.	61	6
201410	56	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	In addition, as shown in the middle-left panel, the average probability distribution for the timing of liftoff shifted only slightly to a later liftoff, and the average probability distributions for the level of the funds rate through 2016, not shown, were relatively little changed.	61	6
201410	57	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Consistent with this, there was no appreciable increase in the perceived probability of a return to the zero bound after liftoff.	61	6
201410	58	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	One explanation for the significant change in the market-implied path but only small changes in our survey expectations is that investor beliefs that drive the pricing of interest rate futures diverged from the average beliefs of those we survey.	61	6
201410	59	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	An alternative explanation is that risk premiums in the futures market might have shifted lower, perhaps exacerbated by large changes in positioning over the period.	61	6
201410	60	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	We do have some evidence for large positioning changes.	61	6
201410	61	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	For example, CFTC data show that over 60 percent of the substantial speculative short position in Eurodollar futures that had been building since mid-2013 was unwound over the intermeeting period, much of this occurring around the significant volatility on October 15.	61	6
201410	62	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	That day, against the backdrop of an increase in perceived downside risks to global growth and fears of the spread of Ebola, a weak retail sales print appeared to trigger a surprisingly sharp decline in Treasury yields and a spike in volatility across markets.	61	6
201410	63	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	The unexpectedly large moves reportedly led to a rapid unwind of crowded positions predicated on higher US interest rates and continued low volatility.	61	6
201410	64	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	The resulting position adjustments amplified the moves in various markets and led to large price swings, especially in Treasury securities.	61	6
201410	65	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	The intraday trading range of the 10-year Treasury yield on October 15 was 37 basis points, a six-standard-deviation move over the period since 1998, as shown in the middle-right panel.	61	6
201410	66	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Amidst these large intraday movements, Treasury market cash and derivative volumes were at or near record highs.	61	6
201410	67	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	And as shown in the bottom-left panel, daily trading volume in Eurodollar and 5- and 10-year Treasury futures contracts exceeded the amount of open interest.	61	6
201410	68	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Liquidity also became strained, as evidenced by substantial increases in Treasury bid–asked spreads and declines in measures of market depth.	61	6
201410	69	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	During this time, dealers reported reduced willingness and ability to make markets or warehouse risk for Treasury and other securities.	61	6
201410	70	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Many market participants also reported that algorithmic and high-frequency trading activity may have contributed to the increased volatility and reduced liquidity, though more data and analysis are necessary to understand the exact drivers.	61	6
201410	71	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Overall, the moves on October 15 were highly unusual, given the depth and breadth of US Treasury market liquidity.	61	6
201410	72	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	It is possible that as the structure of fixed- income markets evolve, events like this may result in further punctuated periods of very high market volatility.	61	6
201410	73	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the bottom-right panel, implied volatility across markets had been trending higher before increasing sharply on October 15, especially in fixed-income and equity markets.	61	6
201410	74	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	However, despite the rise, a standardized measure of implied volatility across markets remained well below its longer-run average level.	61	6
201410	75	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Further, much of the sharp rise in implied volatility has since retraced, though measures of interest rate implied volatility remain higher, perhaps reflecting a risk premium demanded by market participants following the events of October 15.	61	6
201410	76	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Market-based measures of longer-dated US inflation compensation also shifted significantly over the intermeeting period.	61	6
201410	77	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-left panel of your next exhibit, the Board staff’s measure of five-year, five-year-forward inflation compensation fell to levels below those at the outset of LSAP 3 or following the “taper tantrum.”	61	6
201410	78	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	In contrast, dealer expectations for five-year CPI inflation five years ahead from the Desk’s survey have been very steady.	61	6
201410	79	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	This suggests that recent declines in market-based measures may not reflect changes in inflation expectations but instead may reflect declining risk premiums.	61	6
201410	80	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	In a special question from the most recent Desk surveys, shown in the top-right panel, respondents attributed about half of the recent decline in the market-based five- year, five-year-forward breakeven rate since early September to lower market expectations for inflation and the other half to declines in risk premiums.	61	6
201410	81	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	A few respondents to this question noted that news of a leadership change at the large bond fund manager Pimco, which is a known large holder of TIPS, may have shifted risk premiums in TIPS and thus narrowed breakeven inflation rates.	61	6
201410	82	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Other market participants generally downplayed Pimco-related effects on inflation markets.	61	6
201410	83	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	They instead attributed the bulk of recent breakeven narrowing to recent low inflation readings, increased downside risks to global growth and inflation, and effects from US dollar strength.	61	6
201410	84	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Concerns regarding lower global inflation were also driven in part by worries over a slowdown in China and by lower commodity prices.	61	6
201410	85	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle-left panel, industrial metal prices have recently fallen sharply, the share prices of companies with large exposures to China have declined, and oil prices have continued their sharp declines since late June.	61	6
201410	86	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	The middle-right panel shows the recent appreciation of the US dollar against the euro and other major currencies, a development which market participants largely attribute to a divergence in monetary policy expectations and growth outlooks between the United States and most foreign economies.	61	6
201410	87	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Following this recent appreciation, many have begun to discuss the potential effect that further dollar appreciation may have on domestic growth and inflation.	61	6
201410	88	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Despite a weakening euro, measures of inflation compensation in the euro area, shown in the bottom-left panel, continued to decline and recently reached the lowest levels on record.	61	6
201410	89	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	The declines have come despite the ECB having announced numerous easing measures since its June meeting, and market participants remain concerned that the announced actions will be insufficient to return inflation to target.	61	6
201410	90	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	These concerns were amplified following the October ECB meeting, when President Draghi declined to offer an explicit target for the size of the ECB’s balance sheet amidst questions surrounding the efficacy of the already announced purchase and lending programs.	61	6
201410	91	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the bottom-right panel, expectations for the effects of these programs on the ECB’s balance sheet vary widely.	61	6
201410	92	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Summing up the central tendencies of the estimates for each program yields an expected balance sheet expansion of about 700 billion euro over the next two years, below the 1 trillion euro amount that many market participants initially interpreted the ECB to be targeting.	61	6
201410	93	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Subject to questions surrounding ECB balance sheet size and program effectiveness, a substantial share of market participants expect purchases of sovereign bonds sometime in 2015:Q1.	61	6
201410	94	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Finally, on Sunday, the ECB published the long-awaited results of its comprehensive assessment of the European banking sector.	61	6
201410	95	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	While the tests identified a net new capital need of only 5 billion euro, mainly in the periphery, market participants widely viewed the tests as credible, and price action was consistent with this conclusion.	61	6
201410	96	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Negative interest rates on eligible euro-area investments continue to challenge management of the SOMA euro foreign reserves portfolio.	61	6
201410	97	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	As discussed in previous briefings, we continue to pursue a strategy to invest incoming cash flows in the shortest-tenor, non-negative-yielding investments.	61	6
201410	98	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	As a result, duration of the portfolio has lengthened and now exceeds the Desk’s internally managed limit of 12 months, as shown in the top-left panel of your next exhibit.	61	6
201410	99	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Due to the prospects for continued negative interest rates in the euro area, the tradeoff between investing incoming cash flows in shorter-tenor negative-yielding investments and longer-tenor non-negative-yielding instruments will become more pronounced, and the portfolio’s duration is likely to climb further toward the authorized 18-month limit under our current strategy.	61	6
201410	100	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	We will circulate a memo ahead of the December meeting that discusses potential approaches given these tradeoffs.	61	6
201410	101	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Separately, on October 21, the Desk successfully performed the first non-dollar small-value liquidity swap exercise, in which we drew a small amount of euros from the ECB’s euro liquidity swap line.	61	6
201410	102	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Other central banks in the standing swap network conducted similar tests.	61	6
201410	103	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	In terms of the current dollar swap lines, demand at these auctions declined to zero.	61	6
201410	104	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	However, as we noted in a recent memo to the Committee, the Bank of England, Bank of Japan, European Central Bank, and Swiss National Bank still view continuing the seven-day operations for an additional month as prudent.	61	6
201410	105	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	As the monthly extensions are likely to continue in the near future, we intend to notify the Committee only when these foreign central banks expect to discontinue their routine auctions or if the circumstances surrounding future renewals change in a material way.	61	6
201410	106	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	We will consult with the subcommittee on foreign currency on a monthly basis to request the reaffirmation of its intent to approve routine drawings.	61	6
201410	107	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Turning to domestic operations, while Treasury and MBS purchases generally proceeded smoothly over the intermeeting period, measures of MBS operation execution deteriorated somewhat amid increased market volatility.	61	6

201410	116	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	To start, the content of the Policy Normalization Principles and Plans, published after the September FOMC meeting, was largely in line with market expectations.	61	6
201410	117	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Market participants were surprised, however, by some of the announced changes to the overnight RRP parameters.	61	6
201410	118	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Following the announcement of changes to the ON RRP parameters and leading into quarter-end, some short-term money market rates declined, as shown in the middle-left panel, with some rates dipping below the overnight RRP offered rate, even though the aggregate cap did not bind until September 30.	61	6
201410	119	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Treasury bill yields, not shown, also declined.	61	6
201410	120	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	The distribution of triparty repo rates shifted downward following the testing structure changes, and the share of volumes trading below the overnight RRP offered rate increased.	61	6
201410	121	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Market participants reported several factors contributing to some money market rates trading lower than the overnight RRP offered rate ahead of quarter-end.	61	6
201410	122	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	First, market participants had not anticipated the introduction of an overall cap at the September FOMC meeting, and the proximity of this announcement to quarter-end reportedly led some investors to scramble into other money market instruments.	61	6
201410	123	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	In addition, the introduction of the cap reportedly led to increased demand for securities that matured after quarter-end, given expectations that the overall cap would bind on September 30.	61	6
201410	124	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Finally, the prospect of a binding overall limit may have motivated cash investors to lend at lower rates in advance of quarter-end to gain favorable access to borrower balance sheets on days when the cap was seen as likely to bind.	61	6
201410	125	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	On quarter-end, the aggregate cap bound as expected.	61	6

201410	133	2014-10-29	meeting	LOGAN	Despite declines in many short-term rates and money market volumes over quarter-end, market participants characterized trading conditions as orderly, with less volatility than many had expected, and there were few signs of significant pressures at major custody banks.	61	6

201410	143	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Lorie.	61	6
201410	144	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	First, as discussed in past meetings, the Desk recommends allowing firms that meet the existing set of eligibility criteria to apply to become counterparties in overnight RRP operations.	61	6
201410	145	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	We recommend reopening the application process as an issue of fairness, in order to provide equal treatment to eligible institutions, and we anticipate that the addition of new counterparties would only modestly increase demand for overnight RRPs.	61	6
201410	146	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-right panel, we estimate that 21 money market mutual funds are eligible to apply and that about 13 of them are likely to do so.	61	6
201410	147	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Together, the 21 eligible funds have about $240 billion in assets under management, which would represent a roughly 12 percent increase from the total AUM of existing money market fund counterparties.	61	6
201410	148	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	We estimate that if all 21 funds had been counterparties, demand on a typical day in August would have been about $20 billion higher, assuming that the funds would have exhibited similar take-up for overnight RRPs, as a fraction of AUM, as the current counterparties of the same fund type.	61	6
201410	149	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Of course, this overestimates additional usage, because not all 21 funds have expressed interest in participating in operations.	61	6
201410	150	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Many FHLBs have also expressed interest in becoming counterparties, and four appear likely to meet the eligibility criteria based on a preliminary assessment of available data.	61	6
201410	151	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	The addition of these institutions could increase demand on certain days.	61	6
201410	152	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	For example, the four institutions that appear eligible have left between $2 million and $15 billion in reserves unremunerated in their Federal Reserve accounts over the past year.	61	6
201410	153	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	However, based on the behavior of existing FHLB counterparties, we do not anticipate that their participation would substantially affect volumes in the federal funds market.	61	6
201410	154	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	President Lacker raised some important points about the extended RRP counterparty management strategy in the future and how the Desk would explain this new wave of extended counterparty applications.	61	6
201410	155	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	As discussed in a June memo, the Desk’s preference is to transition to a more traditional counterparty management approach after this last wave.	61	6
201410	156	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	In the traditional approach there would be rolling admission for any firm that meets the eligibility criteria and rolling exit for counterparties that no longer meet eligibility criteria or whose performance is below standard, similar to our management strategy for primary dealers.	61	6
201410	157	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	However, particularly because of the temporary nature of the ON RRP facility, it seems important to amend this traditional approach.	61	6
201410	158	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	The simplest amendment is to set an upper limit on the number of extended counterparties.	61	6
201410	159	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Under this approach the Desk would indicate in the announcement of the new wave of applications that this would be the last such wave and, after adding the accepted counterparties, the total number of extended counterparties would not increase and the eligibility criteria would not change.	61	6
201410	160	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Of course, this approach does limit flexibility, especially because the extended counterparty list could be used for more traditional draining operations.	61	6
201410	161	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	One could couch these statements on the limit on the total number of extended counterparties and eligibility criteria as current anticipations along with an emphasis on the temporary nature of the ON RRP facility.	61	6
201410	162	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	If the Committee does not object to a final reopening of the application process to a new wave of counterparties, we would incorporate any suggestions from the Committee today on the appropriate communication strategy and circulate a draft Desk statement announcing the new wave for further comment.	61	6
201410	163	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Next, the staff proposes two changes to address concerns with the current federal funds effective rate.	61	6
201410	164	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	First, we intend to transition the underlying data source for the federal funds effective rate from the brokers to FR 2420.	61	6
201410	165	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	This change is expected to have little effect on the level of the federal funds effective rate but should enhance both its robustness and its consistency with the IOSCO principles for benchmark rates.	61	6
201410	166	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Additionally, as shown in the middle-left panel, the FR 2420 data capture a larger volume of federal funds transactions than the brokered data.	61	6
201410	167	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	This should make the effective federal funds rate more resilient to modest changes in trading activity.	61	6
201410	168	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Second, the staff would also like to publish a new overnight bank funding rate, which would comprise both Eurodollar and federal funds transactions of US-based banking offices.	61	6
201410	169	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Such a rate would provide a useful benchmark for a broader set of money market transactions and could serve as a backup in contracts for the effective federal funds rate.	61	6
201410	170	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	The underlying data for this rate would also come from FR 2420, subject to establishing that we have the legal authority to collect data from foreign banking offices controlled from the United States.	61	6
201410	171	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	This blended rate is expected to differ little from the federal funds effective rate on most days, although on quarter- end dates or during times of stress there could be greater divergence between the two rates due to the different lender groups in Eurodollars and federal funds.	61	6
201410	172	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Both of these changes could be announced in the fourth quarter of 2014, and we would expect to implement them in late summer 2015.	61	6
201410	173	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	The time between announcement and implementation is needed to enhance the data collection process, including issuing a Federal Register notice and responding appropriately to any comments that we receive, as well as to ensure the quality of the data.	61	6
201410	174	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	In the interim, the staff will work on the development of internal systems, controls, and governance principles for the new rates.	61	6
201410	175	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Please let us know if you have any concerns about these plans.	61	6
201410	176	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Finally, I would like to mention a possible new service the Federal Reserve System could offer called segregated balance accounts, or SBAs, which is outlined in the middle-right panel and discussed in more detail in a memo you received before the meeting.	61	6
201410	177	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	SBAs are an arrangement that allows banks to borrow funds from a variety of lenders, including FHLBs, and place those funds in specific accounts at the Federal Reserve that earn the IOER rate.	61	6
201410	178	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	The transaction is designed to remove credit risk, as borrowed funds would be fully collateralized by an equal amount of reserves that are segregated from the bank’s other assets.	61	6
201410	179	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	This arrangement could allow additional banks to compete for money market funds, and as a result, money market rates and the rates paid on borrowings secured by SBAs could be pushed up closer to the IOER rate.	61	6
201410	180	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	SBAs, by allowing banks to provide accounts that safeguard invested funds, should facilitate competition among a wide set of banks based predominantly on offered rates.	61	6
201410	181	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	If successful, that should lead to greater pass-through of the IOER rate and a redistribution of reserves toward banks with relatively low balance sheet costs.	61	6
201410	182	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	While SBAs could help improve the magnetic pull of IOER, they would not require the Federal Reserve to pay interest to nonbank institutions directly.	61	6
201410	183	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Additionally, unlike overnight RRPs, SBAs do not require setting an additional administered rate.	61	6
201410	184	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	The balances held in an SBA would earn IOER for the borrowing bank, and the rate and terms paid on the loan secured by the balances in the SBA would be determined privately by the participating parties.	61	6
201410	185	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	However, as with other tools for the FOMC’s consideration, there are potential risks and uncertainties that must be considered.	61	6
201410	186	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	One concern is that SBAs may reduce arbitrage activity in the federal funds market and lead to lower volumes, potentially making the effective federal funds rate more sensitive to idiosyncratic trades.	61	6
201410	187	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	There are also a number of complex legal and regulatory issues that must be resolved.	61	6
201410	188	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	In addition, at this time, interest in these accounts is unknown, as banks would need to weigh the costs associated with establishing and managing these arrangements against the benefit of earning the spread between possible SBA rates and the IOER rate.	61	6
201410	189	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	More broadly, the Committee might also want to avoid additional complexity in the communication of its policy implementation framework during normalization and the possibility of unintended consequences.	61	6
201410	190	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	The final panel outlines some next steps that staff could take to lay the groundwork for SBAs, if there was sufficient interest from the Committee in the Federal Reserve System establishing these new accounts.	61	6
201410	191	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Some of these steps can proceed internally within the System whereas others would require engagement with other agencies and the private sector.	61	6
201410	192	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201410	193	2014-10-29	meeting	POTTER	That concludes our prepared remarks.	61	6
201410	194	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you very much.	61	6

201410	504	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	These tests were the subject of one of the memos you received ahead of the meeting.	61	6
201410	505	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	As noted in the top panel of your first exhibit, reflecting in part the experience gained since September, the staff now recommends that the Committee authorize a series of preannounced modest decreases and increases in the ON RRP rate after the October FOMC meeting.	61	6
201410	506	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	In particular, the ON RRP rate would first be lowered from the current level of 5 basis points to 3 basis points, then raised to 7 basis points, and finally increased to 10 basis points.	61	6
201410	507	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	The rate would be held at each of these levels for two weeks before finally being returned to 5 basis points.	61	6
201410	508	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	A draft resolution that would allow such testing by temporarily expanding the authorized range for the ON RRP rate to 0 basis points to 10 basis points is attached to your handout.	61	6
201410	509	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Varying the ON RRP rate would affect its spread relative to the IOER rate and could provide additional information about the effect of that spread on money markets and the demand for ON RRP.	61	6
201410	510	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	In addition, changes in the ON RRP rate could assist in the assessment of the effectiveness of the ON RRP rate as a floor for short- term interest rates.	61	6
201410	511	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Of particular interest may be the results of the testing at 7 basis points and 10 basis points, as these may provide greater insight into the extent to which the proximity of the ON RRP rate to the zero lower bound is influencing the strength of the floor.	61	6
201410	512	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	The staff recommends that a full schedule of any planned ON RRP rate changes be preannounced by the Desk following the October FOMC meeting to reduce the chance that rate variations would be read as signaling a change in the stance of monetary policy.	61	6
201410	513	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	The bottom panel discusses possible testing of term RRPs to address market pressures at year-end.	61	6
201410	514	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Most market participants expect that balance sheet constraints combined with high level of reserves in the system will once again exert downward pressure on money markets around year-end.	61	6
201410	515	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	In the past, dynamics similar to those visible around quarter-ends have been observed around year-ends, but generally with more pronounced effects.	61	6
201410	516	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	This anticipated pressure raises two questions.	61	6
201410	517	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	First, does the Committee desire to take action to address it? 	61	6
201410	518	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Second, if the Committee does desire to do so, what action could it take?	61	6
201410	519	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	The Committee may wish to test the ability of supplementary tools to improve control over short-term interest rates and to help prevent a deterioration in money market liquidity as pressures build near year-end.	61	6
201410	520	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	If so, the staff recommends that the FOMC consider conducting a series of term RRP operations that span December 31, 2014.	61	6
201410	521	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	These operations would provide one of relatively few remaining opportunities prior to liftoff to meaningfully test the utility of additional supplementary tools and determine their efficacy in helping to control short-term interest rates.	61	6
201410	522	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	By increasing the availability of safe money market instruments ahead of year-end, term RRP operations could temper the potential for a buildup of pressures in money markets in the final weeks of the year.	61	6
201410	523	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	For example, such operations could absorb some demand that would otherwise push down rates on term securities, such as Treasury bills, that mature after the turn of the year.	61	6
201410	524	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	In addition, these tests may also signal to the market that the Committee, while not inclined to increase the overall limit on ON RRP usage, does have additional supplementary tools available and is prepared to deploy them if warranted.	61	6
201410	525	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Finally, the Desk conducted open market operations in order to limit temporary market strains over quarter- and year-ends prior to the financial crisis, so doing so may not be seen as particularly surprising by market participants.	61	6
201410	526	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Such a term RRP exercise could be sized to try to offset the anticipated decline in the available stock of safe money market assets that tends to occur around year-end.	61	6
201410	527	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	A staff analysis suggests that on quarter-ends in 2014, the supply across a number of types of money market assets has declined, in aggregate, by about $150 billion to $200 billion.	61	6
201410	528	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	However, this staff analysis omits a number of significant asset classes, including bilateral federal funds and Eurodollar activity, due to a lack of daily data; in addition, the increase in demand observed at the September 30 ON RRP operation exceeded these amounts.	61	6
201410	529	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Accordingly, $300 billion of term RRP over year-end might be a more realistic estimate of what would be required to meet the increase in demand for safe money market assets.	61	6
201410	530	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	The Desk could announce following the October FOMC meeting that it has been authorized to conduct term RRP operations in December to cross year-end, with a cumulative size limit of up to $300 billion, and that it will announce specific operational details by early December.	61	6
201410	531	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	By helping to resolve some of the uncertainty regarding the availability of safe money market instruments ahead of year-end, and thus facilitating advanced planning by market participants, the early announcement should avoid the “scramble” that reportedly took place in the short period between the September FOMC meeting and quarter-end.	61	6
201410	532	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	The staff recommends that term RRP operations be conducted at several different times over the course of December.	61	6
201410	533	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	For example, fixed-quantity auctions could be conducted each Friday in December for $25 billion, $50 billion, $100 billion, and $125 billion, with each operation settling the Monday after the auction and maturing on January 2, 2015.	61	6
201410	534	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Bidding behavior and movements in money market rates associated with these operations could provide readings of year-end pressures over the course of December.	61	6
201410	535	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Of course, this proposal is preliminary, and should the Committee pursue this option, it would need to be refined based on market participants’ feedback, operational considerations, and evolving market conditions, including issuance plans by the Treasury Department.	61	6
201410	536	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Once the specific plan is determined, the staff could submit it to the Chair for approval, notify the Committee, and release the operational details to market participants.	61	6
201410	537	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	A draft resolution for such an approach is included in the handout.	61	6
201410	538	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Alternatively, the Committee may find it desirable to take no action to address year-end pressures, for example, if meeting participants are concerned about appearing to accommodate “window dressing” behaviors by banks and are comfortable with potentially significant downward pressure on short-term rates.	61	6
201410	539	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	This strategy would provide a second observation of the performance of the current framework on quarter-ends, without the potentially confounding surprise factor of an announcement relatively late in the quarter, as was the case in September.	61	6
201410	540	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	In addition, taking no action could reinforce the FOMC’s earlier communication that occasional day-to-day volatility in money market rates is acceptable and that the ON RRP facility will remain small.	61	6
201410	541	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Another possibility would be to mix these two approaches by testing term RRPs over year-end and then, so long as the test went well and liftoff did not appear imminent, allowing the March quarter-end to pass without Desk action.	61	6
201410	542	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Depending on your decisions regarding these testing issues, we will have copies of the Desk statement available for review tomorrow.	61	6
201410	543	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	Thank you.	61	6
201410	544	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	That concludes my prepared remarks.	61	6

201410	660	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Tarullo.	62	6
201410	661	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	62	6
201410	662	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Fabio said a good bit of what I might have said, Jeff, in response to your observation.	62	6
201410	663	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I think there’s not going to be a perfect alternative here, and we have recognized that in our discussions over the last couple of meetings.	62	6
201410	664	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	We have aims that are somewhat in tension with one another.	62	6
201410	665	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Number one, as the Chair just stated a few moments ago, is wanting to have a lot of credibility at the point of liftoff and perhaps for a meeting or two thereafter.	62	6
201410	666	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Number two is not wanting to put in place a program which invites a significant change in the financial industry that may, in turn, increase the chances of runs in periods of stress.	62	6
201410	667	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I think what’s being proposed here is a way to avoid signaling in advance that we’re going to have a cap increase if there are any problems with the floor.	62	6
201410	668	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t think anybody is taking that off the table, but what I think the staff is proposing here is a way to determine whether a mix of instruments will do the job sufficiently so that we don’t have to raise the cap.	62	6
201410	669	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	If what we learn in December is, notwithstanding the mix of instruments, there’s still an awful lot of softness that makes a majority of the Committee uneasy, then we might actually have to think about raising the cap when we lift off.	62	6
201410	670	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But this is a way of giving ourselves a chance of not doing that.	62	6
201410	671	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	By doing this, we’re going to lose some information that we might otherwise have had by just keeping the $300 billion cap.	62	6
201410	672	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Suppose everything goes well in December.	62	6
201410	673	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	We’re not going to know whether that’s because participants adjusted and made arrangements beforehand or because of the term.	62	6
201410	674	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	We’re not going to know whether it was because September 30 was a special date, because that’s the day on which balance sheets are frozen for stress testing and CCAR purposes, or whether it’s just an end-of-quarter issue.	62	6
201410	675	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	So we’re not going to know some of that, but that’s what happens when you have to make policy decisions in real time.	62	6
201410	676	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	You’re not able to do everything you want.	62	6
201410	677	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Although there are elements of this that I sort of regret, I really do think this is the best way to try to balance those two ends which are potentially in tension with one another, and it gives us the best shot at an outcome that doesn’t compromise either of those goals.	62	6
201410	678	2014-10-29	meeting	NATALUCCI	I guess one way to respond, to try to regain some of the information, would be not to do it in March.	62	6
201410	679	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	That’s a good point.	62	6
201410	680	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	So what I was going to say is after this is done, we can in January debate whether (a) we would like to have the cap, (b) we would like to keep everything that we had in December, or (c) we want to kind of “go cold” and see what happens in March without any program at all.	62	6

201410	811	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	I will be referring to the materials distributed for the US outlook.	11	1
201410	812	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	The net tightening in overall financial conditions since the September Tealbook projection led us to revise down our medium-term economic outlook.	11	1
201410	813	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	However, as you can see from the first panel of your forecast summary exhibit, the spending data that we received since the previous Tealbook resulted in our making only minor revisions to the near-term GDP projection.	11	1
201410	814	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	In particular, although the data on consumer spending that we received after the September Tealbook closed— and reported at the September FOMC meeting—surprised us to the upside, subsequent consumption data were weaker than we expected.	11	1
201410	815	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	As a result, our near- term PCE forecast is about unrevised from our previous Tealbook projection.	11	1
201410	816	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Revisions to the other major categories of spending were relatively small, and more or less offset each other.	11	1
201410	817	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	The data we received this morning on orders, shipments, and inventories of durable goods had no material effect on our near-term forecast.	11	1
201410	818	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Over the medium term, we adjusted down our projection for real GDP growth by about ¼ percentage point in each of the next three years.	11	1
201410	819	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	This revision primarily reflects financial conditioning assumptions that, taken as a whole, we see as less supportive of economic activity than those used in September.	11	1
201410	820	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Specifically, in this Tealbook we have a higher projected path for the dollar and a somewhat lower trajectory for equity prices over the medium term; the negative effects of these revisions on economic activity are only partly offset by the downward revisions we have made to longer-term interest rates.	11	1
201410	821	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	In addition to these changes in financial assumptions, we also have a slightly slower projected pace of foreign economic growth, which is a small drag on US GDP growth, along with a lower expected path for oil prices that provides some boost to domestic economic activity.	11	1
201410	822	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Since last Wednesday when the October Tealbook projection was closed, equity prices have retraced a portion—but not all—of their decline since the previous Tealbook; however, this would only shave a bit from the downward revision to our projection for GDP growth in the October Tealbook.	11	1
201410	823	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Most of the revision to projected longer-term interest rates reflects a downward revision to our assumed path for the federal funds rate.	11	1
201410	824	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	We continue to assume that the federal funds rate will lift off from its effective lower bound in the second quarter of 2015.	11	1
201410	825	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	However, reflecting the wider output gap and slightly lower path for core inflation that we have in the current forecast, the inertial Taylor rule that we use to set our policy rate assumption prescribes a funds rate path that rises less steeply after liftoff than that in our September projection.	11	1
201410	826	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Turning to conditions in the labor market, the September employment report was a little stronger than we had expected.	11	1
201410	827	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	In the household survey, the unemployment rate—shown in panel 2—declined to 5.9 percent in September; we had expected it to hold steady at 6.1 percent.	11	1
201410	828	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Meanwhile, in the establishment survey, the level of total payroll employment—panel 3—was about 90,000 higher last month than in our previous Tealbook projection.	11	1
201410	829	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	We took some of this better-than-expected news on board in revisiting our near- term forecast for the labor market.	11	1
201410	830	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Over the remainder of the projection period, however, we weakened our outlook for the labor market in line with the downward revisions we made to the pace of real output growth.	11	1
201410	831	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	In particular, we now expect the unemployment rate to be 5¼ percent at the end of 2017—¼ percentage point higher than in our September forecast, and equal to our estimate of the natural rate.	11	1
201410	832	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Similarly, the projected level of payroll employment at the end of 2017 is about 700,000 lower than in our previous projection.	11	1
201410	833	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	The next two panels summarize our inflation projection.	11	1
201410	834	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	As you can see from panel 4, we have marked down our near-term projection for total PCE price inflation noticeably; this downward revision to headline inflation is mainly attributable to recent declines in crude oil prices, which we have fed through to our forecast for consumer energy prices.	11	1
201410	835	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	As you can see from panel 5, we also slightly lowered our near-term projection for core PCE price inflation; this revision reflects incoming data that have been a little softer than expected as well as a downward revision to core import prices over the second half of this year.	11	1
201410	836	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Further out, our core inflation forecast is just a touch lower than in September, reflecting both the wider margin of slack in the current projection and the pass-through of lower core and energy prices.	11	1
201410	837	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	We continue to anticipate that core PCE inflation will move up gradually over the projection period—from 1.5 percent this year to 1.8 percent in 2017—as labor and product markets tighten.	11	1
201410	838	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	As always, numerous risks surround our outlook.	11	1
201410	839	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	The final panel notes two risks to our baseline projection that we presented as alternative scenarios in the Risks and Uncertainty section of the Tealbook.	11	1
201410	840	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	First, as you know, our medium-term inflation projection hinges on the assumption that the longer-term inflation expectations that are relevant for wage and price setting are currently at 1.8 percent.	11	1
201410	841	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	In the scenario titled “Lower Long-Term Inflation Expectations,” we considered the possibility that this assumption is wrong.	11	1
201410	842	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Specifically, we assumed that the current level of these expectations is 1.5 percent—a value that is comparable to recent actual inflation—and that longer-term expectations are set adaptively with reference to the behavior of actual past inflation.	11	1
201410	843	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Under these assumptions, core inflation runs about ¼ percentage point below the Tealbook baseline over the medium term and the unemployment rate falls to 4¾ percent by the end of 2017.	11	1
201410	844	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Liftoff of the federal funds rate is delayed until early 2017; at that time, inflation one to two years ahead remains about ½ percentage point below the Committee’s 2 percent longer-term objective.	11	1
201410	845	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	A second scenario explored the possibility that, although the financial market volatility over the past few weeks seems to have eased, it may instead represent the first installment of what could prove to be a broader and more prolonged reassessment of risk.	11	1
201410	846	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	In particular, we considered a scenario in which heightened risk aversion results in a large reduction in equity prices, persistently wider risk spreads for longer-term interest rates, and lower consumer and business confidence.	11	1
201410	847	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	The resulting hit to economic activity yields an unemployment rate path that is more than a percentage point above the Tealbook baseline by the end of the medium term, with the federal funds rate stuck at the effective lower bound for the next five years.	11	1
201410	848	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Interestingly, the pace of increases in unit labor costs, and thus price inflation, are essentially unchanged from our baseline, as slower wage growth stemming from a higher unemployment rate is roughly offset by the effect of reduced productivity growth from less capital deepening.	11	1
201410	849	2014-10-29	meeting	ENGEN	Steve Kamin will now continue our presentation.	11	1
201410	850	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Thank you.	11	1
201410	851	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	I’ll be referring to the materials labeled “Material for the Foreign Outlook.”	11	1
201410	852	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	I find it extremely irritating when a company is rolling out a new product—for example, since it seems to be on my mind, Arby’s new Hawaiian BBQ brisket sandwich—and they run commercials for it on television every seven minutes.	11	1
201410	853	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	You may have felt the same way when you read about the effect of the dollar on the US economy in our note to the Committee, again in a box in the Domestic Economic Developments and Outlook section of the Tealbook, and then again in the Risks and Uncertainty section of the Tealbook.	11	1
201410	854	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	All I can say is that, like Arby’s new Hawaiian BBQ brisket sandwich, the dollar has been very much on our minds lately, given its sharp run-up in recent months and the implications of any future appreciation for US activity and prices.	11	1
201410	855	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	If it is any consolation, however, I will not be discussing the dollar until later in my remarks.	11	1
201410	856	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	In the meantime, I would like to address that other elephant in the room, the recent surge in financial volatility around the world.	11	1
201410	857	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Although financial newspapers were running stories to interpret the surge with headlines like “The Global Economy Stalling,” our assessment is that incoming data from abroad, while disappointing, on balance, were hardly weak enough to presage widespread retrenchment.	11	1
201410	858	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Accordingly, as shown in panel 1, we have marked down our forecast for foreign economic growth just a bit beyond the near term.	11	1
201410	859	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Certainly, the global economic indicators that we follow, such as the index of new export orders shown in panel 2, do not signal an imminent global slowdown.	11	1
201410	860	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Moreover, the rise in the dollar and decline in oil prices we’ve seen in recent months should provide some support for economic activity abroad.	11	1
201410	861	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	To be sure, much of the concern in financial markets has focused on the euro area and China, but even there, the news has not been uniformly bad.	11	1
201410	862	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	In the euro area, as shown in panel 3, the Eurocoin coincident indicator continues to signal expansion, although it has weakened recently.	11	1
201410	863	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	The most recent data, including PMIs, German auto production, and consumer confidence, have been reasonably assuring, and we are projecting that euro-area GDP will continue its paltry recovery in the quarters to come.	11	1
201410	864	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	A second area of concern has been China, where a turndown in the property market, the red line in panel 4, has prompted fears of a financial sector bust, a sharp slowdown in growth, and spillovers to trading partners around the world.	11	1
201410	865	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Such concerns were especially pronounced when data for August showed a sharp decline in industrial activity.	11	1
201410	866	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	In the event, industrial production rebounded in September and third-quarter GDP came in, by our estimate, at a very solid 7¾ percent annual rate, allaying fears of an imminent hard landing.	11	1
201410	867	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Although we’ve marked down our forecast a bit, as domestic demand appears to have lost some momentum, we are still projecting solid growth.	11	1
201410	868	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	All told, as Lorie suggested earlier, our sense is that the earlier downdrafts in markets likely were prompted not so much by markdowns to investors’ modal forecasts for the global outlook but rather by a heightened focus on the downside risks to the outlook, coming after a period when investors had appeared quite sanguine.	11	1
201410	869	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Although markets probably overdid their mood swing, the downside risks are certainly significant.	11	1
201410	870	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	In the euro area, the economy’s underlying momentum is weak enough that it would not take much to push it back into recession.	11	1
201410	871	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Moreover, with headline inflation down to only 0.3 percent, additional declines, even if caused by falling energy prices, could further unhinge inflation expectations, boost real interest rates, and diminish confidence in the authorities’ willingness to do what it takes to support the economy.	11	1
201410	872	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	The ECB apparently is considering additional measures, such as corporate bond purchases, and the recent completion of the bank stress tests is an important achievement, but there are good reasons to be worried.	11	1
201410	873	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	The same is true of China.	11	1
201410	874	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	The recent declines in housing prices and sales are probably helpful in curbing excesses and should not, by themselves, lead to unmanageable stresses.	11	1
201410	875	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	But once begun, it is hard to know when this correction will end.	11	1
201410	876	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Although the Chinese government has the capacity to backstop the financial sector, a vicious cycle of falling property prices, mounting defaults, lending cutbacks, and contractions in spending could unwind so quickly that the authorities fall behind the curve.	11	1
201410	877	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	A hard landing in China, in turn, might trigger distress in other parts of the global economy.	11	1
201410	878	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	As I threatened earlier, these considerations bring us to the dollar, whose run-up in recent months appears attributable in large part to increased concerns about the foreign outlook.	11	1
201410	879	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 5, the starting point for our forecast of the broad real dollar has moved up 3½ percent between the time of the July Tealbook, the green dashed line, and the present.	11	1
201410	880	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 6, we anticipate further increases in the dollar against the AFE currencies as, in our baseline forecast, US short-term interest rates rise faster than markets currently expect.	11	1
201410	881	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	But the dollar declines against the EME currencies, panel 7, as the Chinese renminbi appreciates, dragging up the currencies of its Asian neighbors.	11	1
201410	882	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	All told, returning to the solid black line in panel 5, we continue to project some decline in the broad real dollar.	11	1
201410	883	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	However, we are now assuming a bit less dollar depreciation than we had previously.	11	1
201410	884	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	The note we circulated to the Committee last week describes how we have revised our forecasts for the EME currencies in three respects.	11	1
201410	885	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	We now assume that surprises to US interest rates will affect these currencies, we have scaled back the extent to which the Chinese renminbi appreciates over the next year, and we have scaled back how much other Asian currencies will respond to changes in the renminbi.	11	1
201410	886	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	As can be seen by comparing our current forecast with the red dashed line, which represents the forecast that we would have written down for this Tealbook had we not revised our approach, these revisions lead to only a slight lift to our dollar projection, but they should tie our exchange rate forecast more closely to the overall global outlook as well as to surprises in interest rates associated with policy normalization.	11	1
201410	887	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Of course, any forecasting process will have trouble capturing movements in asset prices such as the exchange rate.	11	1
201410	888	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	In consequence, we can hardly preclude the possibility of a further large run-up in the dollar.	11	1
201410	889	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Your next exhibit draws on our SIGMA general equilibrium model to explore the effects of a 10 percent appreciation shock to the dollar, similar to some of the analysis we presented in our note to the Committee and in the Tealbook.	11	1
201410	890	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Starting with panel 1, the blue line shows how the shock is phased in over several quarters and then gradually dies out, assuming that monetary policy (panel 2) follows the staff’s baseline projection and does not respond to the shock.	11	1
201410	891	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Note that the movement of the dollar in this scenario would be very large compared with its variation in recent years, but not entirely unprecedented.	11	1
201410	892	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	In response, and with no cushion from monetary policy, both output growth (panel 3) and core PCE inflation (panel 4) drop below 1 percent on a four-quarter basis.	11	1
201410	893	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Of course, in reality, monetary policy would not remain unchanged, and the red lines in the panels assume that policy responds to the shock in a manner consistent with the Taylor (1999) rule.	11	1
201410	894	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 2, the federal funds rate lifts off one quarter later than in the baseline and is 50 basis points below baseline by 2016.	11	1
201410	895	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	In consequence, the dollar (panel 1) appreciates less in response to the shock than when monetary policy is held fixed.	11	1
201410	896	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Both GDP growth (panel 3) and, to a lesser extent, inflation (panel 4) fall by less as well.	11	1
201410	897	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Bottom line:  Movements in the dollar can indeed be an important influence on the US economy, although adjustments in monetary policy can moderate its effects.	11	1
201410	898	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Nellie Liang will now continue our presentation.	11	1
201410	899	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Thank you, Steve.	11	1
201410	900	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	I will be referring to “Material for Briefing on Financial Stability Developments.”	FS	FS
201410	901	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	My briefing today summarizes our recent QS financial stability assessment.	FS	FS
201410	902	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Recent financial market developments illustrate the potential for shocks to trigger sizable increases in volatility and declines in asset prices.	FS	FS
201410	903	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	However, the US financial system appears resilient to shocks of the magnitude we’ve seen to date, in line with our judgment that vulnerabilities remain, on balance, at a moderate level.	FS	FS
201410	904	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	While we view asset valuation pressures to be above average—a notable “orange” in our heat map—reflecting some reach-for-yield behavior in a low-rate environment, there is substantially more capital and less short- term wholesale funding in the financial system than in the mid-2000s.	FS	FS
201410	905	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Turning to your first exhibit, as shown in the top-left panel, the largest domestic banking firms reported in their third-quarter earnings releases that their capital exceeded their new fully phased-in Tier 1 common equity requirements, including the proposed international SIFI surcharge.	FS	FS
201410	906	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	For leveraged nonbank financial firms, for which we have much less data, leverage also appears relatively low, though likely it has been rising at hedge funds.	FS	FS
201410	907	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	And as shown to the right, net short-term wholesale funding for the broad financial sector, expressed as a ratio to GDP, has remained low and is back to levels of the early 1990s.	FS	FS
201410	908	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	The lower levels, combined with less leverage, suggest that the potential for fire-sale externalities is much diminished.	FS	FS
201410	909	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Our overall assessment is also supported by subdued growth in household sector debt, shown in the middle-left panel by the decline in the blue shaded area since the crisis.	FS	FS
201410	910	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	As we highlighted in a box in the QS summary, lower debt burdens of households at this time likely make the economy much less vulnerable to a sharp house price decline than in 2007, when high debt levels made spending especially sensitive to a house price collapse.	FS	FS
201410	911	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Turning to asset valuations, as shown in the middle-right panel, the expected real return on equity for the broad market remains in a range of about 6 to 7 percent, despite the recent decline in prices, rise in volatility, and some unwinding of leveraged positions.	FS	FS
201410	912	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Its gap to the real 10-year Treasury yield remains wide.	FS	FS
201410	913	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	While this estimated equity premium suggests a lack of valuation pressures, it is vulnerable to a scenario in which profit margins decline more than expected, which, as described in a box in the Tealbook, could cause a significant decline in stock prices.	FS	FS
201410	914	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	In addition, as we have noted for some time, there are pockets of valuation pressures.	FS	FS
201410	915	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Valuations are elevated for small cap stocks (not shown), and risk spreads are narrow and underwriting standards have been loose in the speculative-grade debt markets.	FS	FS
201410	916	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	As shown in the bottom left, the recent small rise in high-yield bond spreads was concentrated mostly in the near term, while far-term forward spreads, an indicator of investor sentiment toward risk, remained near the bottom end of their historical ranges.	FS	FS
201410	917	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Meanwhile, valuation pressures have broadened to the commercial real estate sector.	FS	FS
201410	918	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Property prices have been rising sharply, and as shown to the right, the price- to-income ratio for office properties, the black line, has been moving up.	FS	FS
201410	919	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	CMBS issuance, the yellow bars, has increased, and competition among lenders for loans has led to increases in loan-to-value ratios and more loans with full or partial interest-only periods, and there appears to be some “shopping” for ratings by CMBS issuers.	FS	FS
201410	920	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Investors have been pushing back, but these trends bear watching.	FS	FS
201410	921	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Turning to your next exhibit, as shown in the top-left panel, issuance of high-yield bonds and syndicated leveraged loans remained solid in Q3; total debt outstanding from these combined sources, the black line, has continued to increase and is now close to $2 trillion.	FS	FS
201410	922	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	In addition, the share of the lower-quality debt has been rising.	FS	FS
201410	923	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	As shown to the right, the fraction of leveraged loans with ratings of B-minus or lower at origination, the orange and red bars combined, continued to increase.	FS	FS
201410	924	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	The rise in debt outstanding is showing through to debt positions of some nonfinancial corporate businesses.	FS	FS
201410	925	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	As shown by the black line in the middle left, the net leverage ratio for speculative-grade firms is nearing the top end of its range over recent decades.	FS	FS
201410	926	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	This increase, however, is not evident for investment-grade firms, which account for most of the nonfinancial corporate debt.	FS	FS
201410	927	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	As noted to the right, models that predict defaults and bond returns suggest that a sustained rapid rise in riskier debt would lead to notably higher default rates and lower returns in a couple of years than in a scenario of moderate debt growth.	FS	FS
201410	928	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	The resulting increase in losses would likely reduce credit availability and contribute to a boom-bust credit cycle, and could increase the risks to your macroeconomic objectives.	FS	FS
201410	929	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	If the losses were borne by leveraged investors, the severity of a credit cycle could be greater.	FS	FS
201410	930	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	While banks mostly distribute the leveraged loans they originate rather than hold them, some banks purchase the triple-A-rated tranches of CLOs, though direct expected losses on such holdings appear, at this point, quite manageable.	FS	FS
201410	931	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Currently, other major buyers of these tranches do not appear to be funding them with short-term debt.	FS	FS
201410	932	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	However, in the June SCOOS, a significant number of dealers reported increased demand by hedge funds to fund CLO tranches, and there are reports of increased use of total return swaps (TRS) to gain exposure to loans and CLOs.	FS	FS
201410	933	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Repo financing and TRS are areas that bear watching, since a decline in collateral values could amplify the effects of higher defaults.	FS	FS
201410	934	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	In addition, any losses from credit or duration risk could be exacerbated by growing liquidity mismatch between corporate bond funds and the underlying assets.	FS	FS
201410	935	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	As shown in the bottom-left panel, bond mutual funds and ETFs have expanded relative to the total corporate bond market, implying that more of these bonds are being held with daily or intradaily claims against them.	FS	FS
201410	936	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	As a consequence, there is a greater risk of liquidity price discounts in the event that funds need to sell bonds to meet redemptions.	FS	FS
201410	937	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	However, while this risk looks to have risen notably, we are not sure if any price discounts or volatility this would generate would be substantial or sustained.	FS	FS
201410	938	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	The recent experience at Pimco provides only limited insight into this risk.	FS	FS
201410	939	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Pimco had nearly $2 trillion of assets under management, of which about $530 billion were in open-end mutual funds.	FS	FS
201410	940	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	As shown by the red line in the bottom-right chart, the unexpected resignation by Bill Gross was followed over subsequent days by substantial outflows from the flagship Total Return Fund (TRF), about 4 percent on the day of the announcement, and at a few other smaller funds that he had managed, shown by the green line.	FS	FS
201410	941	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Notably, other mutual funds at Pimco did not have such substantial outflows, showed by the yellow dashed line, suggesting a lack of contagion.	FS	FS
201410	942	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Moreover, the outflows appeared to have had few lasting imprints on market prices.	FS	FS
201410	943	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	The lessons learned from this episode, however, are limited because the TRF had built up a substantial liquidity cushion prior to the announcement well in excess of the withdrawals, and this event was idiosyncratic, rather than arising from more general concerns about asset prices.	FS	FS
201410	944	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Your final exhibit concludes by noting a few policy initiatives that the staff are pursuing related to specific financial vulnerabilities.	FS	FS
201410	945	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	On leveraged loans, supervisors continue to evaluate ways to improve adherence to the leveraged lending guidance.	FS	FS
201410	946	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	To date, our monitoring suggests only limited migration of underwriting to outside of the regulated banking sector, although some smaller credits are being underwritten and distributed by nonbank firms.	FS	FS
201410	947	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Last week, we released the macroeconomic scenarios for CCAR 2015 for the 31 largest BHCs to assess their ability to weather a severe recession.	FS	FS
201410	948	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Relative to last year, this year’s severely adverse scenario specified slightly more severe stresses in the riskier segments of corporate debt markets as well as higher oil prices.	FS	FS
201410	949	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	In the adverse scenario, which is also required under Dodd-Frank, we specified an up and flatter yield curve, which introduces some funding cost stresses.	FS	FS
201410	950	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Separately, the staff has been evaluating interest rate risk in the trading books at the six largest banks.	FS	FS
201410	951	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Our analysis suggests direct losses from interest rate shocks are quite limited, and we did not find in our limited screening that there is a significant concentration among sellers of interest rate protection.	FS	FS
201410	952	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	That is, we don’t find an “AIG” of interest-rate risk.	FS	FS
201410	953	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	That said, many banks’ trading books appear highly correlated.	FS	FS
201410	954	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	On asset management, we are working with other FSOC agencies to evaluate possible systemic risks associated with asset management activities, including the use of debt and derivatives, liquidity transformation, and operational risks.	FS	FS
201410	955	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	Finally, the sharp price moves in Treasury and other futures on October 15, which Lorie described earlier, suggest that high-frequency and algorithmic trading activity may contribute in perhaps unexpected ways to intraday volatility and elevated correlations across asset markets.	FS	FS
201410	956	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	The staff are continuing to work to better understand the events of that day.	FS	FS
201410	957	2014-10-29	meeting	LIANG	That concludes our prepared remarks, and we are happy to take any questions.	FS	FS
