201410	988	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	On the dollar, I think there are two questions.	12	1
201410	989	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	First, what is the probability of it indeed increasing by 10 percent?	12	1
201410	990	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	I think our staff actually looked into these variations in the dollar historically using our data and came up with a number in the neighborhood of 10 percent.	12	1
201410	991	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	So a 10 percent chance of it rising that much.	12	1
201410	992	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Over what period?	12	1
201410	993	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Actually, maybe Chris over there could answer that.	12	1
201410	994	2014-10-29	meeting	ERCEG	Three quarters.	12	1
201410	995	2014-10-29	meeting	ERCEG	That it would rise 10 percent within three quarters.	12	1
201410	996	2014-10-29	meeting	ERCEG	Some of our staff ran a random walk model of the dollar and assessed the probability that it would rise at least 10 percent within three quarters.	12	1
201410	997	2014-10-29	meeting	ERCEG	It came up with a number on the order of 10 percent.	12	1
201410	998	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Okay.	12	1
201410	999	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	I thought Vice Chairman Dudley’s question was, over what historical period did you do that analysis?	12	1
201410	1000	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	ERCEG:  I think they went back roughly 30 years.	12	1
201410	1001	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	All right.	12	1
201410	1002	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Fine.	12	1
201410	1003	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s a good answer.	12	1
201410	1004	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Let’s put it this way.	12	1
201410	1005	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	If you have to think of choosing a random date in that 30-year period compared with now, it seems to me, based on the evolution of the economy, that now it might have a higher likelihood.	12	1
201410	1006	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Yes.	12	1
201410	1007	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I would think it would probably be higher than that.	12	1
201410	1008	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	So 10 percent will be the low number there.	12	1
201410	1009	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	And then, your other question is, well, how do we adjust our forecast in light of these changes in asset prices?	12	1
201410	1010	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Certainly, for the dollar, I think our view takes into account a couple of things.	12	1
201410	1011	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Number one, the basis for our forecast, before we add things onto it, is a random-walk model generated under the assumption that the current level of the dollar incorporates all expectation of future developments that the market already perceives.	12	1
201410	1012	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	But isn’t that future expectation based on their view of how the economy is going to evolve?	12	1
201410	1013	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	And our view of how the economy would evolve might be different.	12	1
201410	1014	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Right.	12	1
201410	1015	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	And when that is true, that is when we add to that.	12	1
201410	1016	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Okay.	12	1
201410	1017	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	You do.	12	1
201410	1018	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Exactly.	12	1
201410	1019	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	That’s when we look at how we think interest rates are going to evolve.	12	1
201410	1020	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	We compare it with how the market thinks interest rates are going to evolve.	12	1
201410	1021	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	And if, for example, we think that US interest rates are going to rise more than the market expects, then we expect that in the future the markets will be surprised by interest rates rising.	12	1
201410	1022	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	In that circumstance, the dollar will rise, and we will build that into our current forecast.	12	1
201410	1023	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	But there are these level shifts.	12	1
201410	1024	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Yes.	12	1
201410	1025	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	But then when the level shifts happen, we basically, in that random walk way, start with the new level and then add our “surprise factors” on top of that, just because we think that it incorporates all of the incoming information that has occurred.	12	1
201410	1026	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	And an important point to make, which I think will distinguish this from the 10-year bond yield, is that we don’t really have any good anchors for what the exchange rate ought to be.	12	1
201410	1027	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	In other words, you can come up with measures of the equilibrium exchange rate or an equilibrium dollar based on, for example, current account considerations or things like that.	12	1
201410	1028	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	But we think that those are extremely poor attractors of the actual dollar.	12	1
201410	1029	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	In other words, the dollar tends not to move toward whatever equilibrium you pick.	12	1
201410	1030	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I can see that.	12	1
201410	1031	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	And how about the stock market?	12	1
201410	1032	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	ENGEN:  As you correctly pointed out, our longer-term interest rates are anchored by our assumed path for policy rates.	12	1
201410	1033	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	On the stock market, we do not have an anchor that is as hard and fast, say, as an assumed path for the policy rate, but we do have a view that is informed by models on what the equity premium will be moving toward.	12	1
201410	1034	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	One way to think about it is, if our view on the equity premium at the end of the medium term is unchanged, then our path will not level-shift for stock prices.	12	1
201410	1035	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The current changes will be retraced at some other time.	12	1
201410	1036	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	And indeed, in this Tealbook, the reduction in current equity prices, at least at the time of the Tealbook, was greater than the reduction in the endpoint further out.	12	1
201410	1037	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	We actually have slightly faster assumed equity price increases over the medium term.	12	1
201410	1038	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	To give a little bit of advertising, not in this next round but the round after, we are planning one of our framework memos that will discuss how we put together the models we use for our financial assumptions.	12	1
201410	1039	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	But that equity-premium model is informed by earnings projections as well as projections for the economy.	12	1

201410	1163	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	If it’s endogenous, then it is led by the fact that we are outperforming, or we have surprised to the upside.	12	1
201410	1164	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	And I think it makes a big difference.	12	1
201410	1165	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	It is less worrisome to me that we have dollar strength as a result of our output increases or improved economic performance than if it is the other case.	12	1
201410	1166	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	We very much take that point, and that’s in fact why we added that section at the end of one of the memos.	12	1
201410	1167	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	That’s a tiny section.	12	1
201410	1168	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Right.	12	1
201410	1169	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Why was it so tiny?	12	1
201410	1170	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	There are a couple of issues.	12	1
201410	1171	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	First of all, this is an issue of how to parse out the changes in the forecast that we have made, let’s say between July and now, and their effect on the US economy.	12	1
201410	1172	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	And in that regard, you certainly have to take into account, what are these impulses that tend to drive economic growth up, and thus, lift the dollar?	12	1
201410	1173	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	And then, what might be the partial equilibrium direct effect of the rise in the dollar once it occurred, even an endogenous response to the US economy’s better outlook?	12	1
201410	1174	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Let’s put it this way.	12	1
201410	1175	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	Even if you fully took on board that much of the rise in the dollar might have been an endogenous response to the US economy, in doing the exercise of parsing out the different influences on the US outlook, you’d still want to know what that direct effect was.	12	1
201410	1176	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	That was one of the considerations in play.	12	1
201410	1177	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	The other one was, when we took a serious look at what were the factors that lifted the dollar over the course of the last four months or so, we came to the view that there was some favorable incoming data on the United States that was indeed tending to boost the dollar, as well as unfavorable data for foreign economies.	12	1
201410	1178	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	But that was not the whole picture, and by our reckoning that wasn’t even most of the run-up in the dollar.	12	1
201410	1179	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	By our reckoning, most of the run- up in the dollar seemed to reflect worries or uncertainties about the outlook rather than markdowns to agents’ modal forecasts for the economies.	12	1
201410	1180	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	And so in terms of parsing through the effects, insofar as that wasn’t a genuine increase in US growth, but was rather changes in agents’ distributions over future likelihoods of economic growth, we thought that a lot of that run-up in the dollar could thus be treated as if it were exogenous, at least in the growth process.	12	1
201410	1181	2014-10-29	meeting	KAMIN	So that’s one of the other reasons why we tend to focus on explaining the exogenous run-up in the dollar.	12	1

201410	1250	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201410	1251	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	My forecast for the real economy has not changed much from the last FOMC meeting, despite the financial market turbulence.	13	1
201410	1252	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	While some of the international data proved to be softer than expected, that surprise did not seem commensurate with the financial market movements of the last several weeks.	13	1
201410	1253	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	My current expectation is that some of the recent asset price movements will prove fleeting, leaving at most a small imprint on real domestic conditions.	13	1
201410	1254	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In effect, I am assuming that there was a temporary flight to quality that will abate as incoming data show only a modest reduction in global growth.	13	1
201410	1255	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	While the dollar has appreciated, my forecast had already built in some appreciation.	13	1
201410	1256	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	As a result, I’ve only marked down my net exports slightly to reflect the somewhat greater appreciation of the dollar and somewhat weaker data in Europe than I had previously expected.	13	1
201410	1257	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I do have some concerns that the combination of an appreciated dollar and reduced prices for oil, grain, and other commodities makes it unlikely we will reach 2 percent inflation as quickly as many of our SEP forecasts predict.	13	1
201410	1258	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Adding in the very modest increases in wages to date, it is quite likely that we will see both core and total PCE inflation rates remaining at 1½ percent or less for several quarters.	13	1
201410	1259	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Because I believe that liftoff should not occur until there’s clear evidence that full employment is within reach and inflation is trending toward our 2 percent goal, my monetary policy assumption differs from that of the Tealbook in that it both defers liftoff and assumes a more gradual increase in interest rates after liftoff from the zero lower bound.	13	1
201410	1260	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The longer we remain well below our 2 percent target, the more risk we take that inflation expectations drift down, implying a loss of credibility with the public.	13	1
201410	1261	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The experience from Japan and now Europe indicates that indifference to very low inflation rates can generate a significant loss of confidence in the ability of a central bank to hit its 2 percent target.	13	1
201410	1262	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	It is hard to rationalize a 10-year German bond trading around 85 basis points and a 10-year Japanese bond trading below 50 basis points with any confidence that 10-year average inflation rates will be anywhere close to the publicly announced targets.	13	1
201410	1263	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The financial market attention to inflation breakeven rates highlights an increased focus on our ability to hit our 2 percent inflation target.	13	1
201410	1264	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	While I currently believe the flight to quality has temporarily distorted Treasury prices in a way that obscures the inflation expectations embedded in them, were the low inflation breakevens to persist, I’d become more concerned that they were signaling a downward drift in longer-run inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1265	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	While my baseline forecast for real variables has not changed significantly, I would say that the financial market turbulence has led me to place more weight on potential downside risks to my forecast.	13	1
201410	1266	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	There are at least two possibilities here.	13	1
201410	1267	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	First, it could be that the financial market movements correctly portend weaker global economic growth, in which case we will all be revising our forecasts downward over time.	13	1
201410	1268	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	But it’s also possible that a global tightening of financial conditions could weaken developed economies enough to cause a slowdown in growth.	13	1
201410	1269	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In either case, I would become more concerned about whether we can reach our employment and inflation goals within the forecast horizon.	13	1
201410	1270	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	As many have noted, because of our limited ability to offset negative shocks when the funds rate is at the zero lower bound, the costs from the downside risks are much greater than those from risks to the upside.	13	1
201410	1271	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	This highlights the advantage of a patient monetary policy, which underlies my current forecast.	13	1
201410	1272	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201410	1289	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	This repricing was driven in part by a very gloomy IMF meeting here in Washington and by weaker-than-expected data from Europe, including a sharp downward revision in German growth prospects.	13	1
201410	1290	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Indeed, in preparation for this meeting my staff looked at the Eurocoin GDP data.	13	1
201410	1291	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Eurocoin is a real-time cyclical indicator for the euro area constructed using 1,000 macroeconomic time series from the major countries of the euro area.	13	1
201410	1292	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	We saw a little bit of it earlier from the staff.	13	1
201410	1293	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Its most recent value is the lowest in a year.	13	1
201410	1294	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	My staff constructed a simple regime switching model to estimate the probability that Europe is in recession based on this data.	13	1
201410	1295	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The main finding is that the estimated probability that Europe is in recession as of September 2014 is about 63 percent.	13	1
201410	1296	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The model fits past European recession data fairly well.	13	1
201410	1297	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	At any point in the past when the recession probability has reached this level, Europe actually was in recession.	13	1
201410	1298	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	While certainly far from definitive, I take this type of result as suggestive of a real risk that Europe had reentered a recession state or will enter into such a state shortly.	13	1
201410	1299	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The Europe-in-recession story seemed to get an extra boost in financial markets when many began to argue that the United States would also suffer from slower-than-expected growth or even outright recession.	13	1
201410	1300	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	This argument was, in my opinion, a bridge too far.	13	1
201410	1301	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The US macroeconomic outlook remains fairly robust.	13	1
201410	1302	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Our tracking estimates for real GDP remain at 3 percent for the second half of 2014, and the St Louis forecast continues to project 3 percent growth in 2015.	13	1
201410	1303	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Labor market data, including revisions to previous months, have been encouraging.	13	1
201410	1304	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Unemployment claims are extraordinarily low, and consumer confidence is at a post-recession high.	13	1
201410	1305	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I expect the unemployment rate to continue to fall in coming jobs reports, moving into the central tendency of the Committee’s estimate of the longer-run normal rate in the first half of next year.	13	1
201410	1306	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	At the current pace, unemployment may be well below 5 percent by this time next year.	13	1
201410	1307	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	In addition to relatively strong US data and a good outlook for 2015, two factors should provide an important tailwind.	13	1

201410	1309	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Lower longer-term rates are normally an important bullish factor for US growth prospects.	13	1
201410	1310	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	In addition, the dramatic fall in oil prices should put additional cash in the pockets of US consumers and cut costs for US producers.	13	1
201410	1311	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	This, too, is a bullish factor for US economic growth.	13	1
201410	1312	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Given these considerations, I have not changed my outlook for the appropriate path of the policy rate.	13	1
201410	1313	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I continue to expect macroeconomic developments, as I have outlined them, to push the Committee toward a somewhat earlier liftoff than commonly assumed.	13	1
201410	1314	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The outlook I have just described is somewhat more optimistic than the marked-down path for GDP described in the Tealbook baseline.	13	1
201410	1315	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	In my view, the current Tealbook baseline overemphasizes possible effects through dollar appreciation.	13	1
201410	1316	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I do not think that we can reliably predict exchange rate movements, at least not to the point at which the Committee can rely on these forecasts for a major part of its policy strategy, and in this respect I agree with President Fisher’s earlier comments.	13	1
201410	1317	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Indeed, the staff has been revamping its dollar forecast models, and we have little experience with the new methodology.	13	1
201410	1318	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Also, I have long regarded the empirical evidence concerning the effects of exchange rate movements on important macroeconomic variable as extraordinarily weak.	13	1
201410	1319	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Thus, even if we could gain some confidence in a particular path for the dollar, the real implications are only estimated with a very large confidence band.	13	1
201410	1320	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	And finally, the changing nature of global production, as hinted at earlier by President Lockhart, has likely altered the interpretation of any empirical evidence we do have.	13	1
201410	1321	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Factory location, in particular, has changed dramatically since the 1980s, a factor that I am not convinced has been appropriately incorporated into the empirical work in this area that I have seen.	13	1
201410	1322	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	This leaves me with a relatively optimistic outlook for the US economy, and this is the same outlook I described in my interview with Bloomberg on October 16.	13	1
201410	1323	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	However, there is a problem with the story as I have it.	13	1
201410	1324	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Presumably, expected inflation should be rising or staying constant in this environment, but some measures of expected inflation are falling.	13	1
201410	1325	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Indeed, the TIPS-based five-year breakeven inflation rate has declined about 60 basis points since the July– August time frame.	13	1
201410	1326	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	In the last 10 days, this measure has stabilized in the 145 to 150 basis point range.	13	1
201410	1327	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The two-year is in the 120 to 125 basis point range.	13	1
201410	1328	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	If we subtract out the difference between CPI and PCE inflation, which my staff puts at 30 to 35 basis points, one could interpret the market as suggesting that PCE inflation will be perhaps 1.1 percent or 1.2 percent over the next five years.	13	1
201410	1329	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I know there are subtleties in this calculation, but this is roughly true, provided investors are close to risk neutral.	13	1
201410	1330	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	This level of expected inflation concerns me because I regard expected inflation as one of the primary determinants of actual inflation and because, in my view, the Committee should be able to attain its inflation target over a period as long as five years.	13	1
201410	1331	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Even an expected inflation rate of 1.1 or 1.2 percent over five years may not be that bad, but the direction is concerning.	13	1
201410	1332	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	These expectations have been falling since the summer.	13	1
201410	1333	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I know longer-term five-year, five-year- forward inflation expectations are more stable, but that’s far in the future.	13	1
201410	1334	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	That’s just a measure, in my mind, of the ultimate credibility of the Committee.	13	1
201410	1335	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	As I was saying earlier, I don’t think those expectations should ever change.	13	1
201410	1336	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Still, I think we should be able to hit our inflation target over a period as long as five years.	13	1
201410	1337	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Undoubtedly, the drop in inflation expectations in the recent data has been wrapped up in the deteriorating global growth outlook.	13	1
201410	1338	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Nevertheless, it’s important that US monetary policy remains nimble enough to react to changing macroeconomic circumstances, if necessary.	13	1
201410	1339	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	This is the source of my suggestion that the Committee could use its state-contingent clause regarding tapering at this time.	13	1
201410	1340	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	After all, we have stated repeatedly that policy is not on a preset path.	13	1
201410	1341	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Unfortunately, I think that despite our best efforts, financial markets do think that policy is on a preset path and that deviations from that path would require such dramatic changes in the incoming data as to be all but impossible.	13	1
201410	1342	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Would recent events meet such a high-bar criterion?	13	1
201410	1343	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	That is, is this a major macroeconomic event?	13	1
201410	1344	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I think that the specter of renewed recession in Europe is an important macroeconomic development.	13	1
201410	1345	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	If this had led to further declines in inflation expectations via continued market turmoil, the Committee might have exercised this state-contingent option at this meeting, possibly with an important effect.	13	1
201410	1346	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	As events have actually unfolded, inflation expectations have stabilized for now, but at an uncomfortably low level.	13	1
201410	1347	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I think that this is sufficient for us to go ahead and complete the tapering process at this meeting.	13	1

201410	1352	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1
201410	1353	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	An all too familiar story may be unfolding.	13	1
201410	1354	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	The economic data on the domestic economy since our latest meeting have been mostly in line with our relatively optimistic forecast, but at the same time we have seen a notable increase in pessimism and nervousness about the economic outlook for the rest of the world.	13	1
201410	1355	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	These global worries undoubtedly impart greater risk to the outlook for the US economy, but it’s still unclear how much weakness to take on board in our baseline forecast.	13	1
201410	1356	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	If this was our first experience with this storyline, I’d say it’s too early to express substantial concern.	13	1
201410	1357	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	But we’ve seen this movie before.	13	1
201410	1358	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	When it comes to communicating an upbeat outlook that is later crushed by reality, we have already crossed the “three strikes” threshold, so I’m nervous.	13	1
201410	1359	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Let me turn to specifics.	13	1
201410	1360	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	As most of us expected, the initial release of weaker August job numbers was an aberration.	13	1
201410	1361	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Data through September, including revisions, indicate that employment growth remains robust.	13	1
201410	1362	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Consumer spending appears to have been a little on the soft side this summer but not by enough to change the outlook by itself.	13	1
201410	1363	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	After all, the improved job market should support stronger consumption.	13	1
201410	1364	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Moreover, the consumer should get a little boost from the fall in energy prices.	13	1
201410	1365	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Meanwhile, even with today’s numbers, business order books continue to be solid, which should support decent investment spending, at least over the near term.	13	1
201410	1366	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	We still see the labor and spending indicators as being in line with our relatively upbeat projection from September that real GDP growth will run at about a 3 percent pace over the next 18 months or so.	13	1
201410	1367	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	This relatively optimistic assessment continues to be consistent with what I heard from my directors and other business contacts.	13	1
201410	1368	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Bankers are reporting strong loan growth.	13	1
201410	1369	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Almost all of my nonfinancial contacts reported solid third-quarter results and a healthy outlook for their domestic business lines.	13	1
201410	1370	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	The agricultural equipment business is an exception.	13	1
201410	1371	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	One large manufacturer is in the midst of laying off 20 percent of his production workforce, both in the United States and worldwide.	13	1
201410	1372	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Much of the story is that this year’s big harvest is depressing crop prices and farm income, which will restrain sales of farm equipment.	13	1
201410	1373	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	This is good news that becomes bad news for that sector.	13	1
201410	1374	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	However, as I said, this market is a bit of an outlier with the reports about recent activity for most other sectors being relatively upbeat.	13	1
201410	1375	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	But these anecdotes, like the incoming data, are largely backward looking.	13	1
201410	1376	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Since our latest meeting, we have also seen a deterioration in the outlook for the rest of the world, an appreciation of the dollar, and increased volatility in financial markets.	13	1
201410	1377	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	That is quite some list.	13	1
201410	1378	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Risks have increased that worldwide events may lead to greater caution on the part of large US multinational corporations.	13	1
201410	1379	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Indeed, the reports I got about the rest of the world became quite a bit darker this time.	13	1
201410	1380	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	No one had anything upbeat to say about economic growth in China or emerging market economies.	13	1
201410	1381	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Europe is a mess.	13	1
201410	1382	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	As President Bullard indicated, there is a 63 percent chance that they are in a recession.	13	1
201410	1383	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	One construction equipment manufacturing CEO that I spoke with said that at a recent sales meeting his previously optimistic European distributors now all look like deer caught in the headlights.	13	1
201410	1384	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	The only optimism I heard was at a recent breakfast meeting with a German policymaker who expressed strong confidence in the outlook for the German economy and pointed to continuing improvements elsewhere around the euro zone.	13	1
201410	1385	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	He didn’t seem too concerned about current low euro-zone inflation, and he seemed to think that every single European country either was or was on the verge of running a current account surplus.	13	1
201410	1386	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I can’t say I know he’s wrong, but this seems worrisome.	13	1
201410	1387	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Another indicator of weak global demand is the strong downward cost pressure I’m hearing about from manufacturers.	13	1
201410	1388	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	The demand for commodities has declined, and my contacts were pretty much unanimous in reporting substantially lower material costs for this year and next.	13	1
201410	1389	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Meanwhile, labor cost pressures remain subdued.	13	1
201410	1390	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	The lack of reported price pressures is consistent with the results from a suite of inflation models we run.	13	1
201410	1391	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Forecasts from both our economic indicator models and those that use the term structure of interest rates point to inflation remaining roughly flat, near 1½ percent.	13	1
201410	1392	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Although we’ve nudged down our near-term forecast some, we continue to override the model’s implications, and we expect better.	13	1
201410	1393	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Like the Tealbook, we project core PCE inflation rising to 1.8 percent by 2017, but this is hardly a victory.	13	1
201410	1394	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	It is three years from now, and we are still below target.	13	1
201410	1395	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	To get there, my assumption for appropriately realistic policy doesn’t start to tighten the funds rate until 2016.	13	1
201410	1396	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	That’s a good deal later than in the Tealbook.	13	1
201410	1397	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	To sum up, as I mentioned at the outset, the incoming data to date, all backward looking, provide good support for solid economic growth over the next 18 months.	13	1
201410	1398	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	But to get there, either the global risks will have to diminish or the US economy will have to strongly decouple from a very weak global economy.	13	1
201410	1399	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I can’t say these assessments are wrong.	13	1
201410	1400	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I have that decoupling in the contour of my baseline projection.	13	1
201410	1401	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	But my takeaway from recent history is either one of the following scenarios:  One, we have been wrong before, and are we ever due for a run of better luck.	13	1
201410	1402	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Or, two, we might consider fastening our seatbelts and convey a bit less complacency in our public projections of economic growth and perhaps be more explicit in warning of the increased likelihood that we will undershoot our inflation objective for another three years.	13	1

201410	1431	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Sorry, Jay.	13	1

201410	1433	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Importantly, on a serious note, the risks that I do see to the US economy have shifted predominantly outside of our borders, as many of us have already discussed.	13	1
201410	1434	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	It is really about the external sector, and the global recovery is in some danger of stalling—Europe, Japan, and China—to say nothing of geopolitical risks from outbreaks of war and disease.	13	1

201410	1436	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Fundamentally, when it comes to real trade flows, the US economy still acts more or less like a closed economy, and the appreciation of the dollar and the slowing demand from abroad will cut into our net exports a bit but won’t derail the recovery.	13	1
201410	1437	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	It’s important to remember, as the staff mentioned, that this negative effect will be at least partially offset by the improved domestic demand from the collapse in oil prices that we have seen.	13	1
201410	1438	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In contrast with the solid domestic growth outlook, the near-term inflation outlook is somewhat more worrisome.	13	1
201410	1439	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In particular, a variety of external factors are lining up together to grind down US prices.	13	1
201410	1440	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Cheaper imports stemming from the stronger dollar, slack abroad, and falling commodity prices will all exert disinflationary pressures at least through next year.	13	1
201410	1441	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	A lot of countries, like Japan and those in the euro area, seem likely to be exporting low inflation for quite some time.	13	1
201410	1442	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	With inflation already running below our target, this situation warrants close attention, particularly if it were to spill over into longer-run inflation expectations and ultimately affect the perceived nominal anchor.	13	1
201410	1443	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	For now, however, I remain cautiously optimistic, especially about the anchoring of inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1444	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Inflation expectations do appear to be well anchored in two dimensions.	13	1
201410	1445	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	First, the perceived inflation target is anchored in the right place, and that’s at 2 percent.	13	1
201410	1446	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Second, the anchor still has significant attraction and holding power for inflation.	13	1
201410	1447	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Regarding the first point, as I mentioned numerous times at our past few meetings, I am unpersuaded that inflation expectations are currently anchored below the 2 percent target as assumed by the Tealbook.	13	1
201410	1448	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	The Tealbook view is, in part, based on an estimated constant in a Phillips-curve regression, and these estimates can be sensitive to model specification and the period of the sample.	13	1
201410	1449	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	My staff generated a range of model-based estimates of long-run inflation expectations, similar to the analysis conducted by the Board staff.	13	1
201410	1450	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In this analysis, it turns out that the key determinant of measured long-run inflation expectations is the regression sample.	13	1
201410	1451	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In particular, if you look at the past 15 years, a period during which surveyed inflation expectations have been well anchored, that implies that longer-run inflation expectations are more or less overlapping with our 2 percent target.	13	1
201410	1452	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, you might ask, why focus on the past 15 years?	13	1
201410	1453	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	That’s a relatively short sample.	13	1
201410	1454	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	That’s because there’s a well-documented shift in inflation expectations that took place back in the 1990s.	13	1
201410	1455	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Before then, we were still in the process of gaining credibility.	13	1
201410	1456	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	As a result, inflation expectations were consistently above realized inflation.	13	1
201410	1457	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	There was a sustained gap between the two.	13	1
201410	1458	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Over time, as we built our credibility and it firmed, inflation expectations have moved closer to realized inflation.	13	1
201410	1459	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	This enhanced credibility is evident in rolling Phillips-curve regressions over various subsamples, and they show that earlier samples actually had the estimated longer-run inflation expectations being about 1½ percent, but now show that to be closer to 2 percent.	13	1
201410	1460	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, I agree with President Kocherlakota that we don’t want to just assume that longer- run inflation expectations are fixed, and we must carefully monitor various survey- and market- based measures of these expectations.	13	1
201410	1461	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	So far, however, the declines in the various measures that we have seen are within the historical range, albeit at the low end that we have seen.	13	1
201410	1462	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In looking at these models, I do want to say—and I think President Kocherlakota made a really important point about thinking about risk premiums—I think they do distinguish between a risk premium and an inflation premium and a liquidity premium.	13	1
201410	1463	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	If a liquidity premium is just a result of market functioning, you wouldn’t want to take that as a serious sign of a shift in economic conditions.	13	1
201410	1464	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	On the inflation risk premium, I think the evidence that we have so far suggests some of it may be coming down to a reduction in the risk of high inflation.	13	1
201410	1465	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, I agree with your point that we want to take this seriously and study it carefully.	13	1
201410	1466	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	But so far I, at least, am not as concerned.	13	1
201410	1467	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I guess I agree with some other comments about the decline we have seen so far in inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1468	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	The one caveat in interpreting the survey-based measures is that they are often overly influenced by the latest inflation data.	13	1
201410	1469	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	For this reason, I wouldn’t be surprised if survey measures fall further in the coming months because the price of oil prices is falling and energy prices are falling.	13	1
201410	1470	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	My staff at the San Francisco Fed has found that longer-run survey expectations, particularly from household surveys, can be excessively sensitive to changes in energy prices.	13	1
201410	1471	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	This was especially true back in 2008, for example, when the jump in oil prices pushed up survey measures of long-run inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1472	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	You actually see this in the SPF, too.	13	1
201410	1473	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think it’s a little warning not to necessarily take any movement one-tenth or two-tenths one way or the other in the SPF or any of these other surveys as literally a loss of credibility.	13	1
201410	1474	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	There just seems to be some excessive sensitivity in there that we have seen even in the past 15 years.	13	1
201410	1475	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Importantly, after the jump in oil prices, you saw a jump in survey responses regarding views of longer-run inflation expectations; once those energy prices stabilized, that bulge in longer-run inflation expectations disappeared.	13	1
201410	1476	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	They went back to where they were once the oil price stopped moving around.	13	1
201410	1477	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	We may see the converse of this situation in the months ahead, with the drop in energy prices pushing down survey measures for a while.	13	1
201410	1478	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	But then, once the energy prices flatten out, these dips in longer-run inflation expectations will likely be temporary.	13	1
201410	1479	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, I’m not trying to downplay the role of inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1480	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I, too, think it’s critically important.	13	1
201410	1481	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think we want to monitor it carefully, and we also have to be aware that those measures do move around a little bit due to transitory factors.	13	1

201410	1515	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Now, having said we are not energy concentrated, I do want to talk about energy, and the reason for that is because even though it’s only 2.6 percent of our employment, including support services, it is about 12 percent of the output of our District—I do have 990 wells in my District out of the 1,900 that operate in the country.	13	1
201410	1516	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I pretend to know something about business, and I’d like to share that with you.	13	1
201410	1517	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I think it’s very important to understand that when you think about the effect of lower energy prices domestically, it has a different effect on different sectors of the energy sector.	13	1
201410	1518	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	For example, horizontal wells, which are the hot new thing, typically have a very big burst of production the first year or two, and then they have rapid declines from that point onward.	13	1
201410	1519	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Whereas the vertical wells tend to produce over a much longer period.	13	1
201410	1520	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I want to point to the example of the Haynesville Shale in Louisiana, where when US natural gas prices began to crater in 2011, drillers just moved out of the area, and production is now 35 percent lower than it was at its peak level in 2011.	13	1
201410	1521	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	That said, it may not be as damaging to our domestic production as we think.	13	1
201410	1522	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	There are offsets, and there are silver linings.	13	1
201410	1523	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	For example, as I have mentioned at many, many meetings here, a Beige Book retail contact noted that you just cannot find mechanics or technicians or truck drivers or welders or pipefitters in areas of the state in which the energy sector was booming.	13	1

201410	1525	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Indeed, if you go through the cycle of those wells and these prices maintain, you might be able to have some release on some of the wage price pressures that we’ve seen.	13	1

201410	1664	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Financial markets have been volatile, but I’m not taking too much signal from that yet.	13	1
201410	1665	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	I have not marked my forecast down as much as the Tealbook in response to the stronger dollar and recent variability in other financial market conditions.	13	1
201410	1666	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	The weakness in the European economy and slowdown in China are not new information.	13	1
201410	1667	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	I had already incorporated much of that into my forecast.	13	1
201410	1668	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Still, the chance these economies may be weaker than expected has increased the downside risk to my forecast.	13	1
201410	1669	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Lower oil and commodity prices will temporarily lower headline inflation over the near term, but as these prices stabilize, I expect inflation to move back up and to continue gradually moving toward our goal.	13	1
201410	1670	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Most models suggest that monetary policy shouldn’t respond to these relative-price shocks.	13	1
201410	1671	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	My forecast that inflation will gradually return to our goal reflects anchored inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1672	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	The Cleveland Fed’s 10-year CPI inflation expectations measure and survey-based measures of medium- to longer-run inflation expectations remain quite stable near 2 percent.	13	1
201410	1673	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Measures of inflation expectations based on asset prices suggest some decline, but I’m wary of reading too much into these measures because during periods of heightened volatility like we’ve seen, flight-to-quality flows into Treasury securities affect the risk premiums on those assets, making it harder to draw a conclusion about inflation expectations from market prices.	13	1
201410	1674	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Nothing over the intermeeting period has changed my view that we’ve made significant progress in labor markets since the start of the asset purchase program in September of 2012, which was set as one of the important conditions for ending the program.	13	1
201410	1675	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Recent research by Cleveland Fed staff suggests that the degree of underutilization of labor resources has been significantly reduced.	13	1
201410	1676	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Our research has estimated the so-called longer-run, normal level of unemployment using five different conceptual approaches.	13	1
201410	1677	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Most of the approaches were more statistical in nature.	13	1
201410	1678	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	One was consistent with the concept from a New Keynesian sticky-price model.	13	1
201410	1679	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Over the past few years, the estimates of underutilization varied quite a bit depending on the concept being used.	13	1
201410	1680	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	However, all of the estimates indicate that underutilization has declined, and they all suggest relatively little underutilization remains today.	13	1
201410	1681	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Of course, these estimates are subject to considerable uncertainty, and they’re based on the unemployment rate rather than on broader measures of labor market activity, but even these broader measures, as summarized in labor market condition indexes, show improvement.	13	1
201410	1682	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	In thinking about the implications of the broader index of labor market conditions for policy, I took advantage of the fact that one of the creators of the Board’s index is now a Cleveland Fed economist and asked him to examine what a Taylor-type rule would look like if instead of using the unemployment rate we used the broader conditions index.	13	1
201410	1683	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	This turned out to be a more complicated exercise than I had anticipated because the conditions index is constructed to indicate a change in conditions rather than a level of activity.	13	1
201410	1684	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	One way to get around this issue is to focus on monetary policy difference rules.	13	1
201410	1685	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	What we find is that currently a policy rule based on the conditions index and a policy rule based on the unemployment rate would yield pretty similar levels of the federal funds rate and point to a federal funds rate slightly above the current level.	13	1
201410	1686	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Now, this is work in progress, but so far the results support the view that judged by either the unemployment rate or the broader labor market conditions index we are getting nearer the liftoff.	13	1
201410	1687	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	13	1

201410	1797	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In December of 2013, when we initiated the taper, the FOMC statement made reference to watching for evidence that inflation was moving back to target over the medium term.	13	1
201410	1798	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the first part of this year, there were such signs, as inflation rose more rapidly than many forecasters had expected.	13	1
201410	1799	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	These signs have proven to be transitory.	13	1
201410	1800	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	At this point, the medium-term inflation outlook is no better than it was last December.	13	1
201410	1801	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Indeed, in December 2013, the Tealbook projected that inflation would be back to target by 2018.	13	1
201410	1802	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Tealbook now projects that inflation will remain below target until early in the next decade.	13	1
201410	1803	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This more subdued inflation outlook comes even though the Tealbook’s outlook for monetary policy is considerably more accommodative than it was a couple of months ago.	13	1
201410	1804	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We have a 2 percent inflation target, and that target is like any other goal.	13	1
201410	1805	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Its credibility relies on our consistently taking clear actions to push inflation back toward that target.	13	1
201410	1806	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am concerned that failing to react to the ongoing subdued inflation outlook has begun to create significant downside risks to the credibility of that target.	13	1
201410	1807	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We can see that downside risk reflected in the behavior of longer-term market-based inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1808	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As of last week, the five-year, five-year forward inflation breakevens—measured by spreads between TIPS and nominal Treasuries—fell to under 2.2 percent.	13	1
201410	1809	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It is very low by historical standards, lower than all but 1 percent of the daily observations in the previous 10 years.	13	1
201410	1810	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, as many have noted, the potential variation over time and the relative liquidity demand for TIPS and nominal Treasuries sort of reflect quality issues in the Treasury market.	13	1
201410	1811	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It means we should interpret these data with care, and it’s useful to supplement this observation about Treasury inflation breakevens by looking at the recent behavior of five-year, five-year forward inflation expectations embedded in zero coupon inflation swaps.	13	1
201410	1812	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The current reading on that measure is also unusually low, lower than all but 3 percent of the daily observations of the previous 10 years.	13	1
201410	1813	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I focused on market-based measures of inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1814	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As many of you have noted, survey-based measures of inflation expectations have been considerably more stable, but I do not think we should be overly sanguine about this stability.	13	1
201410	1815	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As a January 2014 memo on the staff inflation outlook described, survey-based measures of inflation expectations remained surprisingly stable in Japan, even as the credibility of that central bank eroded.	13	1
201410	1816	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To sum up, Madam Chair, the inflation outlook remains subdued.	13	1
201410	1817	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I see little evidence that inflation is, indeed, trending upward over the medium term.	13	1
201410	1818	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am concerned that our failure to respond to the subdued inflation outlook is creating a substantial downside risk to the credibility of our inflation target.	13	1
201410	1819	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Consistent with this concern, market-based measures of longer-term inflation expectations are unusually low by historical standards.	13	1
201410	1820	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you.	13	1

201410	1827	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Financial conditions remain very accommodative.	13	1
201410	1828	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Banks are well capitalized and tending to ease lending standards.	13	1
201410	1829	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Moreover, fuel for continued gains in consumer spending is evident in solid job gains and lower energy prices—lower energy prices that are likely to boost the growth rate of real income.	13	1
201410	1830	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Moreover, we have a saving rate that still seems relatively high compared with the underlying trend in net worth to income.	13	1
201410	1831	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	A growth trajectory of just short of 3 percent still seems the most likely outcome.	13	1
201410	1832	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In particular, I’d be very hesitant to put too much weight on recent financial market developments.	13	1
201410	1833	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Yes, financial market conditions are slightly tighter than where we were the previous FOMC meeting, but they’re still very accommodative, and what we’ve seen could reverse quickly, and, in fact, already has reversed to a significant degree.	13	1
201410	1834	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to the labor market side of our mandate, I want to just offer a couple of brief thoughts.	13	1
201410	1835	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, some have argued that the large increase in job vacancy rates that we’ve seen, which are above and beyond what one would expect given the unemployment rate, indicates a significant tightening of the labor market and a potential precursor of faster wage growth.	13	1
201410	1836	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	That was brought up by President George and was part of the weekly briefing at the Board this week.	13	1
201410	1837	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I think that’s certainly a possible explanation, but I think there is an alternative explanation worth considering.	13	1
201410	1838	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The end of the extended unemployment compensation benefits at the end of last year essentially led to a significant expansion in the effective supply of labor, as people basically had to start really looking for work.	13	1
201410	1839	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	This meant that the ability to hire someone at a given wage increased, as there was a larger effective pool of potential employees available.	13	1
201410	1840	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Put differently, firms had an incentive to post more job openings because the prospect of actually making a match and bringing someone on board increased.	13	1
201410	1841	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	What did we see?	13	1
201410	1842	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	We saw payrolls growing rapidly relative to the underlying growth base.	13	1
201410	1843	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	It sort of fits what we actually saw in terms of the economic data.	13	1
201410	1844	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In other words, some of the increase in job vacancies reflects an increase in demand responding to the increase in effective supply.	13	1
201410	1845	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	It would not have happened to the same degree if extended unemployment compensation benefits had not been ended.	13	1
201410	1846	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	This alternative explanation, and the fact that compensation trends haven’t accelerated, makes me less concerned that the decline in job vacancy rates is a sign of tightness in the labor market.	13	1
201410	1847	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	On the inflation side, I think we need to carefully distinguish between the fall in actual inflation and developments in terms of inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1848	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Overall inflation has fallen and will fall considerably more next month, reflecting the recent sharp decline in gasoline prices, but it strikes me this is mostly a positive for the outlook, assuming that oil prices stabilize at or above $70 to $80 per barrel, as the drop in energy prices will boost real income and the effect on overall inflation will likely be transitory.	13	1
201410	1849	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In contrast, I would put somewhat more weight on the decline in market-based measures of inflation compensation.	13	1
201410	1850	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	However, even here there are few signs that what’s going on in the TIPS market is feeding through into survey-based measures of inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1851	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In fact, an analysis by our research economists in New York suggests that most of the decline in forward TIPS-based breakevens that is beyond the next year or two is due to a decline in the inflation risk premium, in other words, what investors are willing to pay for inflation protection rather than reflecting an actual decline in expected inflation.	13	1
201410	1852	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Finally, although I said it before, I think it bears repeating.	13	1
201410	1853	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The dangers of too-low inflation are considerably less when the economy is growing and nominal incomes are rising at a decent rate.	13	1
201410	1854	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The risk of the United States getting locked into a debt–deflation dynamic seems very low to me.	13	1
201410	1855	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In contrast, in Europe the risks are considerably higher—lower actual inflation, much slower nominal income growth, very high debt burdens, very little deleveraging having actually taken place, and a greater decline in inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	1856	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	If I was going to worry about it, I would be much more worried about it with respect to Europe than the United States.	13	1
201410	1857	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, the European outlook obviously was important in provoking the risk-off trade we saw a few weeks ago, but even here I think it’s important to highlight that it isn’t all negative.	13	1
201410	1858	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	On the positive side of the ledger for Europe, the impulse toward fiscal contraction does seem to be fading.	13	1
201410	1859	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In addition, although we didn’t discuss it, I think the early read on the asset quality review and the supervisory stress test seems, at worst, neutral and possibly even favorable because the exercises, I think, are viewed as mostly credible, and the fact is that the net capital need for the banking system appears very manageable.	13	1
201410	1860	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	One more broad question, in terms of risks to the outlook, it seems like we’re going through a pretty significant regime shift in terms of what’s happening to commodity prices and what’s happening to terms of trade around the world—a regime shift that’s the first major change in this for many, many years, and I’d like to highlight it and encourage the Board staff to maybe look into this a little bit.	13	1
201410	1861	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	It strikes me that there’s going to be quite a bit of collateral damage associated with this, especially to some emerging market economies.	13	1
201410	1862	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I think it would be very interesting to just sort of do a deeper dive into this issue to sort of see what kind of things could actually happen in terms of bad macroeconomic performance, but also financial-stability consequences, corporate failures, et cetera, because I think this shift in commodity prices is pretty noteworthy.	13	1
201410	1863	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	My own story about what’s happening is basically that we had this huge impetus to commodity demand as China was rapidly urbanizing, and commodity supply took a long time to catch up.	13	1
201410	1864	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	But commodity supply has finally caught up with demand, and so we’re actually seeing pretty much a sea change in terms of the sustainable level of commodity prices.	13	1
201410	1865	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we’re just seeing the very early signs of what this means, and I’d like to delve into this a little deeper because I don’t really understand what the implications are, and I think the implications potentially could be pretty significant for the global economic outlook.	13	1
201410	1866	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you.	13	1
201410	1867	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	13	1

201410	1882	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	More generally, and finally, I’d like to ask about how we should think of the implications of the recent market turbulence, which, if this meeting had taken place a week ago, we’d all be talking about and worrying about.	13	1
201410	1883	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	On the exchange rate, I’m not sure where in the whole set-up this comes in, but I think the exchange rate has been a sign that those countries that we’re worried about who had weak economies actually have a factor going in their favor.	13	1
201410	1884	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	I just gave a lecture a few weeks ago in which I explained that when we cut our interest rates and/or engage in QE, on balance, we’re doing good for foreign economies because the output effect is quite large and typically outweighs the substitution effect of the exchange rate.	13	1
201410	1885	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	In some countries the exchange rate is declining because of expansionary monetary policy, and that means they’re acting in a way that will cure some of the effect on us of the foreign growth decline that we’re worried about very much.	13	1
201410	1886	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	Secondly, I think that in Europe the big fear at the IMF meetings was based on the decline in German output of automobiles in September, and all of a sudden if you look at the numbers, that’s sort of mostly disappeared, and it looks like a one-time shot.	13	1
201410	1887	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	And China, we were all very worried until we got a number that essentially was close to 7½ percent, and now we’re all feeling much better.	13	1

201410	1889	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	On the implications of market turbulence, I just want to talk about it.	13	1

201410	1901	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	I think if we look at the capital markets, the reason we don’t want to have a Fed put is that we rely on the capital markets, particularly the equity markets, to also send price signals.	13	1
201410	1902	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	If every time a signal is appearing we suddenly go in and wipe it out, in a way that doesn’t change the underlying realities—and maybe it could change the underlying realities—then we stop the capital markets working as they should.	13	1

201410	1906	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	We more or less agree with the path of market interest rates, and that gives a nice impression that as we move along that path it will all be a nice, smooth thing, and everybody will be very happy because we are just going down this gradually rising path.	13	1

201410	2138	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	On the question of whether lower energy prices and the higher dollar will leave an imprint on inflation beyond the next couple of quarters, however, I heard mixed views.	13	1
201410	2139	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	A number of you argued that inflation will move back to 2 percent over time, in an environment of continued reductions in resource slack and well-anchored expectations, but a number of you noted worrisome downside risks.	13	1
201410	2140	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, there is the question of just how well anchored inflation expectations really are.	13	1
201410	2141	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Many of you noted that measures of longer-term inflation expectations are challenging to assess at this time.	13	1
201410	2142	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Survey-based measures, including the latest reading from the dealer survey, have remained stable, but both five-year and five-year, five-year- forward breakevens have declined noticeably since our September meeting.	13	1
201410	2143	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	As President Bullard and others noted, this is a concerning development.	13	1
201410	2144	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	However, a large share of the decline in breakevens could be attributable to factors other than a reduction in longer-term inflation expectations, such as a decline in the inflation risk premium, perhaps partly reflecting lower probabilities of high-inflation outcomes, the appreciation of the dollar, and liquidity effects.	13	1
201410	2145	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Even in survey-based measures, we may see some movements in the near term.	13	1
201410	2146	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	As President Williams noted, we’ve often seen in survey measures a relatively short-lived overreaction of longer-term expectations to events that should produce only a transitory increase in inflation, particularly an increase in oil prices.	13	1
201410	2147	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thus, we should be aware that survey measures of longer-term inflation expectations could decline in coming months, but that such effects could well prove transitory.	13	1
201410	2148	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	In all, while most of you see these recent developments as largely transitory, and thus continue to expect that inflation will move gradually back toward 2 percent, some of you are concerned that we may be seeing the beginning of a worrisome downward adjustment in inflation expectations.	13	1
201410	2149	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	As President Kocherlakota emphasized, a failure on our part to take decisive action could exacerbate this risk by diminishing the credibility of our commitment to our 2 percent inflation objective.	13	1
201410	2150	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Inflation developments will certainly bear close watching.	13	1
201410	2151	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	With regard to risks to the outlook, almost all of you discussed risks pertaining to the global outlook.	13	1
201410	2152	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Markets have been quite focused on foreign developments, and economic news from abroad since the September meeting has, on balance, been less reassuring.	13	1
201410	2153	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Many of you mentioned downside risks from China and Europe.	13	1
201410	2154	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Because the euro area is at the zero lower bound and fiscal policy options are limited, the risks to economic growth and inflation seem asymmetric and weighted to the downside.	13	1
201410	2155	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	In terms of the spillovers to the United States, some of you noted that the United States is still a relatively closed economy, and thus the risks to the US outlook are not outsized.	13	1
201410	2156	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	However, several of you worried that with the United States also operating at the zero lower bound, it would be difficult to respond to weakness in the US economic growth or inflation outlook if there was a more significant downgrade in the foreign outlook.	13	1
201410	2157	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	A number of you also commented on the recent spell of financial market volatility.	13	1
201410	2158	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	You noted that because many of us at past meetings have expressed concerns about signs of complacency in some market segments, some increase in volatility could arguably be a healthy development from a financial-stability standpoint, and several of you noted that we’re likely to see further episodes of volatility as normalization approaches.	13	1
201410	2159	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	While movements in financial markets that significantly threaten the economic outlook could certainly require some response, many of you cautioned that we should take market movements like those we recently saw in stride.	13	1
201410	2160	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Let me stop there and see if anybody would like to comment on this summary.	13	1

201410	2163	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	As I mentioned at the beginning of my remarks, I think we’ve reached the point at which we can declare that there’s been a substantial improvement in the outlook for the labor market since the inception of our asset purchase program, and I think it’s also important that we acknowledge the recent progress that we have seen in labor market conditions.	13	1
201410	2164	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Alternative B proposes to do that by eliminating the reference to “significant” slack.	13	1
201410	2165	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	I support that change, but I would note that in my assessment appreciable slack still remains in the labor market, so we do have some way to go before reaching our goal of maximum employment.	13	1
201410	2166	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	On inflation, the recent declines in oil and other commodity prices, along with the effects of the dollar appreciation on prices of other imported goods and services, will surely hold down inflation in the near term.	13	1
201410	2167	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	My own medium-term inflation outlook, however, is little changed, and I continue to believe that the risks of inflation running persistently below 2 percent have diminished since earlier in the year.	13	1
201410	2168	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	In our December 2013 SEP, the central tendency for four-quarter PCE inflation in 2014 was 1.4 to 1.6 percent.	13	1
201410	2169	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	This projection appears to be right on the mark, but our central tendency for the unemployment rate in the current quarter was 6.3 to 6.6 percent.	13	1
201410	2170	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Given that we’ve revised down our estimate of the longer-run normal rate since December by only a small amount, we seem to be on the path of measurably tighter resource utilization than we expected at the beginning of this year, which, in my view, diminishes the downside risk to inflation.	13	1
201410	2171	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	The shift down in TIPS inflation compensation was nontrivial, and if longer-term inflation expectations were to shift down, this would clearly be a concern.	13	1

201410	2173	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Indeed, the dealers were about evenly split on the question of whether the decline mostly reflects inflation expectations or other factors.	13	1
201410	2174	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Clearly, we must pay very close attention to this issue as we go forward, but at this point, like many of you, I think we should be cautious about reading too much into the recent market moves.	13	1
201410	2175	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Finally, despite the recent flare-up in financial market volatility, I view financial conditions as remaining highly accommodative.	13	1
201410	2176	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	On approach to liftoff, we are very likely to encounter further pockets of turbulence, and I think we should set a high bar before we decide to lean against such developments.	13	1

201410	2263	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201410	2264	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	A couple of general comments before I go into my prepared remarks.	23	2
201410	2265	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Actually, I have a third comment, which is that I’m surprised President Williams didn’t downgrade his forecast in light of events last night.	23	2
201410	2266	2014-10-29	meeting		[Laughter]	23	2
201410	2267	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But a quick comment on inflation breakevens and compensation.	23	2
201410	2268	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	You can think about dividing inflation breakevens and compensation, as President Williams pointed out yesterday, into three components—expected inflation, risk premiums, and liquidity premiums.	23	2
201410	2269	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think it’s very important for us to strip out liquidity premiums as best we can.	23	2
201410	2270	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Those are due to market function issues that we do want to get rid of.	23	2
201410	2271	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That’s why I think it’s useful to supplement what is going on in the Treasury market with what’s happening in zero-coupon inflation swaps as a market-based measure of expected inflation.	23	2
201410	2272	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But I want to reiterate a point I made yesterday, which is that I would counsel against stripping out risk premiums.	23	2
201410	2273	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Risk premiums are telling you about the co-movement of what is happening with inflation and what is happening with anticipated economic growth, and, basically, how scary things are going to be when inflation is low.	23	2
201410	2274	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	When we see the market-based measure of expected inflation go down, even though our statistical models are forecasting inflation remaining the same, that’s telling us that when growth is going to be low and times are going to be bad, inflation is more likely to be low.	23	2
201410	2275	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As Bill English pointed out yesterday, some of this is just due to people putting less weight on the outcome of high inflation with low economic growth in bad times.	23	2
201410	2276	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But that’s still telling us that low inflation is going to be viewed as more of a problem because it’s going to be taking place with low growth.	23	2
201410	2277	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If an event like low inflation is taking place with low growth, that’s what we should be putting more weight on.	23	2
201410	2278	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think we want to be including risk premiums, not stripping them out.	23	2
201410	2279	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The other comment I will quickly make is that I was very struck by Governor Fischer’s comment on thinking about liftoff as but one component of interest rate policy.	23	2
201410	2280	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I agree with him.	23	2
201410	2281	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We need to be thinking through liftoff to the meetings beyond.	23	2
201410	2282	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The markets, and the public will want us to be thinking about this as a sequence of interest rate moves, but it’s important for us not to get into that.	23	2
201410	2283	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think it’s very important for us to be thinking about this as a strategy of how we’re adjusting interest rates to the data, especially in terms of downside risks.	23	2
201410	2284	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Because we remain close to the zero lower bound, we’re going to have to be very sensitive to the timing of interest rate moves in response to downside shocks.	23	2
201410	2285	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	With that as prelude, Madam Chair, at this meeting I favor alternative A.	23	2
201410	2286	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	At the launch of the taper in December, the FOMC statement said that the Committee would be monitoring inflation developments carefully for evidence that inflation moved back toward its objective over the medium term.	23	2
201410	2287	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I see no such evidence.	23	2
201410	2288	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As I described in the earlier go-round, the medium- term outlook for inflation shows no signs of improvement since last December and is, indeed, arguably worse.	23	2
201410	2289	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The outlook has deteriorated especially markedly since July, and the staff now projects that inflation will not return to target until the next decade.	23	2
201410	2290	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Failing to act in response to this ongoing subdued inflation outlook creates a downside risk to the credibility of our inflation target.	23	2
201410	2291	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In my view, we see that downside risk reflected in the recent fall of market-based measures of longer-term inflation expectations to unusually low levels by historical standards.	23	2
201410	2292	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Madam Chair, under your leadership and that of your predecessor, this Committee has made an explicit commitment to a 2 percent inflation target, but we cannot take the credibility of that commitment for granted.	23	2
201410	2293	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As we have seen in Europe, as we have seen in Japan, the credibility of central banks depends on their taking actions on an ongoing basis to ensure that inflation does indeed stay at 2 percent.	23	2
201410	2294	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In my view, the evolution of the data over the past few months means that we need to take such actions today.	23	2
201410	2295	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To summarize, in light of the continued sluggishness in the inflation outlook and the recent slide in market-based measures of longer-term inflation expectations, I support alternative A.	23	2
201410	2296	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In particular, I believe that the Committee should commit to keeping the federal funds rate target range at its current level, at least until the one- to two-year-ahead inflation outlook has returned to 2 percent, and that the Committee should continue the asset purchase program at its current level.	23	2
201410	2297	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201410	2298	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2
201410	2299	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	23	2

201410	2301	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I support alternative B as written.	23	2
201410	2302	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The primary focus of the bond purchase program was to achieve substantial improvement in labor markets.	23	2
201410	2303	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	With the unemployment rate at 5.9 percent and the strong payroll employment growth over the past several quarters, labor markets are substantially improved relative to when we began the purchase program.	23	2

201410	2307	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The low current inflation rate and the disinflationary pressures we are currently experiencing indicate we may not make much progress toward our inflation goal in the near term, which is certainly consistent with the Tealbook forecast.	23	2
201410	2308	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	With inflation expected to remain below our target for some time, we are provided an opportunity to probe how tight labor markets need to be for us to achieve our inflation target in a reasonable time period.	23	2

201410	2322	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	But I think we don’t wish to look like nervous Nellies because we have seen some long-overdue volatility or because of a market correction, which I have, as you know, repeatedly warned as a distinct possibility.	23	2

201410	2325	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Paragraph 4 includes what I consider still to be the objectionable calendar guidance “considerable time” phrase that has been pointed out by Bill English and others.	23	2

201410	2329	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I have used in speeches, and I think in this room, an analogy to duck hunting.	23	2
201410	2330	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	That is, you want to lead your mallard rather than aim right at it when you shoot.	23	2
201410	2331	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Otherwise, you’re not going to bag it.	23	2
201410	2332	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I worry that if we stick with the last sentence, as written, it could result in our overshooting, and then be followed by a tightening ex post that in every instance I know about historically has resulted in recession.	23	2
201410	2333	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	This is the conclusion of the Economic Letter that Evan Koenig—as the staff would say, exhibit 1, seated behind me—and I wrote recently.	23	2
