201410	2336	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Let me add just one last comment.	23	2
201410	2337	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I am very skeptical about the Tealbook policy simulations.	23	2
201410	2338	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Built into the inflation forecast is the assumption that long-term expectations are anchored at 1¾ percent, which holds down the trajectory of inflation over the next couple of years by approximately ¼ percentage point.	23	2
201410	2339	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Also, the simulations don’t reflect or acknowledge the recessionary momentum that kicks in once the unemployment rate begins to rise.	23	2
201410	2340	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	One last comment.	23	2
201410	2341	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	In my opinion, the Tealbook, Book B, optimal policy simulations on page 8 show yet again why calendar-based forward guidance is a bad idea.	23	2
201410	2342	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	The optimal policy rate path today—which at least the copy I have in front of me is showing in that red line in the top left-hand box—is markedly different from the one calculated in September, because the optimal policy is very sensitive to changes in economic conditions.	23	2
201410	2343	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Given the sensitivity, I don’t want to be locked into a particular timing of liftoff or pace of subsequent rate increases.	23	2
201410	2344	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	You don’t want to give the impression that only a big change in the outlook will get you to change course, which is why I consider “considerable time” as having been, and continuing to be, a bad idea.	23	2
201410	2345	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I believe that we need to consider this in December.	23	2
201410	2346	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	If economic conditions improve between now and then, that will certainly condition my vote then.	23	2
201410	2347	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	But for now, Madam Chair, I support alternative B.	23	2

201410	2354	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Let me begin by discussing alternative A today.	23	2
201410	2355	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Alternative A contains language that would delay the end of tapering at this meeting.	23	2
201410	2356	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	This would mean maintaining a small amount of purchases into our next meeting.	23	2
201410	2357	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Because the amount of purchases is small, the direct macroeconomic effect would be minimal.	23	2
201410	2358	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	However, such a move would maintain some additional optionality for the Committee in the event that the Committee felt the current meeting is not an appropriate one to close a major program.	23	2
201410	2359	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	With QE1 and QE2, we closed programs based on calendar timetables, not macroeconomic conditions.	23	2
201410	2360	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	In both of those cases, the Committee was forced to reopen QE at a later date.	23	2
201410	2361	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	In retrospect, I consider both of those occasions as suboptimal policy decisions by the Committee.	23	2
201410	2362	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Are we making a similar mistake today?	23	2
201410	2363	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Certainly QE has been quite successful compared with the goals that the Committee set out in September 2012.	23	2
201410	2364	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	As I detailed at the previous meeting, forecasts of the Committee and the staff as of September 2012 have been largely accurate, except for unemployment, which has been a very large surprise.	23	2
201410	2365	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The short version of this is the following:  The level of GDP today is about as expected in the September 2012 forecast.	23	2
201410	2366	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Inflation remains below target, as expected in the September 2012 forecast.	23	2
201410	2367	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	But unemployment, at 5.9 percent, is much lower than expected.	23	2
201410	2368	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The staff forecast for the end of 2014, as of September 2012, was 7.6 percent, more than a point and a half above where we actually are.	23	2
201410	2369	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The SEP had a somewhat lower unemployment forecast, but it was still much higher than what actually happened.	23	2
201410	2370	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	If you don’t want to look at unemployment and you want to look at more of the broader measures of labor market conditions, you could look at a labor market conditions index, but such indexes also show substantial improvement in labor markets.	23	2
201410	2371	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	We definitely saw substantial improvement in labor markets relative to expectations, and in this sense the program was quite successful.	23	2
201410	2372	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I think that the open-ended nature of QE3 was very successful as well.	23	2
201410	2373	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	This feature enabled the Committee to continue with the program until goals could be achieved instead of maintaining an artificial calendar end date as with QE1 and QE2.	23	2
201410	2374	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	When the QE3 program was launched, many around the table probably expected it to end in the summer of 2013, a timetable that would have been similar to the one that we used for QE2.	23	2
201410	2375	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	However, Committee attempts to pull back on the program at that juncture proved premature, as the taper tantrum of the summer of 2013 pushed up longer-term rates by around 100 basis points globally.	23	2
201410	2376	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The open-ended nature of the program allowed the Committee to recommit to QE at the September 2013 meeting.	23	2
201410	2377	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	It would have been much harder to end the program in June 2013 and then restart the program in the fall of 2013.	23	2
201410	2378	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Despite the taper tantrum, I think we avoided a lot of unnecessary volatility by having an open-ended program that could be adjusted.	23	2
201410	2379	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The bottom line is that I think QE3 was a very successful open-ended QE program, and if we have to go to QE in the future, I would advocate that we again adopt the open-ended nature and set explicit goals for what we’re trying to achieve with the program.	23	2
201410	2380	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	For today, should we delay the end of tapering as outlined in alternative A?	23	2
201410	2381	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	During the intermeeting period, there was substantial market turmoil brought on by rising recession probabilities in Europe.	23	2
201410	2382	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The effects on the United States are questionable, in my view, but at one point markets were signaling dire consequences for the United States as well.	23	2

201410	2384	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Had we come into this meeting with markets still pricing in a major slowdown in US GDP growth and further downward movements in US inflation and inflation expectations, alternative A might have been a reasonable response.	23	2
201410	2385	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	It is, after all, a low-cost option.	23	2

201410	2388	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The Committee would retain the option of simply ending the program at the December meeting instead of at this meeting, provided that our forecast of the US economy is the correct one, as opposed to the market view.	23	2
201410	2389	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	And then if things did turn into a very dire situation, as markets were pricing in 10 days ago, we would have the option of ramping up QE again instead of starting a new program or being forced to consider the start of a new program.	23	2
201410	2390	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	However, because markets have retreated from their Europe-US contagion view and because the decline in market-based measures of inflation expectations has stabilized, albeit at an uncomfortably low level, I think we can go ahead with alternative B today and end the asset purchase program at this meeting.	23	2

201410	2425	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	23	2
201410	2426	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201410	2427	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Regarding alternative B, I agree that our open- ended asset purchases have served their purpose and we can end them today.	23	2
201410	2428	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	With regard to the forward-guidance language, I’m fine with that as well.	23	2
201410	2429	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	But I am worried about the language in paragraph 2 regarding inflation, and I share the low-inflation concerns expressed by President Kocherlakota.	23	2
201410	2430	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	In September I talked about why I think the risks of tightening too quickly and too aggressively far exceed those of moving too late and too cautiously.	23	2
201410	2431	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	This robust control perspective still leads me to think that we should not be tightening rates for more than a considerable time.	23	2
201410	2432	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	If we stay accommodative but the economy turns out to have more strength than we think, inflation may rise somewhat above 2 percent, but we know how to fix that.	23	2
201410	2433	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	However, if we tighten early and the economy encounters further unexpected headwinds, we have much less room to maneuver.	23	2
201410	2434	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Our unconventional monetary policy tools are likely to be less effective after an unceremonious retreat back to the zero lower bound.	23	2
201410	2435	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	As a result, we could find ourselves in a very difficult spot.	23	2
201410	2436	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	The economy could be stuck in a bad state for a very long time, with attendant damage to its future productivity.	23	2
201410	2437	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	This perspective means we should be highly attentive to downside risks, which today, especially, seem to be to our price stability goal.	23	2
201410	2438	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	We’ve underrun our 2 percent inflation target ever since we announced it in January 2012, almost three years ago.	23	2
201410	2439	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	We continue to express optimism that we will fulfill our obligation, but the time by which we expect to do so keeps receding further and further into the future.	23	2
201410	2440	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Since the September meeting, we’ve encountered some further potential impediments to meeting our policy objectives.	23	2
201410	2441	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I don’t want to claim that they are major game changers.	23	2
201410	2442	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I haven’t changed my forecast very much.	23	2
201410	2443	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	The downside risks are stronger today.	23	2
201410	2444	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I think we should avoid sounding complacent.	23	2
201410	2445	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	That means acknowledging that the risks of lower-for-longer inflation have ratcheted up a notch.	23	2
201410	2446	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I also want to mention that our discussion of long-run inflation expectations has taken on perhaps greater prominence than I’m comfortable with.	23	2
201410	2447	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I think it’s somewhat unsatisfactory that our inflation forecasting models rely so heavily on long-run inflation expectations.	23	2
201410	2448	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Our statistical models are crafted in terms of this more stable, long-run inflation expectation as far out as 10 years, but the economic theories that we tend to write down would place much more emphasis on short-term inflation expectations, things having to do with how marginal costs are expected to change over the future horizons and wage contracts and things like that.	23	2
201410	2449	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Yet there’s no good empirical traction that those models can gain for forecasting inflation.	23	2
201410	2450	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	That’s why we end up with the models that we have.	23	2
201410	2451	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	It’s a tough compromise, and I understand how we end up with long-run inflation expectations being there, but I think we should be uncomfortable with those models leaning so extensively on long-run expectations.	23	2
201410	2452	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Having been below our 2 percent objective for so long should make us even more uncomfortable as the horizon is extended.	23	2
201410	2453	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	As a policymaker, I’m just not as comforted by constant and unchanging survey measures of inflation expectations at the 10-year horizon.	23	2
201410	2454	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I worry that alternative B as written is overly complacent in suggesting that inflation is heading back to our objective within an acceptable period of time.	23	2
201410	2455	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	It fails to mention additional risks of low inflation.	23	2
201410	2456	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Specifically, the last sentence in paragraph 2 worries me.	23	2
201410	2457	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Given developments in Europe, the rest of the world, and perhaps most importantly our own recent low inflation data, the compromise wording that the Committee adopted in September now seems problematic.	23	2
201410	2458	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	This language states “that the likelihood of inflation running persistently below 2 percent has diminished somewhat since early this year.”	23	2
201410	2459	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	It said that in September.	23	2
201410	2460	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	While it’s still possible that this is true, it now seems dated and a bit out of touch.	23	2
201410	2461	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I think it is highly likely that inflation will underrun our 2 percent objective for at least another three years.	23	2
201410	2462	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	The best anyone has at this point is an optimistic forecast and a belief in the magical pull of long-run inflation expectations.	23	2
201410	2463	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Indeed, with the markdown in the Tealbook, its inflation projection is still below 2 percent in 2019.	23	2
201410	2464	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I think this sentence is really only viable if it says “well below 2 percent,” but that’s not helpful today.	23	2
201410	2465	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	The issue is, when do we think we will return to target?	23	2
201410	2466	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I prefer the language that served us in our statements from December 2013 to June 2014:  “The Committee recognizes that inflation persistently below its 2 percent objective could pose risks to economic performance, and it is monitoring inflation developments carefully for evidence that inflation will move back toward its objective over the medium term.”	23	2
201410	2467	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	This statement seems far more consistent with today’s heightened inflation risk, while the proposed alternative B sentence seems to have become overcome by events.	23	2
201410	2468	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	That’s my opinion.	23	2
201410	2469	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I prefer changing that language.	23	2
201410	2470	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201410	2476	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	There has been substantial improvement in labor markets since the asset purchase program was announced in September 2012, so the conditions for ending the program have been met.	23	2

201410	2478	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Although some aspects of the statement still concern me, I welcome some of the changes in language.	23	2
201410	2479	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	In general, I believe the characterization of the economy in the statement should not be just a recitation of movements in the data since the previous meeting, but an indication of the Committee’s view of the implications of changes in the data for the economic outlook and progress toward our goals and, therefore, for policy.	23	2
201410	2480	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	I actually thought that the draft statement language circulated before the Tealbook, Book B, got us closer to this ideal.	23	2
201410	2481	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Nevertheless, the suggested change in the characterization of labor markets in paragraph 1 seems consistent with the improvement we’ve been seeing for some time and supports ending the purchase program.	23	2
201410	2482	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	In paragraph 2, I think it is appropriate to acknowledge that near-term inflation will be held down by the drop in energy prices, but that our consensus outlook of inflation rising gradually back to target remains intact.	23	2
201410	2483	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	In contrast to President Fisher, I would have preferred that we include some reference to financial market volatility in paragraph 1 along with our evaluation that overall financial market conditions remain highly supportive of economic growth.	23	2
201410	2484	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	The volatility has been front and center in the minds of the public, and I believe it would be appropriate for us to give our interpretation of what it means for the outlook.	23	2
201410	2485	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Moreover, although we have signaled an end to the purchases, I could imagine the end of the program will still be met with some volatility, as may occur as we approach liftoff.	23	2
201410	2486	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Giving the public some idea of how we interpreted the intermeeting volatility we have seen might help them assess our likely reaction to volatility of this type in the future.	23	2
201410	2487	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	In our forward guidance on the path of interest rates, the addition of the two new sentences provides some welcome emphasis that our policy is state contingent.	23	2
201410	2488	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	I personally would still prefer that we remove the reference to “considerable time following the end of its asset purchase program.”	23	2
201410	2489	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Leaving it in poses problems for our forward guidance at subsequent meetings, especially if the intention is to continue to use the end of the purchase program as the benchmark, even as that event recedes increasingly into the past.	23	2
201410	2490	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	This is one of the suggestions in the staff memo on forward guidance, but it would not be my preference.	23	2
201410	2491	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	On this issue, I agree with President Lockhart.	23	2
201410	2492	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	I don’t believe there is any economic rationale for tying liftoff to the end of the purchase program, and doing so seems to link the timing of liftoff to that particular event rather than to economic conditions.	23	2
201410	2493	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	In addition, continuing to use the end of the purchase program as our reference state would muddy our communications.	23	2
201410	2494	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	For example, suppose, for the sake of argument, liftoff is to occur next June, which we are going to characterize as a “considerable time from the end of the purchase program.”	23	2
201410	2495	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Such guidance would technically be correct next May, but this would be a month before liftoff, and I don’t think anyone would want to use that forward guidance in May.	23	2
201410	2496	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	It would be very misleading.	23	2
201410	2497	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	So we would need to change the benchmark at some point well before liftoff.	23	2
201410	2498	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	My hope is that in December we will find a way to omit the reference to the conclusion of the purchase program in our forward guidance, replace “considerable time” with a more generic “a time.”	23	2
201410	2499	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	And if there is concern that the public will misinterpret the change in guidance, we should include a sentence clarifying that the change in the Committee’s guidance doesn’t indicate a change in the Committee’s policy intentions.	23	2
201410	2500	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	If that is indeed the case, we should be able to point to the December SEP for confirmation of that.	23	2
201410	2501	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	There is precedent for this, as the Committee included such a sentence in March when it replaced the threshold forward guidance with the current formulation.	23	2

201410	2516	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	There’s going to be more weight on the description of the economy.	23	2

201410	2518	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Part of the reason for the more positive cast is that, at the beginning of paragraph 3, we call out “a substantial improvement in the outlook for the labor market.”	23	2
201410	2519	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Based on the data, we could have easily made that statement at earlier meetings if it weren’t for the fact that we tied our asset purchase program to a substantial improvement in labor market conditions and we hadn’t ended our asset purchase program yet.	23	2
201410	2520	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Ending the asset purchase program, in a sense, released us from that inhibition and let us upgrade the tone of the statement a bit, in a way we might not otherwise have done.	23	2
201410	2521	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	More broadly, my sense over the course of this recovery is that our statements have been a bit on the dour side and have tended to convey a sense of dissatisfaction with the recovery— sort of a “glass half-empty” tone.	23	2
201410	2522	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	And, assuming that the data come in as most of us are expecting and we head toward raising rates sometime next year, I think it’s going to be useful to set the table by gradually shifting to a more positive characterization of the economy—more of a “glass half-full” tone.	23	2
201410	2523	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	We don’t want to go so far as to strain our credibility, obviously, but I believe we have room to work with as we describe economic conditions.	23	2

201410	2617	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Narayana makes a very potent point, which I don’t think was anticipated by those who wanted the language “in a context of price stability.”	23	2
201410	2618	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I believe the people who wanted “in a context of price stability” were thinking that maybe there would be too much inflation from QE and thus would want to adjust it.	23	2
201410	2619	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But as Narayana points out and as we’ll have occasion to discuss a little later this morning, that gets us back to our concept of what the inflation language in the longer-run goals statement actually means.	23	2

201410	2621	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	To not end the QE program at this juncture, given the path we’ve been on for some time and how much has relatively changed over the past six or seven weeks, would send a signal that doesn’t actually reflect where the Committee is.	23	2
201410	2622	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I think the Committee is at about the same place where we’ve been over the past few meetings, and to not end it now would send a more dire signal than people here, as a whole, probably believe.	23	2
201410	2623	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Some of the issues President Kocherlakota raises are very important, but they actually reflect difficulties or problems in our practice over the past six meetings rather than today.	23	2

201410	2625	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	As I listened yesterday, I think there’s a range of views on how much of a risk is posed by what’s going on in Europe, Japan, China, Asia excluding China, and elsewhere, but I didn’t hear any dissent from the proposition that whatever downside risks are out there, that’s high on the list.	23	2
201410	2626	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t think there would be an appetite for, nor would it be appropriate to include anything as strong as, the language that we had back in 2012, when we said that “strains in global financial markets continue to pose significant downside risks to the economic outlook.”	23	2

201410	2628	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But I’d be content with something in paragraph 1 that was pretty neutrally stated, such as “Uncertainty around global economic prospects has increased”—something that just indicates that there is a negative potential out there.	23	2
201410	2629	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	And we can avoid the use of who thinks it’s increased, how much we think it’s increased, or how high the risks can be—but just take note of that.	23	2
201410	2630	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Finally, with respect to the forward-guidance language, as I suggested at the beginning, there are disadvantages to the approach that’s being taken here, even though I was an advocate of it.	23	2

201410	2633	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But I think the reason why those of us who supported it did so was not because we thought it was perfect, but because, first, we thought there were greater risks associated with, for example, removal of “considerable” today and the potential effect on markets that that would have had even if we had qualitative language in there.	23	2
201410	2634	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Second, at least from my point of view—as someone, I think, already referred to—the debate over the right adjective at each succeeding FOMC meeting seemed one that would elicit mostly frustration among a lot of people.	23	2
201410	2635	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	So, again, I don’t think it’s perfect.	23	2
201410	2636	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Nobody thinks it’s perfect.	23	2
201410	2637	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	It’s just a question of, is there a better alternative?	23	2
201410	2638	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	And I don’t think there is, even though it’s going to, in President Plosser’s language, create some problems for us over the next few meetings.	23	2

201410	2667	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Again, because we have very limited ability to respond to risks of greater-than-expected slack and disinflationary pressures when we’re at the zero lower bound, as compared with a much greater ability to tighten faster if inflation or the elimination of slack were to accelerate, I think our strategy of vigilant patience is very appropriate.	23	2

201410	2672	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I think the approach of anchoring “considerable time” to the end of purchases this month is the best option, while acknowledging that all options have some risks.	23	2

201410	2703	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	We really need to be careful about how we discuss what we’re going to do after liftoff, in terms of how fast we’re going to go, because it seems to me that it really depends on two things that are highly uncertain:  one, how the economy itself evolves; and, two, how financial conditions react to tightening.	23	2
201410	2704	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	As we tighten monetary policy, financial conditions are going to respond.	23	2
201410	2705	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	If they respond very mildly, like what happened over the past year in response to the asset purchase taper, then we’re probably going to have to do more.	23	2
201410	2706	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	If they respond really a large amount, like the taper tantrum, then we’re going to have to do less.	23	2
201410	2707	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we really don’t want to lock ourselves in with markets in terms of how fast we’re going to go once we actually lift off, because it depends on these two things.	23	2
201410	2708	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	And I’m just totally uncertain about how these things are actually going to evolve.	23	2

201410	2776	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	And I’m afraid it’s going to be one of these statement carbuncles [laughter]—hard to scrape off.	23	2
201410	2777	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Fisher.	23	2

201410	2804	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	Thanks very much, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	2805	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	I’d like to begin by thanking the members of the communications subcommittee—Loretta Mester, Jay Powell, and John Williams—for their good work and collegiality in leading me through the graveyard of buried bodies and buried ideas, as I understand are there.	92	9
201410	2806	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	[Laughter]	92	9
201410	2807	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	I also want to thank the staff who supported our efforts:  Bob Tetlow, who you’ll hear in a while; Todd Clark from the FRB of Cleveland; and Stacey Tevlin.	92	9

201410	2810	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	At Ben’s last meeting, I think it must have been, he referred to the need to revise the Statement on Longer-Run Goals and Monetary Policy Strategy, so there seemed to be an extra need to get it done this year.	92	9

201410	2818	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	You received a list of questions that we chose to take up in this first attempt to change, or at least to review, the original consensus statement, and we were guided by discussions with several of you—especially with the Chair, who had chaired this subcommittee previously—about the issues to take up.	92	9
201410	2819	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	The three, which Bob Tetlow will introduce in greater detail soon, were the symmetry of the 2 percent inflation goal, what the “balanced approach” characterization of policy strategy means, and the relationship between the objective of financial stability and the dual-mandate goals of price stability and maximum employment.	92	9
201410	2820	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	We do not have legislation that puts financial stability on an equal footing with the dual-mandate goals, but it’s being talked about more and more in many central banks, and we thought it was worth taking that up.	92	9
201410	2821	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	This is not a meeting to decide on the statement.	92	9

201410	2828	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	You have all received the staff background paper, and Bob Tetlow will now introduce the topic and the considerations relating to these three issues that we’ve begun to consider.	92	9
201410	2829	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	Bob— thank you.	92	9
201410	2830	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Thank you, Governor Fischer.	92	9
201410	2831	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	I’ll be referring to the handout titled “Material for Briefing on Longer-Run Goals and Monetary Policy Strategy (‘Consensus Statement’).”	92	9
201410	2832	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	My briefing will summarize the memo that Todd Clark, Stacey Tevlin, and I prepared under the auspices of the subcommittee on communications.	92	9
201410	2833	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	As you know, the subcommittee identified three topics for discussion at this meeting.	92	9
201410	2834	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	As shown at the top of the handout, these topics were the clarification of the symmetry of inflation preferences around the Committee’s 2 percent goal, the clarification of the “balanced approach” monetary policy strategy, and the clarification of the role of financial stability in achieving the dual mandate.	92	9
201410	2835	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	I will go through each of these topics in order and then close with a few words on why you might prefer to leave the statement as it is now.	92	9
201410	2836	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	The memo first explored the case for preferring symmetry—or asymmetry—of inflation around the Committee’s announced 2 percent longer-run goal and for communicating that preference to the public.	92	9
201410	2837	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	The memo argued that a symmetric target would provide a clear focal point for longer-term inflation expectations.	92	9
201410	2838	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	This is so in large part because a symmetric target would be more likely to deliver a record of inflation that aligns with the announced level of the target.	92	9
201410	2839	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	An asymmetric target—a “ceiling,” for example—would tend to render inflation that averages less than 2 percent, with the shortfall of inflation from 2 percent likely to be a function, in part, of the variances of the shocks that are affecting the economy.	92	9
201410	2840	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	In this way, a symmetric target facilitates clear communications by generating outcomes consistent with the stated goal of 2 percent inflation.	92	9
201410	2841	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	This, in turn, fosters transparency and public accountability.	92	9
201410	2842	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	It might be worth noting that the evidence from surveys and financial market expectations suggests that at least a portion of the public currently regards the Committee’s preferences as being symmetric.	92	9
201410	2843	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	This may be because some policymakers have said as much, including Chairman Bernanke in his April 2012 press conference.	92	9
201410	2844	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	We also identified reasons why participants might have asymmetric preferences for inflation around the 2 percent goal.	92	9
201410	2845	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	First, while participants may agree that 2 percent is the best single target for inflation, they might view the costs of the distortionary effects of inflation above 2 percent as higher than the costs of inflation below 2 percent.	92	9
201410	2846	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Second, as the memo noted, the history of inflation in the United States during the 1970s and 1980s might lead policymakers to fear that long-term inflation expectations are more likely to become unanchored when inflation is above 2 percent than when it is below that level.	92	9
201410	2847	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Of course, a case could also be made for the opposite—namely, that inflation is more likely to be costly when it is persistently below 2 percent than when it is above.	92	9
201410	2848	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	This might be so because, all else being equal, lower inflation increases the likelihood of the zero lower bound becoming a binding constraint.	92	9
201410	2849	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	The staff memo also reported on possible benefits of clarifying the meaning of the “balanced approach” monetary policy strategy.	92	9
201410	2850	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	On the one hand, “balanced approach” could be a statement about the Committee’s loss function, without specific reference to what that function implies for the conduct of monetary policy.	92	9
201410	2851	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Alternatively, “balanced approach” could describe how the Committee might respond to deviations of variables from their target levels in a dynamic setting; that is, it could be seen as a statement about the reaction function.	92	9
201410	2852	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Regarding the loss-function interpretation, “balanced approach” might mean that equal weights are applied to the inflation and employment arguments of the Committee’s loss function.	92	9
201410	2853	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	The memo noted that there is little in the research literature that provides reliable guidance on what the proper loss-function weights should be; results tend to be idiosyncratic to the model under consideration, although some recent research suggests that at least some popular, mainstream models are consistent with roughly equal weights on the two objectives.	92	9
201410	2854	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Finally, a number of policymakers have at times alluded to “balanced approach” being consistent with, or equivalent to, the two legs of the dual mandate having equal footing as objectives in monetary policy.	92	9
201410	2855	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Regarding the reaction-function interpretation, “balanced approach” might suggest that the time horizons over which the Committee would aim to return the two goal variables to target, conditional on “appropriate monetary policy,” would likely be similar.	92	9
201410	2856	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Alternatively, the Committee could provide information about the conditions that would lead it to tolerate an overshooting or undershooting of one mandate variable relative to its longer-run goal in order to facilitate the more rapid convergence of the other mandate variable to its goal.	92	9
201410	2857	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	At a more modest level, a statement to the effect that tradeoffs between mandate variables always matter—so that the public understands that one variable is never subordinated to the other— might be helpful.	92	9
201410	2858	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	On financial stability, the memo discussed whether the consensus statement could address the possibility that monetary policy could respond to financial-stability concerns, as a way of promoting the Committee’s dual-mandate goals.	92	9
201410	2859	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	The memo took as given that macroprudential and supervisory tools would be operative and noted that these tools presumably would be the first line of defense against financial instability.	92	9
201410	2860	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	At the same time, we also argued that it would be imprudent to assume that these nonmonetary tools could be relied on to consistently achieve their goals.	92	9
201410	2861	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	The memo devoted some space to considering why financial instability might warrant special attention from monetary policy, in view of the fact that financial stability is not directly a part of the dual mandate.	92	9
201410	2862	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Or, to put the same point in the form of a question, what makes financial instability different from other asymmetric risks?	92	9
201410	2863	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	We identified two main reasons.	92	9
201410	2864	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	First, monetary policy may be able to affect the probability of an episode of financial instability, its likely cost, or both.	92	9
201410	2865	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	And, second, an episode of financial instability can reduce the efficacy of monetary policy for offsetting the effects of that episode or the effects of other shocks.	92	9
201410	2866	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Either of these reasons provides a prima facie case for using monetary policy to mitigate a buildup of financial market vulnerabilities.	92	9
201410	2867	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	We argued that this prima facie case is not one that is operational at all times.	92	9
201410	2868	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Financial instability is an episodic phenomenon.	92	9
201410	2869	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	As such, emerging instability might induce policymakers to set aside temporarily their direct pursuit of maximum employment and price stability in order to temper the likelihood or severity of a possible episode of financial instability.	92	9
201410	2870	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	At the same time, however, it bears noting that identifying the appropriate monetary policy response to incipient instability might not be a straightforward exercise.	92	9
201410	2871	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	The staff memo closed by listing three reasons why participants might choose to retain the current consensus statement language—even if policymakers largely agree with the affirmative arguments outlined in the memo.	92	9
201410	2872	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	First, any change in policy communications runs the risk of being misinterpreted.	92	9
201410	2873	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Second, to the extent that policymakers view changes in consensus statement language as likely to be costly to reverse, there is some value in retaining the option value of waiting until the appropriate change in language becomes clearer.	92	9
201410	2874	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	And, finally, the current language of the consensus statement is the product of compromise.	92	9
201410	2875	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Participants may judge that the comity of the Committee is best served by not perturbing that compromise.	92	9
201410	2876	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	That concludes my prepared remarks.	92	9
201410	2877	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	I am, together with Todd and Stacey, happy to answer your questions.	92	9
201410	2878	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Are there questions for Bob?	92	9
201410	2879	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	92	9
201410	2880	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Bob, I thought you said that economic models come out with roughly equal weights, and my comments are different from that.	92	9
201410	2881	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	So I’m wondering what you meant by that statement.	92	9
201410	2882	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	There’s a reference in the full memo to a paper by Debortoli, Kim, Lindé, and Nunes.	92	9
201410	2883	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	They took the Smets-Wouters model and looked at what the optimal Ramsey policy was in there.	92	9
201410	2884	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Then they said, what would the loss-function weight on the output gap be for the kind of loss functions that, for example, we use to carry out optimal control scenarios for the Committee?	92	9
201410	2885	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	It turns out that the coefficient in that case would be a coefficient of unity, which would actually be much higher in unemployment space.	92	9
201410	2886	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	This is one of these cases in which, once the model starts to get sufficiently complex, there are some more channels through which monetary policy works, and, more important, there are more shocks that break the “divine coincidence.”	92	9
201410	2887	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Then you get the result in which a higher weight on resource utilization becomes appropriate.	92	9
201410	2888	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Okay.	92	9
201410	2889	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	So you would agree that, in the broader literature, it would be maybe more coincidental that you would come out with exactly equal weights, because these models have preferences and all kinds of assumptions in them, and then you have to figure out what the optimal weights are.	92	9
201410	2890	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	They might come out one way, or they might come out another way, but they wouldn’t come out exactly equal.	92	9
201410	2891	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Is that fair?	92	9
201410	2892	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	Yes, that’s certainly fair.	92	9
201410	2893	2014-10-29	meeting	TETLOW	And I think that’s what we said.	92	9
201410	2894	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Are there other questions?	92	9
201410	2895	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	[No response]	92	9
201410	2896	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Okay.	92	9
201410	2897	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Then let’s begin our go-round.	92	9
201410	2898	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Tarullo is first.	92	9
201410	2899	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	2900	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Let me apologize in advance for doing what I always say we shouldn’t do, which is to read statements.	92	9
201410	2901	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But because I knew I was going first and I wanted to make sure I made the points I wanted to make, I did write this one out.	92	9
201410	2902	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	When we were debating the original version of this statement nearly three years ago, I suggested that its practical benefits would be limited.	92	9
201410	2903	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	And I think this has turned out to be the case.	92	9
201410	2904	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	The statement has received relatively little attention, in large part because the agreed-upon text did not reflect an actual consensus on the Committee and was necessarily drafted with significant ambiguities, as I believe are well explained in the staff memo.	92	9
201410	2905	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I suspect most people who read it already knew that a 2 percent target was in some way or another assumed by most, if not all, FOMC members.	92	9
201410	2906	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Sometimes, of course, agreed-upon wording turns out to have a life of its own, particularly when that wording is committed to later interpretation or implementation by actors other than those who originally agreed to it.	92	9
201410	2907	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	That’s why, for example, vague statutory language can, over time, acquire reasonably well-specified meanings.	92	9
201410	2908	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But there are no such authoritative interpreters of the goals statement, with one quasi-exception that I’ll mention in a bit.	92	9
201410	2909	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	All members of the FOMC are able to stick to their own preferred interpretations, contradictory as they might be, and I think this is precisely what’s happened.	92	9
201410	2910	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	There is a case for changing the statement so that it will have some information content.	92	9
201410	2911	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Three years ago, I was largely focused on the meaning of “balanced approach” in paragraph 5.	92	9
201410	2912	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	This paragraph purported to address, albeit in a very general way, how the Committee would deal with situations in which circumstances create policy tension between the inflation and unemployment goals.	92	9
201410	2913	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I’ll return to this issue in a moment.	92	9
201410	2914	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But the intervening period has revealed, at least to me, that there is not even consensus on the most basic goal articulated in the statement.	92	9
201410	2915	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	And, while there has always been disagreement on the unemployment goal, the differences in the past year or two have surprisingly centered on the inflation goal.	92	9
201410	2916	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Of course, the reason most emphasized by our former Chairman for adopting a statement was that it ratified in a formal way the Committee’s embrace of a flexible inflation target.	92	9
201410	2917	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I would have anticipated that disagreement would arise when some argued that temporary toleration of above-target inflation would lead to higher employment in the steady state, and others would have weighted more heavily the risks of nontransitory above-target inflation.	92	9
201410	2918	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But, instead, over the past few years, we’ve had discussions in this Committee during which some participants have seemed to suggest that, because they find slack in labor markets to have diminished substantially, it is time to raise rates even though inflation has persisted below target for much of the period since adoption of the goals and strategy statement.	92	9
201410	2919	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Now, one’s first reaction to this circumstance might logically be to conclude that perhaps estimates of the natural rate are too high, given the absence of wage pressures or above-target inflation.	92	9
201410	2920	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But let’s put that issue aside for a moment in order to note that those taking this position have essentially converted our two goals into a single goal.	92	9
201410	2921	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But here’s the irony, at least to me:  Implicitly, that single goal is not the inflation target, which is usually the aim of those on the hawkish side of monetary policy who don’t like the dual mandate.	92	9
201410	2922	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Instead, the single goal appears to be, while maybe not maximum employment, enough employment.	92	9
201410	2923	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	How does this circle get squared for those taking this position?	92	9
201410	2924	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	It happens in one of two ways, I think, which are, in practical terms, consistent with one another.	92	9
201410	2925	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	One is to treat the 2 percent inflation number as a ceiling, not a target, with no policy response being called for unless inflation threatens to exceed the target.	92	9
201410	2926	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	The other is to stipulate, as a formal matter, that there is an inflation target but to assume that inflation will somehow and always, almost gravitationally, move upward in periods of even modest economic growth.	92	9
201410	2927	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	So, again, policy attention to measures to increase inflation is never needed.	92	9
201410	2928	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I disagree with both of these propositions, as I suspect many of you do.	92	9
201410	2929	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	There may be other reasons for the position taken, and I suspect I’d disagree with those as well.	92	9
201410	2930	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But for present purposes, the issue is not who’s got the better policy position.	92	9
201410	2931	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	The issue is whether there is a shared commitment to an inflation target.	92	9
201410	2932	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Given current and, possibly, future conditions, it would be useful to clarify, if we could, that the controlling view on the Committee is that we do have a flexible inflation target, which contemplates policy action in at least some circumstances in order to raise inflation from a level that is persistently below 2 percent as well as to lower or stave off inflation that would rise above 2 percent on a nontransitory basis.	92	9
201410	2933	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	While I hope I am proven wrong, I suspect that not everybody would agree with such an articulation.	92	9
201410	2934	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Still, for a healthy majority of the Committee to adopt it would be to communicate some significant information to the public.	92	9
201410	2935	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	On the symmetrical issue raised in the staff memo, I think the fact that the Japanese experience of the past 20 years seems at present more threatening in parts of the world than the stagflation of the 1970s might actually argue for asymmetrically worrying more about inflation risks on the downside.	92	9
201410	2936	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	But that perspective is obviously time contingent.	92	9
201410	2937	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	An explicitly symmetrical position seems better suited for a statement of longer-run goals and strategy.	92	9
201410	2938	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	As to the “balanced approach” issue, the illustrations I suggested to elaborate the very general statement in paragraph 5—I suggested these three years ago—are perhaps of less immediate relevance today, though they may, again, be so in the future.	92	9
201410	2939	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	In any case, I would anticipate considerable difficulty in agreeing on such illustrations, even among those who could agree on much else in the statement.	92	9
201410	2940	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	So I’d be happy with a statement such as that crafted on the top of page 8 of the staff memo, indicating that the Committee is equally concerned about deviations from both mandates.	92	9
201410	2941	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	With respect to financial stability, I’ve done a good bit of thinking about the role of financial stability in monetary policy.	92	9
201410	2942	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	And, to be honest, I still don’t have a formulation that even I’m satisfied with.	92	9
201410	2943	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	So I’d anticipate that even a subset of us who more generally agree on broader monetary policy matters would have a lot of difficulty agreeing among ourselves, certainly in the next couple of months.	92	9
201410	2944	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	A threshold issue, of course, is that, unlike price stability and maximum employment, financial stability is not even an explicit statutory goal.	92	9
201410	2945	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Important as the issue is, I think it probably requires more discussion, analysis, and, perhaps, experience before we’d be ready to integrate financial-stability considerations in succinct form into the current or revised statement elaborating on the statutory mandate.	92	9
201410	2946	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	That’s the case for making a change.	92	9
201410	2947	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I actually think that the case for not making a change is somewhat stronger, and I’m going to turn briefly to that now before ending.	92	9
201410	2948	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	I do think that the views on goals and policies offered by our former Chairman and current Chair have been noted by market actors and commentators, and this is what I meant earlier by the one quasi-authoritative interpreter.	92	9
201410	2949	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	In that sense, the statement has provided some useful color in public understanding of the goals and strategy of a majority of the Committee.	92	9
201410	2950	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	We didn’t necessarily need the statement to accomplish that, but the statement has been a vehicle for Chairman Bernanke and then-Governor, now Chair, Yellen to articulate a shared general—if not, perhaps, unanimous—interpretation.	92	9
201410	2951	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Given the large and fractious nature of this Committee, making any noncosmetic changes would likely be a difficult process, and any changes coming out of that process might, as Bob was warning us, actually risk injecting confusion rather than more clarity into public understanding of FOMC proclivities.	92	9
201410	2952	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	So even though I have, in the past, advocated for changes in what is the current statement, I think there’s a good argument—and, as I say, in the end, I believe this is the better argument—for following Hippocratic principles and leaving it alone.	92	9
201410	2953	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	It’s not all that relevant, but, for that very reason, it’s not having a negative effect on public understanding of Fed policies.	92	9
201410	2954	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	And if this is the outcome in January, I’ll be content to abstain once again, rather than to dissent, again on the ground that the statement does not affirmatively advance the understanding of Fed policies.	92	9
201410	2955	2014-10-29	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201410	2958	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	2959	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	As someone who was deeply involved in trying to craft the earlier statement in the subcommittee on communications, I know, as does Chair Yellen, how difficult that was to get to where we ended up.	92	9
201410	2960	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	I think that, for those reasons and some other reasons, I’d prefer that we not attempt changes at this time.	92	9
201410	2961	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m concerned that, in doing so, we might inadvertently signal a shift in policy.	92	9
201410	2962	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Should this occur, it would be particularly disruptive at this stage of the normalization process.	92	9
201410	2963	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m actually not opposed to considering changes, in principle, to the statement, but I think doing so at a time when policy is more nearly under normal circumstances would be a more fruitful way to proceed.	92	9
201410	2964	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m just concerned that attempts to change it could lead to an unraveling of the delicate consensus and the vagueness of what we’ve achieved.	92	9
201410	2965	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	That said, I do have some reactions to the memo, and I’ll try to share those a little bit.	92	9
201410	2966	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m not averse to specifying the symmetry of our objectives.	92	9
201410	2967	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	I always thought that that symmetry was implicit in what we had said.	92	9
201410	2968	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	We could even go further by stating a target range that is symmetric around 2 percent.	92	9
201410	2969	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Again, I wouldn’t have any real, serious objections to that.	92	9
201410	2970	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	In fact, the subcommittee did consider such language at one point.	92	9
201410	2971	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	I do have some trepidation as to what that might imply regarding how we might then go about discussing the symmetry of the employment mandate in a similar way, if we really wanted symmetry.	92	9
201410	2972	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	And what that might devolve into could be quite complicated and very confusing.	92	9
201410	2973	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	So I would approach that with a bit of caution.	92	9
201410	2974	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	I also suggest we leave “balanced approach” as is.	92	9
201410	2975	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Trying to parse out or agree on a loss or objective function would be extremely difficult in a Committee this big.	92	9
201410	2976	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	The economic viewpoints on the Committee are very diverse at this point, and trying to get it to a common loss function or weights on the objective function could be quite difficult.	92	9
201410	2977	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	It would be like opening Pandora’s box.	92	9
201410	2978	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	In particular, trying to do so in such a short time frame would be very difficult.	92	9
201410	2979	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	To approach this, we would need many careful discussions and thoughtful alternatives and approaches, because if we did it on short notice, we would undoubtedly regret it at some point down the road.	92	9
201410	2980	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	I do regard the diversity of views on this Committee as a strength.	92	9
201410	2981	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	And, while I understand and appreciate that “balanced approach” is a bit vague, it does indicate that the Committee weighs both nominal and real factors as an important part of its policy deliberations.	92	9
201410	2982	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	As Governor Tarullo just mentioned, both our former Chairman and our current Chair have articulated that message quite clearly.	92	9
201410	2983	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	So I think it does have some content.	92	9
201410	2984	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	All told, the language of the current document was carefully and painfully crafted.	92	9
201410	2985	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Upsetting that balance at a time when policy is in flux would not be a very wise approach.	92	9
201410	2986	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	With regard to financial stability, I oppose elevating financial conditions to the same level as our fundamental goals of maximum employment and stable prices.	92	9
201410	2987	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	I think they should be used primarily as an indicator of economic conditions that we would respond to when activities in financial markets are worrisome and when monetary policy can perhaps have a direct effect on that behavior or perhaps is precipitating that behavior.	92	9
201410	2988	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	At a minimum, different financial developments will likely entail differential monetary responses of various kinds.	92	9
201410	2989	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Reacting to a bank panic might be one response, whereas reacting to a stock market crash or a currency crisis in some part of the world could be very different responses.	92	9
201410	2990	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	We have no systematic way of thinking about that.	92	9
201410	2991	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	How the Committee would act in such circumstances is best left to particular episodes and to the FOMC statement, which would presumably describe or explain why policy was being set, perhaps, in an unusually tight or unusually loose stance or maybe not reacting at all.	92	9
201410	2992	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Determining appropriate monetary policy in response to financial market conditions is a more complex undertaking, and I would rather that we not get engaged in that in our statement of longer-term strategies.	92	9
201410	2993	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Finally, I don’t think the material in the memo devoted to how the Committee would act in a precise way in some hypothetical examples really belongs in a statement of longer-run goals and objectives.	92	9
201410	2994	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Those tend to be tactics, and we should avoid those.	92	9
201410	2995	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Thus, at this juncture, I believe it would be wise to avoid upsetting the apple cart.	92	9
201410	2996	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	We should simply leave the statement as is for the time being.	92	9
201410	2997	2014-10-29	meeting	PLOSSER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201410	2999	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Lacker.	92	9
201410	3000	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3001	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Let me start with an endorsement of a characterization of the consensus statement as a delicately crafted compromise.	92	9
201410	3002	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	We each bring particular frameworks to bear on monetary policy questions we face, and then some of these frameworks conflict, as Governor Tarullo pointed out.	92	9
201410	3003	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I think the consensus statement we drafted did a masterful job of articulating as much as it could by way of areas of agreement while allowing each of us to read the statement as compatible with his or her own framework.	92	9
201410	3004	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	In a sense, it’s the smallest tent we could get all of us—or all but one of us—into.	92	9
201410	3005	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I don’t see this as a weakness.	92	9
201410	3006	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I see this as a strength.	92	9
201410	3007	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I see this as just a recognition of the reality of the scientific uncertainty about many of the questions that face us when we do monetary policy, about which reasonable people—reasonable, well-informed economists—can disagree.	92	9
201410	3008	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	And I think it strengthens policy that we have a framework that encompasses different views.	92	9
201410	3009	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	The fourth paragraph, the one about our maximum-employment mandate, is an illustrative case in point.	92	9
201410	3010	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	There are serious differences of opinion around the table about how to interpret the natural rate of unemployment, though we all agree that it makes sense to think of maximum employment in terms of some form of what you would call a natural rate.	92	9
201410	3011	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	There are different meanings of that term, though.	92	9
201410	3012	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Paragraph 4 is careful not to call the question.	92	9
201410	3013	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	It’s agnostic about whether maximum employment does or does not correspond to the “estimates of the longer-run normal rates of output growth and unemployment” that are published in the SEP.	92	9
201410	3014	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	The proponents of any of a variety of views about the behavior of the natural rate can thus read the consensus statement as not inconsistent with their views.	92	9
201410	3015	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I’m deeply skeptical about prospects for modifying the consensus statement in a coherent way.	92	9
201410	3016	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Let me first say that I think the consensus statement should be a relatively permanent document, conveying what we believe to be timeless principles.	92	9
201410	3017	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	It shouldn’t reflect commentary on current or passing issues in monetary policy.	92	9
201410	3018	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Accordingly, there’s a risk involved if we’re to make regular, substantive changes to the statement.	92	9
201410	3019	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Observers could come to doubt whether the Committee is going to stick to its precepts long into the future—that what’s in the statement represents precepts that will guide our behavior long into the future.	92	9
201410	3020	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	This risk would be particularly acute if we were seen as making opportunistic changes motivated by this year’s issues du jour.	92	9
201410	3021	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	The current shortfall of inflation strikes me as one such preoccupation.	92	9
201410	3022	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	It’s legitimate to debate what to do about it.	92	9
201410	3023	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	We’ve been doing that every meeting.	92	9
201410	3024	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	But if we choose this time to add some forceful language about the symmetry of our inflation preferences, I think it could look a bit contrived—it could look a bit oriented toward where inflation is now relative to 2 percent.	92	9
201410	3025	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I’m dubious about the notion of symmetry on more fundamental grounds as well.	92	9
201410	3026	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	In our standard theoretical models, there are a variety of costs and benefits.	92	9
201410	3027	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	They vary asymmetrically about the optimal inflation rate, and the symmetry that we see in a lot of reduced forms is an artifact of the linear-quadratic approximations, a popular analytical technique.	92	9
201410	3028	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	But it’s really a shortcut, and so it essentially imposes symmetry when there often is none in the fundamental underlying models.	92	9
201410	3029	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Beyond that, these frameworks reflect equilibrium, in which we have perfect credibility, and it’s quite plausible to think that, if our credibility erodes, we’d be quite likely to be different above 2 than below 2.	92	9
201410	3030	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	So I’d oppose attempting to articulate some sense of symmetry around our inflation goal.	92	9
201410	3031	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I haven’t advocated 2 percent inflation as a ceiling.	92	9
201410	3032	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I’m not quite sure I’ve heard that around here, and I’m not sure it isn’t something of a straw man.	92	9
201410	3033	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	But I could be wrong about that.	92	9
201410	3034	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I’m skeptical about going beyond the current “balanced approach” language.	92	9
201410	3035	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	One’s mind is instantly drawn to the notion of equal weight in a policymaker’s objective function.	92	9
201410	3036	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	However, as the staff memo points out, in the models we use—and there was an exchange between President Bullard and Mr Tetlow about this—for applied policy analysis, the policy objective function that maximizes household welfare generally places much larger weight on inflation, and we have just a couple of examples in which they’re roughly equal.	92	9
201410	3037	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	So it would take a very special coincidence of model parameters to deliver equal algebraic weights in a reduced-form policy objective function that policymakers thinking about household welfare can be thought of as acting as if they’re maximizing.	92	9
201410	3038	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Remember, this is a Committee that can’t agree on what constitutes maximum employment.	92	9
201410	3039	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	We’re talking about a weight on deviations from something, and we can’t agree on what the thing is that we’re taking deviations from.	92	9
201410	3040	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	So it’s hard to believe we’re going to agree on weights to place on deviations from maximum employment.	92	9
201410	3041	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	We should stick with “balanced approach”—it’s hard to imagine a smaller tent we can all fit in.	92	9
201410	3042	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Adding language to our consensus statement about financial stability strikes me as equally hopeless.	92	9
201410	3043	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Here the economics are even less developed and even more contentious.	92	9
201410	3044	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think we have a clear sense of how much financial stability or instability we want or is optimal.	92	9
201410	3045	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	So I don’t see us finding a consensus way of doing that.	92	9
201410	3046	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	I’m not unalterably opposed to amending the consensus statement, in principle.	92	9
201410	3047	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Maybe with the passage of time and the accumulation of greater insights, we will be able to collectively improve on it.	92	9
201410	3048	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	But for now, I think that it’s served us reasonably well and we should leave well enough alone.	92	9
201410	3049	2014-10-29	meeting	LACKER	Thank you.	92	9

201410	3063	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	So I personally don’t see a compelling reason to change the language of the consensus statement, but I do see value in having the discussion on longer-run goals and strategy.	92	9
201410	3064	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Regarding the inflation goal, I believe the public perceives our inflation goal as a symmetric target.	92	9
201410	3065	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	A number of Committee participants have said in speeches that persistent inflation above our goal and persistent inflation below our goal are both undesirable.	92	9
201410	3066	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	But I want to note that a shared view on the symmetry of the 2 percent inflation target does not necessarily mean that there’s agreement on the policy to achieve it.	92	9
201410	3067	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	I don’t think there’s that much to be gained by changing the language on this.	92	9
201410	3068	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	But should there be a consensus to do so, I would not object to an appropriate revision acknowledging symmetry and clarifying that inflation can be expected to vary in the short to medium run, but that, over the longer run, we aim for 2 percent inflation.	92	9
201410	3069	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Regarding financial stability, before making changes to the consensus statement, I would prefer the Committee to have a fuller discussion of its approach to financial stability, the tools that it will use and their efficacy in addressing financial-stability issues as they arise, and the nexus between monetary policy and financial stability.	92	9
201410	3070	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	I think we’d benefit from further work on these issues by Governor Fischer’s Committee on Financial Stability and others at the Board and in the System.	92	9
201410	3071	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	The FOMC might then discuss its preferred approach and, in light of that discussion, consider potential revisions to the consensus statement later next year or further in the future.	92	9
201410	3072	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	I am perhaps most trepidatious about making changes to the “balanced approach” language.	92	9
201410	3073	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	I admit that it is ambiguous, and, in the abstract, it perhaps would be desirable to clear up some of that ambiguity.	92	9
201410	3074	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	On the other hand, it is not clear to me that the language could be clarified in a satisfactory way to encompass the nuances of various interpretations, economic models, and approaches to monetary policy around the table.	92	9
201410	3075	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	So before making such a change, we might do well to have a fuller discussion of loss functions.	92	9
201410	3076	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Before we can even ask about the weights in the loss function, we need to first agree on the form of the loss function and its components.	92	9
201410	3077	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Do we agree that the loss function is quadratic?	92	9
201410	3078	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	How do we think about the treatment of financial stability in the loss function?	92	9
201410	3079	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	Unless we have such a discussion, it would be premature to change the “balanced approach” language, which, in the end, seems to have done a very good job of balancing many considerations.	92	9
201410	3080	2014-10-29	meeting	MESTER	The last question on the agenda was about the SEPs.	92	9
