201410	3094	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	While I agree that more precise language is possible that makes even clearer that our inflation target is symmetric and not a ceiling, I think the previous Chairman made that quite clear in his press conference.	92	9
201410	3095	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Similarly, his press conference made clear that there was a balanced approach to the dual mandate, a position I strongly endorse.	92	9
201410	3096	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Given the broad acceptance of the previous Chairman’s comments in the markets, I see little advantage in relitigating these issues.	92	9
201410	3097	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	The risk is that, rather than simply clarifying what I see as critical elements of the framework—symmetric attention to inflation deviations and balanced responses to both pillars of the dual mandate—we could raise a question in the markets as to whether we are now or continuously reconsidering one or both of these elements.	92	9
201410	3098	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In my view, any uncertainty about symmetry and balance would be counterproductive.	92	9
201410	3099	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	In terms of financial stability, I think this is a good area in which to seek a broader consensus on how we define financial stability, as well as the appropriate responses of the central bank to incipient or full-blown instability.	92	9
201410	3100	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I am not optimistic that a consensus can be reached by January.	92	9
201410	3101	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, I do think it would be productive to have a special session in which we can have a structured discussion on the role that financial stability should play in our monetary policy deliberations.	92	9
201410	3102	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	I also believe that it might be useful to consider whether there is a consensus that there are times when we would make monetary policy to address financial-stability concerns even though it might move us away from our inflation and employment targets.	92	9
201410	3103	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Once we have a clearer, common understanding of what financial stability means and when it would affect monetary policy decisions, we could then discuss how it might be incorporated into the longer- run policy statement.	92	9
201410	3104	2014-10-29	meeting	ROSENGREN	Also, there might be some advantage to thinking about a consensus forecast over time as well.	92	9
201410	3105	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201410	3106	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	92	9
201410	3107	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3108	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	My comments are going to strongly echo what’s already been said here, so I’ll be brief.	92	9
201410	3109	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The consensus statement established an inflation target for the United States.	92	9
201410	3110	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Therefore, it’s quite an important document for this Committee.	92	9
201410	3111	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Previous to that, the FOMC did not have an official inflation target.	92	9
201410	3112	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I think that establishing an inflation target has been quite valuable to the Committee during this era of very low inflation.	92	9
201410	3113	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	It could have gone very differently if there had been some doubt that maybe a large fraction of the Committee thought 1 percent inflation or 0 percent inflation was okay.	92	9
201410	3114	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	That could have led to very different dynamics for the US economy.	92	9
201410	3115	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	So it’s actually been quite helpful to adopt the inflation target, as former Chairman Bernanke predicted at the time.	92	9
201410	3116	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	My general feeling, echoing many of the previous comments, is that the statement does not require modification.	92	9
201410	3117	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	The statement is written in a way to garner widespread consensus around the table—I would not want to disturb that consensus.	92	9
201410	3118	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I think that trying to change the consensus statement before we return to a more normalized policy environment—that is, this coming January—carries substantial risk of muddling our near-term policy intentions in the minds of financial market participants and the general public.	92	9
201410	3119	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	So I recommend no change.	92	9
201410	3120	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I have a few comments on specific issues that also echo the previous comments.	92	9
201410	3121	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I regard the inflation target as symmetric, and I’ve said so publicly on many occasions.	92	9
201410	3122	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Hitting the inflation target, on average, is closer to price-level targeting.	92	9
201410	3123	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	In this sense, it’s closer to optimal policy in many leading theories.	92	9
201410	3124	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	I think the “balanced approach” language is brilliant and should not be altered.	92	9
201410	3125	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	It may seem fair to say that the weights on inflation and unemployment are equal or should be equal, but research on the topic suggests otherwise.	92	9
201410	3126	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	If you read the literature, the actual weights on the two objectives are going to depend on details of modeling assumptions, preferences, technology, and frictions that are in the model.	92	9
201410	3127	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Those parameters are all going to come together in a way to determine what the right weights are on the two objectives from the point of view of household utility, as President Lacker was saying.	92	9
201410	3128	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	So it’s just not clear that it always comes out to be exactly equal.	92	9
201410	3129	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	That is something that seems as though it would be the right thing, but it’s not.	92	9
201410	3130	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	As an example, I’ll point out a favorite paper I like to quote to all of you here—Ravenna and Walsh.	92	9
201410	3131	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	That’s a New Keynesian model with explicit search-theoretic unemployment in it.	92	9
201410	3132	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	You have the unemployment friction in there.	92	9
201410	3133	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	You have the sticky price friction in there.	92	9
201410	3134	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	You might have thought you were going to get roughly equal weights to balance the two frictions.	92	9
201410	3135	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	That isn’t what they got.	92	9
201410	3136	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	They got pretty heavy optimal weight on inflation.	92	9
201410	3137	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	That’s just the outcome of one piece of research, but I think the nature of research shows you that it’s not going to come out to be equal and it could go the other way.	92	9
201410	3138	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	It could be that other types of models with other types of assumptions would put heavy weight on the unemployment side and less weight on the price-stability side.	92	9
201410	3139	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	So it’s just not something that naturally falls out of models, at least in my experience.	92	9
201410	3140	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Another example, one from the older research literature, is Rotemberg and Woodford, who calculated optimal weights in their model that certainly were not equal.	92	9
201410	3141	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	On financial stability, I agree with the previous comments that this would be very difficult.	92	9
201410	3142	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Anything beyond what’s in the existing consensus statement would be very difficult.	92	9
201410	3143	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	There’s a clear lack of consensus on models or even approach on this issue around the table.	92	9
201410	3144	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	It’s an issue of our time.	92	9
201410	3145	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	It’s a macroeconomic issue of first-order importance.	92	9
201410	3146	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	But I don’t think we have anything like the right approach or language to be able to put it into a statement of this kind.	92	9
201410	3147	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	How the Committee should react to asset price bubbles remains a vexing issue, as it has been for this Committee since the 1990s, and I don’t believe we’re likely to resolve it anytime soon.	92	9
201410	3148	2014-10-29	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3149	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201410	3150	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Lockhart.	92	9
201410	3151	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3152	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I tend to agree with those who’ve already argued to leave the statement unchanged at this juncture.	92	9
201410	3153	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I think the benefit versus the cost of changing the statement at this time doesn’t add up for me.	92	9
201410	3154	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	But should the Committee—and it doesn’t appear to be the trend—decide to consider adjustments, here are my views.	92	9
201410	3155	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Our preferences should be symmetric around the 2 percent inflation objective.	92	9
201410	3156	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I’d object to any change that suggests an asymmetric preference.	92	9
201410	3157	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I think there is some risk in fiddling with the language that is already interpreted in a way consistent with the Committee’s intentions.	92	9
201410	3158	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I’m satisfied with the current “balanced approach” language.	92	9
201410	3159	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	It adequately captures the general principle that the Committee gives due consideration to both elements of the dual mandate.	92	9
201410	3160	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I don’t think more explicit language is likely to do justice to the diversity of views about how that principle would be applied tactically by various members of the Committee across a wide range of circumstances.	92	9
201410	3161	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	In my view, tactical flexibility—in which more emphasis is put on one element or the other, depending on circumstances—should be preserved.	92	9
201410	3162	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I don’t think risk-management nuances, for instance, are easily captured by a more narrowly constructed explanation of “balanced approach.”	92	9
201410	3163	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Also, in reaction to a deviation of inflation from our objective, my emphasis on the inflation side would depend on my reading of how solidly inflation expectations are anchored.	92	9
201410	3164	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	As regards further clarification of how financial-stability considerations relate to the dual-mandate goals, I am comfortable with the current language.	92	9
201410	3165	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	In my view, financial-stability concerns should be given consideration in monetary policy, as opposed to macroprudential policy, to the extent that there’s a threat to the attainment of our price-stability and employment objectives.	92	9
201410	3166	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I think the current language is flexible enough to accommodate incorporating financial-stability considerations into policy decisions if, in the Committee’s judgment, the threat to our statutory objectives is sufficient and we believe monetary policy tools can be effective.	92	9
201410	3167	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Regarding SEPs, I’ve already said in earlier meetings that I favor a review of this element of our communication tool set.	92	9
201410	3168	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	I’d like to see another try at a consensus forecast.	92	9
201410	3169	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	In a conversation with President Rosengren—and correct me if I misinterpret what you said—he noted that the Bank of England’s Monetary Policy Committee actually votes on whether the forecast is the consensus, as opposed to agreement with the forecast.	92	9
201410	3170	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	That’s a distinction that struck me as providing some potential for us to take another look at this and possibly succeed.	92	9
201410	3171	2014-10-29	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3172	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201410	3173	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Fisher.	92	9
201410	3174	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3175	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I think Governor Tarullo summarized this adequately and appropriately.	92	9
201410	3176	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	The better argument is the Hippocratic argument, which is to do no harm in the end.	92	9
201410	3177	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	And I would suggest that we worked very hard, as was mentioned earlier, to achieve a very delicate balance here.	92	9
201410	3178	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I’m worried that if we open this up, centrifugal force might just tear it apart at a very delicate time as we approach liftoff.	92	9
201410	3179	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Having said that, I want to make a couple of comments very quickly.	92	9
201410	3180	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	With regard to the first question and the 2 percent longer-run objective, just to clarify in my antepenultimate meeting, I have no problem with a strategy that has policy respond symmetrically to above-target or below-target inflation, as long as inflation is appropriately measured.	92	9
201410	3181	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I think we want to be very careful not to give the impression, though, that deviations of inflation from target are always undesirable.	92	9
201410	3182	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Supply-driven inflation deviations can actually improve resource allocation and the distribution of risk in the economy.	92	9
201410	3183	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Accordingly, I don’t think we should deduct price- stability penalty points from the grade we assign policy just because realized inflation is off target over a period.	92	9
201410	3184	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	To me, genuine signs of poor policy are significant fluctuations in medium- term average inflation that are not linked to real activity and any indication that, as President Lockhart just said, expected average inflation at medium-term horizons and even longer is not firmly anchored.	92	9
201410	3185	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	That’s what I worry about.	92	9
201410	3186	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	But I have no problem with having a symmetrical approach to inflation.	92	9
201410	3187	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	With regard to the case for changing the use of “balanced approach,” the memo—I thank you and the subcommittee for putting it together—appropriately says that the primary reason the Committee might determine that it would like to change the “balanced approach” sentence is that it is vague.	92	9
201410	3188	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	However, I view specificity as also having a downside.	92	9
201410	3189	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	It can take us to a stated plan of action, and, if we deviate from said stated plan, it could undermine our credibility.	92	9
201410	3190	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I’ve argued many times at this table, as any businessperson would, that certainty clearly helps decisionmaking, uncertainty undermines decisionmaking, and false certainty is a destructive force.	92	9
201410	3191	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	And, for what it’s worth, I view central banking and economics to be a judgmental art form and definitely not a science.	92	9
201410	3192	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I think the mathematization and quantification of economics have helped but are no substitute in the end for judgment, and I would not argue for anything more specific than what’s already in the consensus statement as written.	92	9
201410	3193	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Lastly, with regard to the issue of financial stability, there is some wiggle room for doing this, in that the act calls for us to maintain moderate interest rates, but I’d be very careful here.	92	9
201410	3194	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	First of all, financial stability is not exogenous to monetary policy.	92	9
201410	3195	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	In fact, it’s implicit in it.	92	9
201410	3196	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	I would suggest that we not tamper with the way the statement currently reads.	92	9
201410	3197	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Here’s the bottom line, Madam Chair:  My approach is, do no harm—leave it as it is.	92	9
201410	3198	2014-10-29	meeting	FISHER	Thank you.	92	9

201410	3200	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President George.	92	9
201410	3201	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3202	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	I appreciate the work of the subcommittee and staff to give us a head start on considering whether changes to the statement are needed.	92	9
201410	3203	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	My own conclusion is that the statement has done a pretty good job of representing a consensus at this table and has held up well in the public eye over the past few years.	92	9
201410	3204	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	Given that, I would not revise the statement, particularly at a time of heightened interest in and attention to policy normalization and related communications.	92	9
201410	3205	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	Quickly, in terms of the questions, I view the Committee’s goal of longer-run inflation at 2 percent as a symmetric target.	92	9
201410	3206	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	If inflation moves above 2 percent, as it did throughout most of 2011, it warrants the same level of concern and monitoring as when it’s running below 2 percent.	92	9
201410	3207	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	Regarding the balanced approach, my view is that paragraph 3 of the consensus statement offers the necessary context because it rightly notes that firmly anchored inflation expectations are key to meeting our objectives.	92	9
201410	3208	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	Determining the relevant monetary policy stance by ascribing weights to either inflation or employment could be misleading and oversimplifies the policymakers’ considerations.	92	9
201410	3209	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	Finally, I am comfortable with the current statement’s treatment of financial stability.	92	9
201410	3210	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	While I firmly believe the setting of interest rate policy should avoid promotingconditions of undue risk-taking and potential financial imbalances, I would question whether we can credibly elevate financial stability as a primary objective of monetary policy rather than a necessary condition for achieving our longer-run goals.	92	9
201410	3211	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	However, to the extent that we rely on macroprudential and supervisory tools as the first line of defense, I do think we should have a clear understanding and confidence that these mechanisms can effectively perform, even if it is imprudent to assume that they can be consistently relied on.	92	9
201410	3212	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	In terms of other areas for improved communication, I’m open to considering again the value of a consensus forecast, but I think the Committee already made a serious effort in that direction and encountered substantial obstacles.	92	9
201410	3213	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	So I’m mindful that, with policy normalization and its attendant communication challenges, we might be ahead to maintain some consistency and defer further adjustments to the SEP or a consideration of a consensus forecast until after we deliver a successful exit and return to more normal policy stances.	92	9
201410	3214	2014-10-29	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you.	92	9
201410	3215	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201410	3216	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	92	9
201410	3217	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3218	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	There doesn’t seem to be a lot of disagreement, but I prepared these comments, so let me go ahead.	92	9
201410	3219	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Turning to the specific questions we were asked to address, on the first, regarding symmetry, I’d always thought our original Committee agreement was that the inflation objective is symmetric.	92	9
201410	3220	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I don’t recall anyone disagreeing during our subsequent FOMC deliberations when we have discussed that longer-run inflation expectations are supposed to be 2 percent, according to our monetary policy strategy.	92	9
201410	3221	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Symmetry and “balanced approach” clearly support this expectation for the public.	92	9
201410	3222	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Chairman Bernanke publicly stated that our 2 percent was not a ceiling—it was symmetric.	92	9
201410	3223	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Many of us around the table have said the same.	92	9
201410	3224	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Any hint that the Committee is unsure about the symmetry of our inflation objective would make its achievement vastly more difficult now.	92	9
201410	3225	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	To date, the only sustainable achievement of our 2 percent objective has been in our years-ahead forecasts.	92	9
201410	3226	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	So I can see a case for further clarifying our current commitment to symmetry.	92	9
201410	3227	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Although I recognize there’s not much taste for this, I think it would be a positive step for expanding transparency.	92	9
201410	3228	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	One way to accomplish this would be to add a new third sentence in paragraph 3:  “The inflation goal is symmetric, and the Committee expects inflation to average 2 percent over sufficiently long time periods.”	92	9
201410	3229	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	The public can easily understand that success with respect to our inflation objective will lead to 2 percent inflation, on average.	92	9
201410	3230	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	On the second question, I currently see no reasonable path for the Committee to elaborate on the “balanced approach” language in paragraph 5.	92	9
201410	3231	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	It was a difficult task to get to this very general language in 2012.	92	9
201410	3232	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	This language encompasses the range of views on the Committee in a workable fashion.	92	9
201410	3233	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	On the issues of weights on our dual-mandate objectives, I believe our current “balanced approach” language captures well the equal footing of maximum employment and price stability as codified in the Federal Reserve Act.	92	9
201410	3234	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Stating numerical weights would give an illusory precision for our policy strategy, especially as details such as changes in the Okun’s law relationship could modestly alter the numerical mapping between output and employment and unemployment over time.	92	9
201410	3235	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Now, on financial stability, I do not think we’re intellectually close to a point at which we can go beyond what is currently in the consensus statement .	92	9
201410	3236	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	But let me talk about that at greater length for the benefit of the newer FOMC members, who weren’t here for our March 2013 discussions, which I think are pretty informative on the range of policy considerations.	92	9
201410	3237	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Financial instability risk is an important concern for public policymakers, but I’ve not heard a convincing argument for why it should be another separate objective for the FOMC.	92	9
201410	3238	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Yes, I strongly support the use of our supervisory and macroprudential tools.	92	9
201410	3239	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	This approach falls under the category of using financial instruments to address financial-stability objectives and reserving monetary instruments to address our dual-mandate monetary policy goals.	92	9
201410	3240	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Although it sounds important to at least acknowledge the possibility that, at some time, the FOMC might have to make a difficult financial-stability call to tighten monetary conditions at a time of low inflation and low employment, I cannot yet imagine supporting even hinting about this unless we had a much better analysis of the likely effectiveness of such actions.	92	9
201410	3241	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Recent efforts to use modestly higher interest rates in Norway and Sweden were ineffective for addressing the stated financial risks, and, in Sweden, inflation has been well below its target.	92	9
201410	3242	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Chairman Greenspan spoke of this type of action back in 2002, I believe, at the annual Jackson Hole symposium.	92	9
201410	3243	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	He essentially concluded that the kind of rate increases needed to rein in excessive financial market risks would require cracking the economy.	92	9
201410	3244	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	That’s my paraphrasing of what he said.	92	9
201410	3245	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	He said it would engender a bad economic outcome.	92	9
201410	3246	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Both of these comments are simply reminders that, if monetary policy tools are called on, being effective at rooting out financial instability risks will almost certainly require substantial increases in short-term policy rates.	92	9
201410	3247	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	That means higher unemployment, and lower inflation, than our objectives.	92	9
201410	3248	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Using the blunt tool of monetary policy to address financial instability risks reminds me of treating a sick patient.	92	9
201410	3249	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	After discovering a growing malignancy in a relatively already unhealthy patient, doctors are considering two tools—surgery to remove the malignancy or chemotherapy.	92	9
201410	3250	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Chemotherapy is a blunt tool and will damage the overall health of the already sick patient, but the hope is to rid their body of the malignancy.	92	9
201410	3251	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Surgery is a more direct tool, and you can imagine that that’s preferred.	92	9
201410	3252	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	But the malignancy may be inoperable, and surgery is not feasible.	92	9
201410	3253	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	In situations like this, blunt tools may be the only hope anyone has.	92	9
201410	3254	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	If the FOMC faced an analogous extreme situation and contemplated raising short-term policy rates against the best interest of our employment and inflation objectives, I would expect we would also state very loudly that, first, a malignancy on the financial system had made this imperative; and, second, there was no choice but to remove the root causes of those malignancies as soon as possible.	92	9
201410	3255	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	I can’t imagine taking this action without stating how dangerous the financial market structure was for the US economy that we had had to take such action.	92	9
201410	3256	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	To sum up, we just aren’t anywhere close to the point of being able to describe the conditions for tightening monetary policy to address financial-instability concerns that would result in a better path for unemployment and inflation relative to our mandated goals.	92	9
201410	3257	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Until we are sure of that, we shouldn’t change the reference to financial stability in the consensus statement.	92	9
201410	3258	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Finally, although I’d like to see the subcommittee explore enhancements to the SEP, I’m not optimistic that we’d be able to get to a consensus forecast.	92	9
201410	3259	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	But it’s a worthy objective, if somebody has the time to try to pursue that.	92	9
201410	3260	2014-10-29	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201410	3269	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Even though we may end up not making changes—and it seems as though we’re heading that way—I think it’s important for us to have this conversation to understand where we stand.	92	9
201410	3270	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In thinking about the statement, the value of the statement is not simply that it is a consensus, but that it actually provides a description of our longer-run goals and strategies.	92	9

201410	3276	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Let me turn to the issues raised by the subcommittee.	92	9
201410	3277	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of symmetry, I’m very glad to hear the enthusiastic endorsement of symmetry that I’ve heard around the table, and I think it would be helpful for the minutes to reflect that strong endorsement.	92	9

201410	3282	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m sympathetic to Governor Tarullo’s view that the language in paragraph 5 is vague.	92	9
201410	3283	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But as I’ve talked about on other occasions, I actually have found this language very helpful in providing valuable structure to my decisionmaking.	92	9
201410	3284	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think it emphasizes a key point that’s often forgotten—that our mandates are typically complementary.	92	9

201410	3286	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It informs the public that we will not favor one exclusively over the other.	92	9
201410	3287	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And, finally, it appropriately emphasizes that monetary policy is based on a forward-looking evaluation of mandate-relevant macroeconomic variables—one based on projections—not on a backward look at the economy.	92	9
201410	3288	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think all of these are very valuable.	92	9
201410	3289	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I do have a small word change that would be helpful.	92	9
201410	3290	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the first sentence of paragraph 5, there are two uses of the word “from.”	92	9

201410	3292	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think this would clarify that we are concerned about employment being too low and not too high.	92	9
201410	3293	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As it is, people could read the statement as saying that the FOMC is working toward not having economic activity be too high.	92	9
201410	3294	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So that would be my suggestion.	92	9
201410	3295	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Is it clear what I’m trying to describe?	92	9
201410	3296	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	It’s absolutely clear.	92	9
201410	3297	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Okay.	92	9
201410	3298	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Paragraph 5 says “In setting monetary policy, the Committee seeks to mitigate deviations of inflation from its longer-run goal and deviations of employment from the Committee’s assessments of its maximum level.”	92	9
201410	3299	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I would say “deviations of employment below the Committee’s assessments of its maximum level.”	92	9
201410	3300	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So that’s my suggestion for a small change.	92	9
201410	3301	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I don’t feel strongly about that, but, certainly, I think it’s more in keeping with what the second mandate, the full employment mandate, really should mean.	92	9
201410	3302	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The issue I do feel more strongly about is on financial stability.	92	9
201410	3303	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ve heard a number of people suggest that it’s too early to talk about this, and that the intellectual foundations of that are not clear.	92	9
201410	3304	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The intellectual foundations of much of what is in the statement also remain unclear, and I think President Lacker spoke to this very well.	92	9
201410	3305	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We’ve crafted a consensus statement that has served us well despite that, and I think we have to do that on financial stability as well.	92	9
201410	3306	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Over the longer run, I expect that the federal funds rate will converge to about 3¼ percent.	92	9
201410	3307	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That’s low by historical standards.	92	9
201410	3308	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And there’s uncertainty around my longer-run estimate.	92	9
201410	3309	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There’s a distinct risk that the longer-run federal funds rate could be 1 or even 2 percentage points lower than my estimate.	92	9
201410	3310	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If interest rates do remain this low, I am sure that policymakers will be concerned about risks to financial stability.	92	9
201410	3311	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I would expect that the FOMC will put weight on these financial-stability considerations, at least insofar as it perceives that that incipient instability creates a risk for the achievement of its dual-mandate objectives.	92	9
201410	3312	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Indeed, as I understand their comments, some participants in the FOMC may already be putting weight on those considerations.	92	9
201410	3313	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The issue, then, is, does the current language accurately capture this role for financial stability?	92	9
201410	3314	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think paragraph 2 is quite helpful along these lines, and President George and President Rosengren were very helpful in originally getting us to this point about “including risks to the financial system that could impede the attainment of the Committee’s goals.”	92	9
201410	3315	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That’s the way it’s referred to in the second paragraph.	92	9
201410	3316	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The problem is that once we get to what I see as the action paragraph of the statement, paragraph 5, the link between financial stability and our policy decisions is less clear.	92	9
201410	3317	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Actually, this is a more general issue.	92	9
201410	3318	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Paragraph 2 describes how risks to the outlook, including those for financial stability, play a role in our deliberations.	92	9
201410	3319	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But then when we get to paragraph 5, that reference to risks is dropped.	92	9
201410	3320	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So let me suggest adding a sentence to the end of paragraph 5:  “The Committee also takes account of the risks to its projections, including risks related to financial instability, as well as the impact of monetary policy on those risks.”	92	9
201410	3321	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think this is very much in keeping with the dialogue I hear around the table all of the time referring to risk-management issues.	92	9
201410	3322	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It takes into account the possibility that we’re able to affect risks; it’s not just that we’re reacting to them.	92	9
201410	3323	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And it reflects what we have in paragraph 2.	92	9
201410	3324	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As I say, I feel more strongly about this.	92	9
201410	3325	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I understand that the sense of the Committee is, “Boy, we’ve got the perfect statement—or at least perfect enough that we don’t want to change it.”	92	9
201410	3326	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But I think the statement should reflect the factors that are actually going into our decisionmaking, and financial stability is likely to play an increasing role as we move on.	92	9
201410	3327	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Let me mention three other issues.	92	9
201410	3328	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And this is going beyond amending the consensus statement.	92	9
201410	3329	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I don’t think the consensus statement—what I would call the longer-run goals statement—is playing the role that it could and should play in our decisionmaking.	92	9
201410	3330	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The FOMC statement routinely makes little reference to it, except to the 2 percent target.	92	9
201410	3331	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So I’d really encourage the communications subcommittee to explore ways in which the longer-run goals statement, and especially paragraph 5, could be better used.	92	9
201410	3332	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We should always be able to explain how our current decisions are fitting into the framework described in the longer-run goals statement.	92	9
201410	3333	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We should be able to give that explanation in the FOMC statement itself.	92	9
201410	3334	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m a big fan of the idea of a consensus forecast.	92	9
201410	3335	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I thought President Lockhart’s idea was a very interesting one—that maybe we could be ascribing what we all agree is the consensus, even though we don’t agree with the consensus.	92	9
201410	3336	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That’s a very interesting idea that’s worth exploring.	92	9
201410	3337	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Even if we don’t get to a quantitative consensus forecast, I’d really encourage us to work toward having a qualitative one.	92	9
201410	3338	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the consensus statement, paragraph 5 talks about employment and inflation projections, implying that a forecast of some kind is playing a role in our decisions.	92	9
201410	3339	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the Committee should be able to provide a verbal description of that forecast and its attendant risks in justifying our decision.	92	9
201410	3340	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The September FOMC statement has a partial description along those lines.	92	9
201410	3341	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It refers to labor market indicators and inflation moving back toward our dual-mandate objectives.	92	9
201410	3342	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But we could be more detailed.	92	9
201410	3343	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Do we expect that that convergence will take a few years, less, or more?	92	9
201410	3344	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The final comment I’ll make will, I suspect, have very little support in the Committee, but I would hope that we can work toward this over time.	92	9
201410	3345	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Our 2 percent target will be much more meaningful if it has some notion of a benchmark time horizon.	92	9
201410	3346	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	President Lacker referred to a preoccupation with low inflation, which I assume was somewhat directed at me.	92	9
201410	3347	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We could also have a preoccupation with high inflation, and the inflation target will be more meaningful on the high side if we’re thinking about getting back to target within a benchmark time horizon.	92	9
201410	3348	2014-10-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Other central banks have that benchmark time horizon.	92	9

201410	3356	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	President Williams.	92	9
201410	3357	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3358	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	The consensus statement has served the Committee well over the past three years.	92	9
201410	3359	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	It facilitates clear communication by providing a publicly agreed-upon, shared language to describe the overarching principles that guide our decisionmaking.	92	9
201410	3360	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	And, importantly, it has helped clarify the terms of our debates and disagreements.	92	9
201410	3361	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	When we disagree, it’s not about the longer-run goals or strategies but how they apply to a specific situation.	92	9
201410	3362	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	As a concrete example, if inflation is 1½ percent, it’s not just my personal view that inflation is too low.	92	9
201410	3363	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	It’s the Committee’s clearly articulated view that inflation is too low.	92	9
201410	3364	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, because of this shared language, the consensus statement is a foundational document for all of our communications—including our statements, press conferences, speeches, and interviews—so it’s important that we review the consensus statement regularly.	92	9
201410	3365	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’m echoing comments by President Kocherlakota.	92	9
201410	3366	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	We want to make sure that it’s well aligned with our decisionmaking and with our other communications.	92	9
201410	3367	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Even though I am hearing a lot of comments about there being no need for a change, I still think this process is a healthy one, and I’ve learned a lot from the comments I’ve already heard so far today.	92	9
201410	3368	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	With those comments in mind, I’ll now say a few words about the three questions.	92	9
201410	3369	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	First, I personally view the 2 percent goal as symmetric in that inflation should, on average, over time, be close to 2 percent.	92	9
201410	3370	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	And then our desire to return to 2 percent inflation does not depend at all on whether inflation is running above or below the target.	92	9
201410	3371	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think this message is sharp, clean, and clear.	92	9
201410	3372	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	When clearly communicated, symmetry provides a consistent anchor for inflation whether we’re above or below our objective.	92	9
201410	3373	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In contrast, a lack of a clear statement of symmetry can be confusing, and here I’ll give the example of the ECB.	92	9
201410	3374	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	It has articulated in the past an inflation target of below, but close to, 2 percent over the medium term.	92	9
201410	3375	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	This opaque formulation has led to various interpretations.	92	9
201410	3376	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Is this a ceiling or a target?	92	9
201410	3377	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	So we want to avoid that.	92	9
201410	3378	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Second, the “balanced approach” language respects the principle that both of our mandates are important for our decisionmaking, and that neither is subordinate to the other—that is, they’re on equal footing, and, importantly, we don’t have a hierarchical mandate.	92	9
201410	3379	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, I don’t see a great deal of benefit, even if it were possible, in getting more precise about whether the weights in the loss function are literally equal.	92	9
201410	3380	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	After all, even with somewhat different weights, we can still reach broad agreement on policy decisions most of the time.	92	9
201410	3381	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	In thinking about both symmetry and “balanced approach,”	92	9
201410	3382	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	I find it hard to think through concrete examples of this language because, in doing so, you start realizing we are not truly symmetric in our preferences over different outcomes.	92	9
201410	3383	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	For example, zero percent inflation carries with it a lot of different costs and potential risks, compared with 4 percent inflation.	92	9
201410	3384	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	So the “balanced approach” language actually does serve us well—it’s accurate.	92	9
201410	3385	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Third, concerns about financial stability are best viewed as part of the broader category of longer-term probabilistic risks to achieving our dual mandate.	92	9
201410	3386	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Financial excess is often built slowly, but, when bubbles pop or systemically important banks fail, it can be challenging, if not impossible, to achieve either maximum employment or price stability.	92	9
201410	3387	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	For this reason, risks to financial stability need to be part of our ongoing policy discussion.	92	9
201410	3388	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Importantly, though, financial stability is not the only source of longer-term probabilistic risks to our goals that we regularly discuss here and that influence our policy decisions.	92	9
201410	3389	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Other examples we’ve discussed in recent years include concerns about deflation, the zero lower bound, and the loss of anchored inflation expectations.	92	9
201410	3390	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Each of these, I think, is under the same general rubric of concerns about tail risks or, more generally, probabilistic risks to the outlook.	92	9
201410	3391	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Issues like these are already part of our ongoing discussions under the broader risk- management rubric.	92	9
201410	3392	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Therefore, it could be useful—and I’m picking up a theme that President Kocherlakota raised—to include some reference to risk management, broadly defined, in paragraph 5 of the consensus statement describing how we navigate tradeoffs between our goals.	92	9
201410	3393	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	This would echo the “balance of risks” reference at the end of paragraph 2, which I actually think is really well worded.	92	9
201410	3394	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Such an approach would be preferable to adding explicit reference only to financial stability in paragraph 5, for a couple of reasons.	92	9
201410	3395	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	One is, I do think that suddenly adding a clause about financial stability explicitly to paragraph 5 might be misinterpreted as a statement of a change in our conduct of our policy rather than a clarification of our existing strategy.	92	9
201410	3396	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Also, just as a matter of factual content, financial-stability concerns are a subset of many of these probabilistic risks that we do think about under risk management.	92	9
201410	3397	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	The sentence in paragraph 2 really captures this right:  “The Committee’s policy decisions reflect its longer-run goals, its medium-term outlook, and its assessments of the balance of risks, including risks to the financial system that could impede the attainment of the Committee’s goals.”	92	9
201410	3398	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	That sentence nailed it, and I think finding a way, potentially, whether over the next few months or next year, of echoing those comments in paragraph 5 would be useful.	92	9
201410	3399	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	But, again, I agree with many people in the room that we don’t really know the answer to how we bring financial stability specifically into monetary policy decisionmaking.	92	9
201410	3400	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	But it would be helpful to include some notion of risks to the outlook being an important part of our decisionmaking, because they are.	92	9
201410	3401	2014-10-29	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you.	92	9
201410	3402	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201410	3403	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	92	9
201410	3404	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3405	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	What I’m hearing around the table is pretty much where I am:  The consensus statement we have is pretty good in the sense that it reflects the consensus that we could all subscribe to—the smallest tent we could come up with, as President Lacker said.	92	9
201410	3406	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m quite skeptical that we’re going to be able to improve on this to a sufficient degree to justify bringing this forward to the public.	92	9
201410	3407	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So my view would be that the subcommittee could spend its time on other things, and what I’m going to argue for is spending time working on developing a consensus forecast, because I think that would really be something that is achievable.	92	9
201410	3408	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Other central banks have done it.	92	9
201410	3409	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	We could do it, too, and I believe it would also solve a lot of the issues with the SEP, frankly.	92	9
201410	3410	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Before I get into that, though, let me talk a little bit about the three questions.	92	9
201410	3411	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	On the symmetry of the inflation target, I think it’s actually a little trickier than what people have been laying out.	92	9
201410	3412	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	We’re basically saying we agree on symmetry within small intervals of 2 percent.	92	9
201410	3413	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So between 1.99 and 2.01 percent, we’re completely symmetric, but I don’t think we’ve agreed that we’re completely symmetric in the case of 0 versus 4 or minus 2 versus 6.	92	9
201410	3414	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	What we really want to say to people very clearly—and maybe it doesn’t have to be in the consensus statement, but maybe it could be in the minutes—is that we don’t think 2 percent is a ceiling.	92	9
201410	3415	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	We basically are targeting 2 percent and would expect to spend roughly half the time slightly above 2 percent and about half the time slightly below 2 percent, and that’s really what we’re for.	92	9
201410	3416	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	But I don’t think symmetry is quite right, because I don’t feel symmetric as I get further and further away from 2 percent because it depends on the economic circumstances.	92	9
201410	3417	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	For instance, if you told me that I was at 1 percent inflation and real GDP was growing 8 percent, I wouldn’t be too worried about inflation being 1 percent.	92	9
201410	3418	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	But if you told me that real GDP was growing 0 percent, then I’d be quite concerned about it.	92	9
201410	3419	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So I don’t think symmetry really holds up on examination.	92	9
201410	3420	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of the balanced approach, I completely don’t believe we should try to do any further elaboration, and I think it really captures the fact that we pay attention to both of these things.	92	9
201410	3421	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t believe an equal-weights rule is a good one.	92	9
201410	3422	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	How much weight you put on the two objectives depends on how far you are away from the objectives.	92	9
201410	3423	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	And it depends on the particular economic circumstances.	92	9
201410	3424	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In my own mind, how much weight I put on 1 percent inflation versus 2 depends on a whole bunch of other things that are going on in the economy that affect the economic outlook.	92	9
201410	3425	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So my weights really change over time dynamically.	92	9
201410	3426	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of financial stability, I’m not against trying to put financial stability more explicitly into the consensus statement, but I think it’s tricky.	92	9
201410	3427	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t see financial stability as a third objective of monetary policy, so I don’t like seeing monetary policy being set to achieve financial stability.	92	9
201410	3428	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I guess I see it a little differently.	92	9
201410	3429	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I see financial stability as a necessary condition to be able to achieve our dual-mandate goals over time.	92	9
201410	3430	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	If you don’t have financial stability, then the transmission channels of monetary policy are impaired, which disrupts the effectiveness of monetary policy in achieving the Committee’s objectives.	92	9
201410	3431	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s different from saying we’re going to conduct monetary policy with a goal of generating the financial-stability outcomes we want.	92	9
201410	3432	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I think monetary policy is a really blunt tool and not a very effective tool, quite frankly, in terms of responding to financial-stability concerns.	92	9
201410	3433	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The causality matters:  Is it monetary policy driving financial stability, or is financial stability something that’s taken into consideration in terms of how you conduct policy?	92	9
201410	3434	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Let me turn to the consensus forecast.	92	9
201410	3435	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	We all recognize that the SEP and the dot plot aren’t so great.	92	9
201410	3436	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	They’re not so great because they don’t really represent very well where the mass of the Committee is, and they’re not very good, because there are all of these modal dots that people actually think represent some sort of uncertainty when, in fact, all they do is represent disagreement.	92	9
201410	3437	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So I think it would be far better for the Committee to have a consensus forecast.	92	9
201410	3438	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	The question is, how do you get to that point?	92	9
201410	3439	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	As President Lockhart referenced—actually, I had a conversation with President Rosengren, and then President Rosengren had a conversation with President Lockhart.	92	9
201410	3440	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Let me tell you about the original conversation I had.	92	9
201410	3441	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I was talking to Ms Shafik, who’s a deputy governor of the Bank of England, and I asked her, “How does the Bank of England manage to come up with this Inflation Report, and why aren’t there dissents by Monetary Policy Committee members from the Inflation Report projection all of the time because, obviously, people probably won’t necessarily agree with that consensus view of things?”	92	9
201410	3442	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	She said exactly what President Lockhart said:  “Well, the reason why there haven’t been dissents”—in a decade, she said, and I don’t know if that’s correct or not, but that’s what she told me—“is that you’re not agreeing with the forecast.	92	9
201410	3443	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	You’re just agreeing that the forecast that’s in the Inflation Report represents the midpoint or the weight of where the committee is.”	92	9
201410	3444	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we crashed on the shoals of “Gee, do I agree with this forecast?	92	9
201410	3445	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Do I not agree with that forecast?”	92	9
201410	3446	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	If we moved to this different formulation for the consensus forecast, it would actually be much more possible for the Committee to sign up for something like this.	92	9
201410	3447	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So this is what I’d like to have the subcommittee on communications work on, because if we were to move to a consensus forecast, that would really further the goals of the Committee substantially.	92	9
201410	3448	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	There’s only so much time in the day.	92	9
201410	3449	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	There’s only so much energy we all have.	92	9
201410	3450	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I guess I would prefer to put that energy into working on a consensus forecast and see if we can actually get to something.	92	9
201410	3451	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	One last point on the consensus forecast.	92	9
201410	3452	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Remember the other thing we got hung up on regarding the consensus forecast was the fact that we didn’t know how to specify the monetary policy assumption because we disagreed about how much asset purchases we’re going to do.	92	9
201410	3453	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Well, that probably is not an issue, at least in the near term.	92	9
201410	3454	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	So maybe that obstacle we faced before is going to be less of an obstacle in the future, but I’ll let the subcommittee on communications work on that.	92	9
201410	3455	2014-10-29	meeting	FISCHER	Well, it’ll have a great effect on the public when we say, “Well, we’ve suspended the consensus forecast for a few months because we can’t agree on policy.”	92	9
201410	3456	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	But, again, all you have to do is to agree that the Committee agrees that this is the midpoint of where the Committee is on the monetary policy assumption, so I still think it’s possible you can get there.	92	9
201410	3457	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	Anyway, this would be worthwhile to pursue.	92	9
201410	3458	2014-10-29	meeting	DUDLEY	I’d be curious about what other people around the table think.	92	9
201410	3459	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Powell.	92	9
201410	3460	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201410	3461	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	I would join many others around the table in saying the consensus statement has provided real value.	92	9
201410	3462	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	It’s constitutional in nature, and so, to me, it’s natural that there would be differences that need to be papered over—I’m okay with that.	92	9
201410	3463	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	I’ll also join the Hippocratic brigade of doing no harm.	92	9
201410	3464	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	Turning to the three changes, I do see the 2 percent medium-term inflation objective as symmetrical, and I would view modest deviations from that objective symmetrically.	92	9
201410	3465	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	I think the word “modest” is important here.	92	9
201410	3466	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	I’m echoing what Vice Chairman Dudley said earlier, in a sense.	92	9
201410	3467	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	I just don’t think we should be contemplating more than modest deviations.	92	9
201410	3468	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	Once you get outside of that band, it’s not at all clear to me how to think about symmetry.	92	9
201410	3469	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	I’d be prepared to say publicly that the objective is symmetrical.	92	9
201410	3470	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	Indeed, the former Chairman did that, as Bob mentioned, at the April 2012 press conference.	92	9
201410	3471	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	He said that the medium-term objective, 2 percent, is “not a ceiling, it’s a symmetric objective.”	92	9
201410	3472	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	And I do think it could undermine the Committee’s credibility if the markets were to conclude that 2 percent is, in effect, a ceiling.	92	9
201410	3473	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	On the balanced approach, I like the existing formulation, and I take the statute to mean that the Committee sees the two sides of the dual mandate as of equal weight.	92	9
201410	3474	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	In fact, I don’t really see a plausible way to read the statute as suggesting different weights.	92	9
201410	3475	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	It’s an interesting thought to me that we can have models that, for example, might conclude that we should focus on one and ignore the other.	92	9
201410	3476	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	I don’t know how that would work in connection with a statute that tells us to address the two of them.	92	9
201410	3477	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	It doesn’t say, “All of you make up your mind about which of these is more important than the other.”	92	9
201410	3478	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	I’ll move on to financial stability.	92	9
201410	3479	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	Like others, I would leave the language as is here.	92	9
201410	3480	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	There really isn’t a consensus about the role of financial stability in monetary policy decisionmaking or about the efficacy of regulation.	92	9
201410	3481	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	This sentence at the end of paragraph 2 really captures it very nicely, and I wouldn’t want to see any changes.	92	9
201410	3482	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	To wrap up, there seems to be pretty broad agreement around the table—not unanimous, but pretty broad agreement—to do basically nothing about the statement, and that will leave our subcommittee with, perhaps, some bandwidth, although there are some things to consider, clearly, in the wake of this.	92	9
201410	3483	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	My own view would be that I was very hopeful we were going to get there on the consensus forecast the last time we looked at it, and I was left with a feeling that it would have been really useful to get there.	92	9
201410	3484	2014-10-29	meeting	POWELL	I was disappointed that we didn’t and would love to take another shot at that.	92	9

201410	3489	2014-10-29	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	92	9
201410	3490	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you very much.	92	9
201410	3491	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I found this conversation very illuminating.	92	9
201410	3492	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I do also view this document as somewhat constitutional.	92	9
201410	3493	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	And, as somebody who was not involved in crafting it, it is very helpful to hear about the thinking that went into it on the part of the drafters.	92	9
201410	3494	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Let me focus a bit on the third question, because I do see the statement as a relatively clear and robust explanation of how the Committee views the two individual parts of the dual mandate and possible tradeoffs between them.	92	9
201410	3495	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	However, to my mind, it does not adequately address financial stability, which I consider to be an implicit third leg of our responsibilities in this area.	92	9
201410	3496	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I also would not want to see financial-stability risks called out as a pressing consideration in our current monetary policy deliberations, but it is important that our longer-run goals framework clearly acknowledges the reality that we do take into account, and should take into account, financial-stability risks in the formulation of monetary policy.	92	9
201410	3497	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I don’t think we can be too precise or prescriptive at this juncture.	92	9
201410	3498	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Neither the Committee’s practice nor the research is sufficiently settled to clearly state, for instance, the prioritization of macroprudential tools and monetary policy in combating financial-stability risks under different circumstances or to specify the circumstances under which we might be willing to tolerate some deviation from either leg of the dual mandate.	92	9
201410	3499	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	But I do think we want to acknowledge that the Federal Reserve’s mandate encompasses financial stability, and that it is central to our deliberations.	92	9
201410	3500	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	In my view, financial stability has been central to the Federal Reserve’s mission and mandate since its inception, although it has been, for the most part, implicit and not clearly called out in the statutory language until we saw the provisions on the Federal Reserve’s prudential responsibilities in Dodd-Frank.	92	9
201410	3501	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Nonetheless, if you think about the creation of the Federal Reserve and the major changes to it over its history, they’ve, in most cases, been in response to major events of financial instability.	92	9
201410	3502	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	It would also be a mistake to confine the use of monetary policy to being a last resort, for a variety of reasons.	92	9
201410	3503	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	First and most obvious is because there have been instances of extreme financial stress in which monetary policy has been the tool of first resort, and we should remember that.	92	9
201410	3504	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Moreover, we may need to rely more heavily on monetary policy relative to macroprudential tools, compared with some other central banks, for several reasons.	92	9
201410	3505	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	First of all, we operate in a highly fragmented regulatory environment and in a system in which the capital markets play a bigger role in the financial markets than they do in many other systems.	92	9
201410	3506	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	And, second, we have somewhat limited macroprudential tools relative to some other central banks.	92	9
201410	3507	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	We’re making huge strides in building structural resilience.	92	9
201410	3508	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	But I think we’re likely to find, as we continue on in this work, that we’re somewhat hampered in our macroprudential toolkit—possibly on constructing time-varying tools that address time-varying sectoral risks and, certainly, on tools that address the borrower side, such as loan-to-value ratios and debt-to-income ratios, which have been proven to be among the most powerful tools in combating the most damaging kinds of financial-stability risks.	92	9
201410	3509	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	If you think about what we are capable of commanding—in contrast, for instance, to the Bank of England—we have a much more fragmented regulatory structure, with a number of regulatory entities that don’t view their mandate as pertaining to financial stability.	92	9
201410	3510	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	They are instead focused, for instance, on investor protections or consumer protections.	92	9
201410	3511	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	And I’d say the FSOC is, so far, a highly imperfect answer to that problem.	92	9
201410	3512	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	In that context, monetary policy really is the only tool that works across the financial system to address periods of very rapid growth in private credit creation, and we may not want to take that off the table.	92	9
201410	3513	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Nonetheless, I think it’s absolutely right, as many here have stated, that we want to be very modest at this juncture in terms of what we could say about how we’re likely to address and view financial stability relative to the other two legs of the mandate.	92	9
201410	3514	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I don’t agree that it’s one risk in a list of risks.	92	9
201410	3515	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	It is a risk for which we have more primary responsibility, and one that is endogenous, to a larger degree, with respect to the tools we have at our disposal.	92	9
201410	3516	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	So, in that sense, I think we should call it out separately.	92	9
201410	3517	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	And I like the proposal that President Kocherlakota put on the table.	92	9
201410	3518	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	It does have an appropriate degree of modestness but also identifies this as an area in which we are going to intensify our work, which is, I believe, the case.	92	9
201410	3519	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	With regard to the other pieces, I don’t think I can really add to the remarks that have been put on the table.	92	9
201410	3520	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	The statement, as drafted, is actually quite good—very carefully crafted language on both the balance and the issue of symmetry.	92	9
201410	3521	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I think it would be difficult for anyone who has observed the Committee’s actions over the past several years not to conclude that the Committee is prepared to act to counter inflation falling persistently below the 2 percent target.	92	9
201410	3522	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	With regard to the consensus forecast proposal, I wasn’t part of the earlier effort.	92	9
201410	3523	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I can see the virtues of having such a forecast.	92	9
201410	3524	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	I believe that, in the case of the Bank of England Monetary Policy Committee, that process is made considerably easier by the fact that they use market expectations of rates, which means that committee doesn’t actually have to agree on a monetary policy course in order to get to a consensus forecast.	92	9
201410	3525	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	That’s something you should take into account in deliberations over whether this is feasible for this Committee.	92	9
201410	3526	2014-10-29	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
